# 元始无量度人上品妙经四注

**The Fourfold Commentary on the Supreme and Wondrous Scripture of Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity**

**Scripture Title:** *The Fourfold Commentary on the Supreme and Wondrous Scripture of Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity*
Commentaries by Yan Dong of the Southern Qi, and Daoists Xue Youqi, Li Shaowei, and Cheng Xuanying of the Tang; compiled and annotated by Daoist Chen Jingyuan of the Northern Song.
Four fascicles.
Source of the base text: *Daoist Canon of the Zhengtong Era*, *Dongzhen* section, *Yujue* category.

---

**Preface to the Collected Commentaries on the Scripture of Salvation**
Composed by Chen Jingyuan, Perfected Master of the Right Street Daoist Registry and Master of True Stillness

When the vast and luminous void remained undifferentiated, the great Dao was about to transform, and thus the mysterious scripture emerged in the midst of heaven. As the formless and empty began to coalesce, the wondrous darkness congealed within the azure vault. Each character spanned a full *zhang* in breadth, its radiance casting eight-cornered brilliance—resplendent and dazzling, its light effulgent and refulgent.

At that time, the Primordial Beginning descended to Mount Bokeling, where the Five Elders encircled him in cloud-borne seats. He commanded the Heavenly Perfected Sovereign to trace intricate patterns, emulating and transcending reality, drafting the hidden scriptures of all heavens and compiling the numinous models of the five directions. These recorded the eras of the Primal Dragon and Han, concealed within the Purple Tenuity Palace of Yuluo, unfolding into thirty-six revered scriptures and dividing into twelve thousand illustrated scrolls. The celestial scripts and cloud-seals of the Eight Assemblies all trace their origin here.

Of old, within the Azure Heaven of the Beginning and the interior of the Jeweled Pearl, the teachings of the Numinous Treasure were expounded, delivering the celestial and human kindred. The Jade Dawn Lord □□ arranged them from beginning to end, secreting them in the Upper Repository, to be transmitted but once every forty thousand kalpas, sworn never to be lightly disclosed to the lower worlds.

Thereupon, the Golden Mother of Tortoise Terrace, moved by the calamities of the Nine Yangs and Hundred Sixes, personally paid homage at the Jade Capital, earnestly entreating their dissemination. Later, the Yellow Emperor Xuanyuan inquired of the Dao upon the northern slopes of Mount Emei, bowing to the Perfected Sovereign and receiving the transmission of the sacred instructions. In the state of Wu, Ge Xuan of Juqu sought the Dao in Guiji Prefecture, supplicating the Perfected on Mount Shangyu, where the chariot of the Great Ultimate Messenger descended, bearing the scrolls of the Numinous Treasure scriptures. This was the supreme scripture, the first to be □□.

Thereafter, those who cultivated and recited it spread throughout the world, its hidden rhymes and secret sounds eluding all comprehension. Yan Dong of the Qi was the first to compose a commentary, gazing upward to trace the revolutions of the celestial qi and downward to fathom the depths of Fengdu’s nether springs. He set it forth in written form, its inner and outer meanings resplendent. Had he not profoundly elucidated the subtle and obscure, how could the essential principles have been so clearly expounded? Thus, those who turned toward this teaching could pierce obstructions and open pathways, awakening understanding in accord with their nature.

Later, the Tang Daoist Xue Youqi, who had served in Qingcheng and cultivated perfection on Mount Heng, composed a true exegesis and preface, clarifying the path of practice. Following him, the Palace Attendant of Great Clarity Li Shaowei and the Dharma Master of Western Florescence Cheng Xuanying each compiled commentaries, citing inner teachings to fill lacunae and supplement omissions, ensuring that matters and principles were fully addressed.

From my youth, I, Jingyuan, have revered the Dao, delving into the jade scriptures in my early years. Undeterred by my ignorance and obscurity, I dared to compile and arrange these texts. Now, from the explanations of the four masters, I have excised redundancies, refined the profound meanings, and assembled them into four fascicles. May this spare the reader from excessive confusion.

Composed on the full moon of the mid-autumn month in the fourth year of the Zhiping era, cyclical year *dingwei*.

---

The Dao abides in quiescent emptiness and formless stillness, where the mind merges with the spirit in silent accord. The scriptures rely upon transcription, transmission, recitation, and chanting to propagate and amplify their teachings. Without quiescence, one cannot merge with the Dao; without recitation, one cannot propagate the scriptures. Though their paths may differ, their essence is uniformly interconnected. When expanded, they reach distant realms; when merged, they return to the same source.

It is through the Dao that scriptures are established, and through scriptures that the Dao is illuminated. The Dao is the fundamental essence of the scriptures, while the scriptures are the manifest functions of the Dao. Essence and function mutually clarify one another, essence and application merging in profound unity. Thus, the true scripture shines forth above the empty vastness, opening the great source within the Purple Ultimate’s hall. The three ranks of true titles distinguish the flying scriptures of all directions; the seven divisions of the myriad scriptures disseminate the luminous traces of cloud-seals.

Thereupon, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy sat in the Upper Palace of the Purple Tenuity within the Jade Capital of the Mysterious Metropolis. The Three Caverns’ orthodox scriptures were placed before him, the Three Great Supplementary Scriptures behind; the two books of the *Dao and Its Virtue* served as his attendants, and the Hidden Scriptures of Jade Clarity as the master of teachings.

Now, the *Cavernous Mystery and Numinous Treasure* is one of the three divisions of the Middle Cavern, and the *Scripture of Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity* is one volume within that division. The methods of cultivation encompass many gates; the chapters for recitation place this volume first. Above, it dispels celestial disasters and safeguards the sovereign; below, it wards off poisonous harms and delivers the multitudes; in the middle, it liberates ancestors and enables one’s own attainment of the Dao. Such is its towering and vast model, unmatched throughout the Three Clarities!

The meaning and purport of this scripture are profoundly obscure, its sounds and rhymes deeply hidden. All expound the principles of the Great Brahma, not the common words of mundane instruction. Thus, it is said that only perfected beings who have already attained the Way, who penetrate the mysterious and fathom the subtle, can fully grasp its chapters. Many recite it, but few truly comprehend it.

Now, undeterred by my insignificance, I have presumptuously shouldered a weight of a thousand *jun*, daring to interpret the sagely intent with my humble faculties. If I might but receive instruction from a mysterious master, I would surely hope to be enlightened.

Composed in the cyclical year *jiawu*, month *gengwu*.

**Preface by Daoist Xue Youqi of Mount Heng**

---

**Fascicle One of the Fourfold Commentary on the Supreme and Wondrous Scripture of Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity**

**The Supreme Cavernous Mystery and Numinous Treasure Scripture of Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity**

Youqi says: *Tai* (Supreme) is the name of utmost greatness; *Shang* (Upper) is the title of revered eminence. *Dong* (Cavernous) means penetrating and all-pervading; *Xuan* (Mysterious) signifies the subtle and wondrous. *Ling* (Numinous) is sagely transformation; *Bao* (Treasure) is that which is cherished and esteemed. *Wu liang* (Primordial Infinity) denotes that which cannot be measured or numbered; *Du ren* (Salvation of Humanity) means guiding from the mundane to the sagely. This scripture reveals the path to transcendence and ascension as a transcendent, unbound by limits or constraints.

Moreover, *Cavernous Mystery and Numinous Treasure* is the name of its rank and order, while *Scripture of Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity* is the title of this single fascicle. As its rank is lofty and exalted, it is further called the *Supreme Scripture*...

The subtle and wondrous efficacy of its teachings is why it is called the *Wondrous Scripture*.

○ *Shaowei* states: *Tai Shang* (Supreme) is the ultimate realm of the Dao. *Dong Xuan* (Cavernous Mystery) is the wisdom that penetrates all. The august and primordial *Yuanshi* (Primordial Beginning) is revered among the myriad sovereigns; the vast and boundless *Da Luo* (Great Canopy) lies above the Three Heavens. As it is supremely great with nothing beyond, and utterly lofty beyond measure, it is thus called *Tai Shang* (Supreme) for its all-pervading penetration, and *Dong Xuan* (Cavernous Mystery) for its profound subtlety. Delving into the obscure to seek clarity, drawing forth the deep to attain the distant, it unites the world’s ultimate principles and exhausts the wondrous numbers of the myriad things—hence it is called *Dong Xuan* (Cavernous Mystery). Without fixed form in its transformations, it is called *Ling* (Numinous); revered, cherished, and esteemed, it is called *Bao* (Treasure). The true scriptures flourish in splendor, as the Five Emperors attend in audience; the jade characters radiate their brilliance, serving as the model for all heavens. Thus, the texts were inscribed on golden tablets, annotated, and disseminated. Treasuring the numinous scriptures, it is called *Ling Bao* (Numinous Treasure). The *Yuanshi Tianzun* (Primordial Heavenly Worthy) responds to the kalpas, traversing the Three Realms to expound the Dharma and deliver humanity. Those who attain the Dao and achieve transcendence are as numerous as raindrops or mist—countless through the ages—hence it is called *Wu Liang Du Ren* (Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity). The celestial scriptures of the Three Caverns, the essential hymns and chants—all such meritorious practices—prioritize deliverance and transcendence, serving as the ladder to true ranks and the root of human cultivation. Thus, it is called the *Supreme Wondrous Scripture*.

○ The Dao states:
○ *Youqi* says: These are the words of the *Tai Shang Yu Chen Gao Sheng Da Dao Jun* (Supreme Jade Dawn High Sage Great Dao Lord). The *Dao Jun* (Dao Lord) is a disciple of the *Yuanshi Tianzun* (Primordial Heavenly Worthy) and the teacher of the *Tai Wei Tian Di Jun* (Heavenly Emperor of the Grand Tenuity). Dwelling in the *Shang Qing Shang Yuan Yu Chen Gong* (Upper Clarity’s Upper Prime Jade Dawn Palace), this is the realm of Upper Clarity, the exalted rank of the Grand Clarity. Having received this scripture, he composed its preface, and thus it is placed at the beginning as its opening mark.
○ *Xuanying* says: According to the *Ben Xing Jing* (Scripture of Original Conduct), the *Dao Jun* was a native of *Xi Na Yu Guo* (Western Jade That Realm). His purple dawn radiated fragrance as the descendant of august royalty. Revering and upholding the *Ling Bao Yuanshi* (Numinous Treasure Primordial Beginning), he was enfeoffed as the *Yu Tai Tian Di* (Jade Terrace Heavenly Emperor) of *Yu Yue Na Lin Chang*. Ascending to the rank of High Sage, he governs the *Xuan Du* (Mysterious Capital). The *Yu Jing Da Dong Jing* (Great Cavern Scripture of the Jade Capital) states: The *Shang Qing Gao Sheng Da Dao Jun* (Upper Clarity High Sage Great Dao Lord) is also called the *Yu Chen Jun* (Jade Dawn Lord). He presides over the *Yao Zhu Yu Que Qi Ying Zi Fang* (Seven Radiant Purple Chambers of the Jade Gate of Elixir Pearls), serving the *Xu Huang* (Vacuous Sovereign). The *Xu Huang* is the *Yuanshi Tianzun* (Primordial Heavenly Worthy). Formerly, in the *Shi Qing Tian* (Beginning Azure Heaven), amidst the *Bi Luo* (Azure Empyrean) and the *Kong Ge* (Empty Songs) of the *Da Fu Li Tu* (Great Floating Black Realm), he received the *Wu Liang Du Ren Shang Pin* (Primordial Infinity for the Salvation of Humanity, Supreme Grade).
○ *Youqi* says: *Xi* (formerly) means past. *Shi Qing Tian* (Beginning Azure Heaven) is the *Dong Fang Jiu Qi Qing Tian* (Nine Qi Azure Heaven of the East), located above the *Yuan Luo* (Round Canopy) and beyond the eastern extremity. *Shi* (beginning) is the name of the first among the five directions; *Qing* (azure) is the color of the nine qi of the east. Thus, the true scriptures say: *Dong Fang Jiu Qi Shi Huang Qing Tian* (Nine Qi Beginning Sovereign Azure Heaven of the East). As the heavens are azure and the qi is green, the azure radiance stretches boundlessly—hence it is called *Bi Luo* (Azure Empyrean). The numinous phoenixes and jade trees resound with songs in the void—hence it is called *Kong Ge* (Empty Songs). *Da Fu Li Tu* (Great Floating Black Realm) is the name of a great realm. *Shou* (received) means the *Dao Jun* stated that he formerly, in this heavenly realm, received the scripture of *Du Ren* (Salvation of Humanity) from the *Yuanshi* (Primordial Beginning).
○ *Shaowei* says: *Shi Qing Tian* (Beginning Azure Heaven) is the *Dong Bei Yu Long Tian* (Northeastern Jade Dragon Heaven). In this heaven, azure radiance interweaves, numinous winds play, and purple characters resound in the forests, naturally forming songs. The sovereign of this realm is named *Fu Li Tian Zun* (Floating Black Heavenly Worthy). When descending to the ten directions to convene for the salvation of humanity, he received this scripture. The *Ling Shu* (Numinous Book) states: In the *Dong Ji Da Fu Li Guo* (Great Floating Black Realm of the Eastern Ultimate), the land is entirely of azure jade, perpetually suffused with azure radiance. There are also *Qing Lin* (Azure Forest) trees, whose leaves naturally bear purple script. When the wind blows through the trees, their sounds form resplendent cavernous hymns, ringing clearly through the vastness—hence it is called *Bi Luo Kong Ge* (Azure Empyrean Empty Songs).
○ *Xuanying* says: *Da Fu Li Tu* (Great Floating Black Realm) means *Da* (great) as vast and boundless; *Fu Li* is the name of its sovereign; *Tu* (realm) is the land within the realm. When the *Yuanshi Tianzun* (Primordial Heavenly Worthy) expounded this scripture, he circumambulated ten times to summon the ten directions. At the beginning of his ascent to the seat,
○ *Youqi* says: *Yuan* (primordial) means beginning; *Shi* (beginning) means first. The *Yuanshi Tianzun* (Primordial Heavenly Worthy) established the inception of the myriad transformations, serving as the foremost of all Daoist teachings. Dwelling in the *Yu Qing Shang Yuan* (Upper Prime of Jade Clarity), he governs the domain of the *Da Luo Xuan Du* (Great Canopy Mysterious Capital), planting the root of heaven and earth and giving birth to the mother of the myriad things. Before transmitting the scripture and expounding the Dharma, he first summoned the perfected of the ten directions, each circumambulation corresponding to one direction—ten directions, ten circumambulations—not the same as a single circumambulation of the ten directions. After completing the summoning, he then ascended to the seat.
○ *Shaowei* says: The *Yuanshi Tianzun* (Primordial Heavenly Worthy) is the responsive title of the *Xu Huang* (Vacuous Sovereign). Arising from the true to respond, it is called *Zheng Xiu* (Attainment and Cultivation). His wondrous thoughts and profound origins are uniquely his own. Thus, the *Dong Shen Jing* (Cavernous Spirit Scripture) states: The wondrous image is formless; the responsive manifestation has substance. The qi of true essence transforms into his countenance. At that time, he turned the scripture ten times, and the ten directions all came to rest. There was no distance too far to respond—all arrived at the seat. *Yi* (arrival) means to approach. The great divine perfected, the exalted sages, the wondrously practicing immortals, and the innumerable hosts came riding the void.
○ *Shaowei* says: *Yang* means cessation. The perfected sages, divine worthies, and their retinues overflow—thousands of chariots, myriad riders—all the heavens came. Measured by this standard, their numbers are beyond count. Crimson clouds and cinnabar skies, emerald carriages and jade wheels, feathered canopies casting shade, flowing essence and jade radiance—five colors flourishing, illuminating the vastness.
○ *Youqi* says: *Yang* means *yang* (center), an ancient character where *yang* was used for *yang* (center). *Yang* (center) means exhaustion or completion. Thus, *Wu Yang Shu Zhong* (innumerable hosts) refers to contemplating their presence.
○ *Shaowei* says: From *Yuan Shi Dong Xuan* (Primordial Beginning Cavernous Mystery) onward is the scripture itself. Beyond measure, all are shaded by feathered canopies and ride emerald carriages, crimson clouds and cinnabar skies bearing jade wheels. The perfected of heaven assemble without exception; the exalted sages arrive in unison. Flowing essence radiates through the ten directions; jade light shines through the void. *Liu Jing* (flowing essence) refers to the five-colored flowing essence within the jade light.

The jade light is the radiance of the perfected ones’ bodies. The great void lies above the Grand Clarity.

○ *Shaowei* says: Crimson clouds and flying auroras coalesce into robes; green carriages and jade wheels are harnessed to dragons and phoenixes. All are the swift, flickering brilliance of essence-light, resplendent in dazzling hues—the sacred vestments of the Heavenly Worthy. The *Statutes* state: From the Brahma Heaven upward, all robes are naturally formed from the wondrous *qi* of flowing auroras.

○ *Xuanying* says: A carriage’s *yu* is its central compartment. Since they wear flowing auroras as garments and ride in green carriages, with canopies of numinous phoenix feathers and teams of nine-colored dragons and phoenixes, their mutual radiance and reflection create feathered canopies casting shade, their brilliance vast and resplendent. Thus it is said: *flowing essence and jade light*, *carriages and robes magnificent*; thus it is said: *five colors*. When the five colors flourish abundantly, it is called *yubo* (lush and vibrant). Countless chariots and myriad riders arrive floating through the void, filling the vast expanse of the great emptiness, all journeying to Floating Blackness to hear the Dharma—hence it is said: *illuminating the vastness*.

For seven days and seven nights, the sun, moon, stars, constellations, *Xuanji*, and *Yuheng* of all heavens halt their revolutions. Divine winds fall silent, mountains and seas conceal their clouds, the sky is free of drifting veils, and the four *qi* grow luminously clear.

○ *Youqi* says: Whenever the term "all heavens" is used, it refers to the thirty-two heavens. Within each heaven, there are sun and moon, their essence-light originally transformed from the roots of this realm. *Xuanji* and *Yuheng* are the seven stars of the Northern Dipper. The *four qi luminously clear* are the *qi* of the four images: heaven, earth, sun, and moon.

When the true transmit truth and the sagely confer sageliness, the Three Luminaries cease their revolutions to remain in illumination, mountains and seas absorb *qi* and swallow mist, the Wind Earl dares not rustle the branches, and the Cloud Marshal ensures no shadows obscure the light. Thus heaven and earth grow bright and open, sun and moon clear and radiant. For seven days and seven nights, as the Dharma rites near completion—though it is said their wheels halt, how could there be night? This is reckoned by the measure of ordinary time, the span of seven days and seven nights.

○ *Shaowei* says: These three are celestial portents. The *Treatise on Astronomy* states: The seven stars of the Northern Dipper are called *Xuanji* and *Yuheng*. The four stars of the Dipper’s bowl form the *Xuanji*; the three stars of its handle form the *Yuheng*. The celestial palaces of the sun, moon, stars, and constellations arrive in their time to hear the Dharma—this is why their wheels halt.

In one land, the earth, mountains, rivers, and forests are leveled as one, without height or depth, the soil all transformed into azure jade, without any other hues.

○ *Youqi* says: "One land" refers to the great land of Floating Blackness. Its mountains bear soaring forests of jade trees, its rivers hold divine streams and numinous ravines. Yet all is level and even, without height or depth to cause imbalance. Since the earth is entirely azure jade, how could there be any杂色 (mixed colors)? This is the wondrous transformation of divine power at that time, naturally causing the sun and moon to halt their revolutions and the mountains and rivers to level themselves.

○ *Shaowei* says: These two are terrestrial responses. The mountains, rivers, and earthly palaces, the dwelling places of the earth’s spirits, respond to the emptiness and transform into azure jade.

The assembled perfected ones sit in attendance as the Primordial Heavenly Worthy of the Dao sits in profound stillness upon a five-colored lion in the empty void.

○ *Youqi* says: The lion exists within the empty void, and the profound stillness is seated upon the lion. The lion is the king of beasts, its might subduing all creatures; with a single roar, all demonic forces submit. The Heavenly Worthy’s divine virtue subdues all demons and thus takes the lion’s seat. Once the Heavenly Worthy ascends to expound the scripture, the assembled perfected ones array themselves to listen.

○ *Shaowei* says: This is the Heavenly Worthy’s manifestation of the Dao.

After one recitation of the scripture, the great sages of all heavens simultaneously proclaim its excellence. At that time, the deaf and ailing men and women of the land regain their hearing.

○ *Youqi* says: Upon first hearing the Heavenly Worthy’s numinous voice, which reveals the wondrous principles of the utmost sageliness, they all cry out in praise—no goodness could be greater. Thus, in the great land of Floating Blackness, whether man or woman, all who hear it find the deaf and ailing restored to hearing. This is the verification of the first recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: At that time, the men and women of the land who heard the Dharma, upon hearing one recitation, awakened in mind and ear—this is called *opening of hearing*. It is also said: the *land* is the body. Hearing the Dharma and awakening is to enter the palace of the heart—this is the *opening of hearing*.

After two recitations, the blind regain their sight.

○ *Youqi* says: First, their ears hear the wondrous meaning; next, their eyes behold the Heavenly Worthy—this is the verification of the second recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: With two recitations, they gradually recognize the scripture’s words—thus it is said their *eyes grow bright*. If one considers the focus of attention, this is not an ailment of the physical form.

After three recitations, the mute can speak.

○ *Youqi* says: Since their eyes can now behold the sacred countenance, their mouths can also speak the scripture—this is the verification of the third recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: With three recitations, their minds awaken to understanding, and they can naturally transmit the wondrous Dharma—thus it is said they *can speak*.

After four recitations, the lame, the chronically ill, and those afflicted with long-standing ailments all rise and walk.

○ *Youqi* says: Since their mouths can now speak the scripture, their feet can also walk the Dao—this is the verification of the fourth recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: Though they could speak after three recitations, they had not yet fully grasped the true principle. By the fourth recitation, they understand how to seek a teacher and inquire into the meaning—thus it is said they *can walk*. *Ji dai* refers to illnesses transmitted through the ages, spreading and affecting others.

After five recitations, those with long-standing chronic illnesses instantly regain their original form.

○ *Youqi* says: Since their feet can now walk the Dao, their entire bodies engage in cultivation—this is the verification of the fifth recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: With five recitations, awakening resides in the heart, and merit nourishes blessings. This enables those with long-standing chronic illnesses to have them all dispelled, instantly regaining their original form, as if they had never been ill.

After six recitations, white hair turns black again, and fallen teeth regrow.

○ *Youqi* says: Since their entire bodies engage in cultivation, their forms receive the true effects—this is the verification of the sixth recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: With six recitations, the merit is abundant and blessings profound, enabling white hair to turn black again and fallen teeth to regrow.

After seven recitations, the old regain their youth, and the young grow even stronger.

○ *Youqi* says: First, the head reveals divine efficacy; next, the entire body bathes in sacred grace—this is the verification of the seventh recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: With seven recitations of the scripture, the old become youthful again, and the young and robust grow even healthier.

After eight recitations, women conceive, and birds and beasts carry young; whether already born or yet unborn, all attain life and completion.

○ *Youqi* says: Those already born revert to youth and shed old age; those yet unborn attain life—this is the verification of the eighth recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: The merit of seven recitations encompasses the seven consciousnesses and transforms the Three Realms; with eight recitations, the blessings extend to the Four Kinds of Birth, bringing joy to all sentient beings. Those born from the womb do not miscarry, those born from eggs do not perish, and all receive nurturance—hence it is said that all attain life and completion.

After nine recitations, the earth’s treasuries open, and gold and jade reveal their forms.

○ *Youqi* says: Once humans attain the life of their nature, they further perceive the opening of the earth’s treasuries, and the people of the land all obtain the precious weight of gold and jade—this is the verification of the ninth recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: The previous passage spoke of the transformation extending to the Four Kinds of Birth; here, even the hidden and solitary receive blessings. The earth’s treasuries are opened, revealing the forms of gold and jade; filling the mountains and rivers, people obtain sufficient use—hence it is said that gold and jade reveal their forms.

After ten recitations, withered bones revive and all rise as living people.

○ *Youqi* says: Having obtained the treasures of the secret treasuries, next the foul and decayed are transformed into the wondrous—this is the verification of the tenth recitation.

○ *Xuanying* says: With nine recitations, the Dao permeates the earth; with ten recitations, it ascends to move the various heavens. Thus, the Supreme One’s *Huihai Lingfu* revives the long-dead withered bones, raising them as living people. At this time, in the entire land, whether man or woman, none do not turn their hearts wholeheartedly, all receive protection and deliverance, and all attain longevity.

○ *Youqi* says: At this moment, in the land of *Fuli*, whether man or woman, young or old, all receive the sacred grace and are universally delivered. The living do not die, and the dead revive—hence all attain longevity.

○ *Xuanying* says: *Qing* means "to exhaust." When the Heavenly Worthy expounded the scripture, all the men and women of *Fuli* sat beside him, hearing the wondrous Dharma and each listening with their whole hearts—hence it is said that none do not turn their hearts wholeheartedly. The people of the land receive this wondrous Dharma of deliverance—hence it is said that all receive protection and deliverance; having attained the Dao of true completion, it is said that all attain longevity. Among all the heavenly and human beings, illnesses vary in severity, and the methods of cultivating the Dao differ according to the depth of merit. For minor illnesses, fewer recitations bring healing; for severe illnesses, greater merit brings cure. Thus, it is known that reciting the scripture ten times reaches the various heavens, revives the dead, restores the bones, and grants longevity.

○ *Shaowei* says: When dragons and tigers roar, wind and clouds arise; when the sage acts, the Three Realms respond—this is the natural principle, the inevitable sign. Thus, with ten recitations of the scripture, a hundred ailments are instantly cured. If not for the great sagacity of the Primordial Beginning, who could achieve this? Yet the old methods of learning mistakenly hold that illnesses of the mind and wisdom are not illnesses of the physical form—this error is grave indeed.

Some say: According to the *Zhongren Sitianshu*, cutting off all habitual tendencies, all people become spiritually luminous and do not undergo womb birth. Now, the Heavenly Worthy expounds the scripture in the *Biluo*, which is the third heaven of the *Zhongren*. Why then do the illnesses of the people of this land resemble those of ordinary mortals in the world below? This view is not adopted here. By the power of authority, what is called "a land" refers to a domain—just as feudal lords take their territories as their lands, the Son of Heaven takes the Four Seas as his land, and the Thirty-Two Emperors each take their thirty-two heavens as their lands. Thus, the Heavenly Worthy’s Dao is all-pervading, and his transformation knows no bounds—one may take the Eight Round Worlds as a single land. If this is considered a land, then who is not within the Heavenly Worthy’s land? That men and women have illnesses is nothing strange. The *Kongdong Lingzhang* says: "The wind stirs the Eight Rounds, turning the floating and distant into brightness." The old explanation says: The eight directions and the various heavens are called the Eight Rounds. The *Xuandu* is the Central Palace, and each of the eight directions has five hundred fifty-five thousand five hundred fifty billion layers. Such are the multitude of heavens, the realm of the Primordial Beginning’s singular transformation.

The scripture says: At that time, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy expounded the scripture once, and the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the eastern direction, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrived floating through the void.

○ *Youqi* says: "At that time" refers to the moment when the scripture was first expounded. With the first recitation, the hosts from the eastern direction arrived in full. Since there are distinctions of rank and hierarchy, it is said to be of boundless and limitless ranks. Like fine dust in a crevice, they are innumerable—hence it is said to be a host without end. All ride the void, floating through space to arrive. *Yang* means "center," the meaning of which has already been explained above. This is the moment when, with the first recitation, the deaf regain their hearing.

○ *Xuanying* says: This passage recounts the Heavenly Worthy’s circuit of scripture recitation to summon the ten directions. The earlier text broadly summoned the ten directions but did not specify their locations. This passage repeats the account so that learners may deeply understand that the Heavenly Worthy’s gathering of the various heavens is not without order. Thus, with the first recitation of the scripture, the perfected great spirits of boundless and limitless ranks from the eastern direction, a host without end, arrive floating through the void. *Yang* means "to cease." The minds of the perfected sages are without attachment; they respond when moved. Thus, hearing the scripture once, they arrive floating through the void. The summons is vast and far-reaching—hence it reaches the boundless. The perfected sages are limitless—hence it is said that the hosts all come to witness the Dharma and transmit deliverance to the heavenly and human beings.

After two recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the southern direction, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.

Youxī says: The meanings of the ten directions all correspond to these first two recitations—this is the moment when the blind regain their sight.

After three recitations of the scripture, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the western direction, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first three recitations, when the mute regain their speech.

After four recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the northern direction, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first four recitations, when the lame and the chronically ill all rise and walk.

After five recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the northeast, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first five recitations, when long-standing chronic illnesses are instantly restored to wholeness.

After six recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the southeast, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first six recitations, when white hair turns black again and fallen teeth regrow.

After seven recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the southwest, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first seven recitations, when the old regain their youth and the young grow strong.

After eight recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the northwest, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first eight recitations, when pregnant women, birds, and beasts bearing young—whether already born or yet unborn—all attain perfect birth and completion.

After nine recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the upper direction, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first nine recitations, when the earth’s treasuries open and gold and jade reveal their forms.

After ten recitations, the immeasurable hosts of perfected great spirits from the lower direction, of boundless and limitless ranks, arrive floating through the void.
Youxī says: This is the moment of the first ten recitations, when withered bones revive and all rise as fully formed humans.

Youxī says: After one recitation, one direction is summoned; after ten recitations, all ten directions are complete. Thus, the thirty-two heavens together with the four cardinal directions, above and below, are called the ten directions.

Shaowēi says: This again recounts the cyclical recitation of the scripture to summon the ten directions. Yet the Heavenly Worthy is of utmost divinity, extending and preserving freedom—why does he not summon the ten directions at once with ten recitations? It is to demonstrate solemnity and earnestness, so that people may awaken and understand. When the men and women of a nation wholeheartedly turn in reverence, those who come are like fine rain or dense mist—an immeasurable host filling half the land, causing the earth to tilt and sink, unstoppable.

Youxī says: *Zé* means "to fill and obstruct." Repeatedly describing the people of the nation turning in reverence to the numinous model, their hearts transformed by the true teaching, coming like fine rain flying through the sky, gathering like dense mist enveloping all—so filled and obstructed that the land tilts and sinks. This illustrates their vast numbers. By reason, the land should not tilt and sink; like grass bending before the wind, how could it be resisted? Thus, the sage is without fixed intent, adapting to things as they are.

Shaowēi says: This nation is the great land of Fuli. "Filling half the nation" means the gathering occupies half the land. *Zé* means "to occupy." Then the Primordial Beginning suspends a single treasure pearl, as large as a grain of millet, in the dark mystery of the void, five *zhang* above the earth. The Primordial Beginning leads the perfected great spirits of heaven, the lofty and venerable sages, the perfected of wondrous conduct, and the immeasurable hosts of boundless and limitless perfected great spirits from the ten directions—all enter into the treasure pearl.

Youxī says: The treasure pearl is a metaphor for the Dao/Way. Thus, it is suspended in the dark mystery of the void, corresponding to the meaning of the "mysterious pearl." "As large as a grain of millet" refers to the chief of the five grains, the foundation of human life. It means that those who obtain the scripture are like those who rely on grain for life. Moreover, to receive the transmission of the numinous writ within the treasure pearl is to find treasure within treasure, mystery within mystery, the true within the true, the Dao/Way within the Dao/Way. Thus, the hosts of the ten directions are drawn into the single pearl, further demonstrating the unfathomable transformations of the divine, beyond the reckoning of worldly principles. "Five *zhang* above the earth" means enabling people to transcend the Five Turbidities and escape the workings of the Five Phases. Having transcended the Five Turbidities, one is naturally free from all afflictions; having escaped the workings of the Five Phases, one is forever beyond mutual harm. Thus, when the Five Phases do not harm one another, all things may be preserved whole, naturally attaining long life and enduring vision, realizing the Dao/Way and becoming perfected.

Heavenly and human beings look up and see only a surging multitude entering through the pearl’s opening.
Xuányīng says: *Bóbó* describes the boundless multitude, like rain or mist, entering the pearl’s opening—this also reveals the infinite nature of true wisdom. Once inside the pearl’s opening, their whereabouts are unknown. The people of the nation disperse, and the earth returns to levelness, no longer tilted or sunken.

Youxī says: The "heavenly beings" are the people of the Azure Beginning Heaven; the "people of the nation" are the people of the great land of Fuli. Since they are not the perfected great spirits of heaven, the lofty and venerable sages, they do not enter the pearl’s opening. By analogy, they are also not part of this grand occasion of witnessing and deliverance. Thus, when looking up, they see only the surging multitude entering, entering without obstruction. The pearl is small, yet it does not hinder the multitude. Many and few accommodate one another; small and great contain each other—thus, their whereabouts are unknown. Earlier it was said to be "tilted and sunken," here "tilted and sunken" means uneven. The high places tilt low; initially, half the land was obstructed, appearing tilted and sunken. When the people disperse, it returns to levelness.

Shaowēi says: Former teachings take the pearl as representing the pure, empty, and perfectly spherical essence, and the millet grain as representing the fragrant chief of the hundred grains. Drawing people into the pearl illustrates the all-embracing nature of the wondrous Dao/Way.

Suspended in emptiness, it does not burden the manifold existences. Five *zhang* above the earth, it distances itself from the five desires. The earth returns to levelness, demonstrating the evenness and smoothness of the great Dao/Way; no longer tilted or sunken, it reveals the recovery of true nature. All these interpretations arise from reading against the text, fabricating heterodoxies to shock conventional sensibilities, claiming such things cannot be.

Let us examine this: When the Primordial Beginning first unfolded the charts, the methods and teachings were not uniform—some took non-action and quiescence as their starting point, guiding beings back to their root; others manifested awe-inspiring transformations, compelling people to submit in reverence. Yet the divine powers are free and unconstrained, their true responses boundless. If a pearl can contain heaven and humanity, how could it be impossible?

Moreover, even the minor arts of banished immortals can conceal and reveal within a gourd—how could the august Perfected of the Void be hindered in their movements within a pearl? Within the precious pearl, the Primordial Beginning completed the recitation of the sutra in full.

Xuányīng says: *Jìng* means "to finish" or "to complete." Those who awaken to the Dao/Way have already ascended into the pearl and entered the wondrous. Once the Heavenly Worthy finished reciting the sutra, he transmitted this true scripture to the Most High Lord of the Dao/Way—this refers to the text below. The multitude of Perfected oversaw the deliverance, bestowing it upon me.

Xuányīng says: This clarifies how the Lord of the Dao/Way received the scripture. The "multitude of Perfected" refers to the offices of the Perfected who supervise and deliver beings. After the Primordial Beginning finished reciting the sutra, he commanded these overseeing Perfected to transmit this scripture to the Lord of the Dao/Way. Having received it, the Lord of the Dao/Way says, "bestowed upon me." At that moment, joy and celebration were beyond words; the Dharma affairs were roughly complete, and the hosts of heaven returned to their positions.

Xuányīng says: The Lord of the Dao/Way, having received the true scripture, has already attained some awakening and understanding. Since the Dharma affairs were thus comprehended, the heavenly hosts and sages each returned to their original stations, resuming their usual abodes. In an instant, all was silent, without even an echo.

Yōuqī says: "I" refers to the Lord of the Dao/Way himself. After transmitting the treasure within the pearl, the sacred bestowed the true, a thousand Perfected jointly overseeing, ten thousand sages delivering in unison. The celebration of this assembly—how could it be fully expressed? Once the Dharma affairs were complete and the heavenly assembly was about to disperse, in that fleeting moment of joy, all became dark and silent.

Shaowēi says: The sage has no fixed mind; true responses follow conditions. They arise when encountered, cease when the cause departs. At that time, the heavenly and human beings, having encountered the scripture and Dharma, were universally delivered, preserving their original years.

Xuányīng says: Having heard this wondrous scripture, the great assembly was all delivered, safeguarding their full blessings. Thus, they fulfilled their allotted lifespans without premature harm. The land turned in reverence, all cultivating virtuous minds.

Yōuqī says: At that time, the people of heaven and earth—men and women alike—upon hearing the scripture and witnessing the Dharma, all exhausted their sincere hearts to deliver those in calamity, free from the misfortune of untimely death. The three karmas stilled, the six senses unarisen, all evils vanished, and myriad virtues arose together. They did not kill or harm, did not envy or resent, did not lust or steal, did not covet or desire, did not hate or suspect. Their words were free of embellishment, their mouths free of foul speech.

Yōuqī says: "Did not kill or harm" refers to eliminating the sins of bodily karma; "did not envy or resent" refers to eliminating the sins of mental karma; "did not lust or steal" refers to eliminating the sins of bodily karma; "did not covet or desire" refers to eliminating the sins of mental karma; "did not hate or suspect" refers again to eliminating the sins of mental karma. *Huáqǐ* means adorned, false, and frivolous speech; "foul speech" refers to vulgar, abusive, and venomous language. Having entirely abandoned these twelve evil deeds, one then attains great harmony. Equal in compassion and love, even those of different bones become kin.

Xuányīng says: When all people refrain from the ten evils and act in accord with the principle of true constancy, they become equal in compassion and love, and those of different bones become kin. The ancients did not exclusively love their own kin or exclusively cherish their own children. Yao and Shun, in their abdications, could make the world turn to them with sincerity—how much more so when the Heavenly Worthy recites the scripture, and an entire land turns in reverence, naturally making those of different bones become kin. The land is secure, the people prosperous, rejoicing in great peace.

Yōuqī says: When compassion and love are equal, all things are as one. Safeguarding the land and its people in abundance, they delight in the eternal days of great peace.

Shaowēi says: To sever life is called "killing"; to injure and wound is called "harm." To resent others for surpassing oneself is called "envy"; to hate one’s peers is called "resentment." Sexual union without propriety is called "lust"; stealing others’ possessions is called "theft." Insatiability is called "covetousness"; indulgence in cravings is called "desire." Disliking others is called "hatred"; suspicion is called "doubt." Once the ten evils are extinguished, those of different bones become kin; when the myriad practices are mystically united, speech is free of discord. Naturally, epidemics do not arise, people suffer no untimely harm, the harvests are abundant, and the land enjoys great peace.

Xuányīng says: When compassion and love are equal, the land is surely secure. Without premature harm, people are naturally prosperous. The five grains ripen, and disasters do not arise. With these manifold virtuous merits, it is said they rejoice in great peace.

When the scripture first emerged as teaching, the land was guided by the Dao/Way. Those with sincere hearts who revered and honored it were all delivered from the world.

Yōuqī says: Thereupon, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy, observing the people’s faith and goodness, revealed the true model to guide them. Those who cultivated with utmost sincerity were certain to ascend as immortals and be delivered from the world.

Shaowēi says: This speaks of one region transforming and all regions benefiting, near people submitting and distant people yielding.

The scripture says: What the Primordial Heavenly Worthy recited within the sutra—

Xuányīng says: This refers to the *Hùndòng Chìwén* and the *Yuándòng Yùlì*, which are the *Língbǎo Běnzhāng*.

—are all the inner names and hidden rhymes of the Celestial Emperors of the various heavens.

Yōuqī says: What the scripture refers to are the hidden names of the thirty-two heavens and the inner taboos of the thirty-two Celestial Emperors mentioned in the latter two chapters. All are the words of the great Brahmā, not to be lightly questioned or scrutinized—hence, they are called "hidden rhymes."

These are also the inner taboos of the Demon Kings and the hidden names of the Hundred Spirits—words not of this world’s common speech.

Yōuqī says: The inner taboos of the Demon Kings are the taboo characters of the Five Thearchs and Great Demons. The hidden names of the Hundred Spirits are the titles of Wúyīng and Báiyuán. Since all are hidden names and inner taboos, they are not the common speech of this world.

The perfected immortals among the exalted sages, who have penetrated the mysteries and probed the subtleties, are able to master their texts in full.

Shaowēi says: The *Zìlín* states: *xī* means "thorough and complete."

Yōuqī says: Since these are inner names and hidden rhymes, not the common speech of this world, only among true persons are there those with the talent to penetrate the mysteries and the insight to probe the subtleties, who can thus comprehend their purport. When recited ten times, the various heavens chant in unison from afar, the ten thousand Thearchs offer rites of reverence, rivers and seas fall silent, mountains and peaks conceal their clouds, sun and moon pause in their course, and the jade celestial pivots cease their turning.

Yōuqī says: This speaks of the exalted sages who have become true persons and penetrated the mysteries and probed the subtleties—when they recite these ten times, their Way resonates with the various heavens, and thus the heavens chant in unison from afar. Their virtue equals that of the ten thousand Thearchs, and so the Thearchs offer rites to welcome them as guests.

Rivers and seas still the flying surges of their waves, mountains and peaks gather in their clouds and mists and raise none. The Three Luminaries halt their radiance, the Seven Brilliant Ones congeal their splendor, heaven and earth stand in steadfast clarity, and day and night shine forth as torches. All demons bind their forms, ghostly spirits extinguish their consciousness, the dead return to life, and white bones become human once more.

Yōuqī says: Since the true Dao proceeds unimpeded, evil demons vanish into concealment, and thus withered bones regain their once-transcended souls, and white bones recover the spirits of their former forms. If one can cause the dead to live again, then surely one can ensure that the living never die—this is the standard of the true person. For those of utmost learning who recite it ten times, the Five Thearchs stand in attendance, the Three Realms bow their heads, demonic spirits lose their sight, ghostly pernicious forces extinguish their consciousness, and those on the verge of death are saved and restored to life.

Yōuqī says: Those of utmost learning are those whose hearts are firmer than iron and stone, whose conduct is more resolute than water and fire, whom heaven and earth cannot surpass, and whom ghosts and spirits cannot delude. They walk paths that others cannot walk, and though they exist, they seem as if absent. Thus, when those whose true names are recorded above the Great Ultimate recite it ten times, the Five Thearchs flank and attend them on left and right, the Three Realms bow their heads in reverence, evil demons lose their eyesight, and those on the verge of death naturally regain life. The Five Thearchs are the celestial Thearchs of the five directions. The Three Realms are the demon kings of the Three Realms.

Shǎowēi says: The great Dao of the exalted sages possesses the majestic power to govern heaven. Those of utmost learning, their strength being slight, can only subdue the earth. Governing heaven enables one to halt the turning of the Three Radiant Ones and restore life to white bones. Subduing the earth enables one to make the Three Realms bow their heads and revive those on the verge of death. The boundaries between great and small cannot be transgressed. The reason for this is that the impure qi of the learned has not yet dissipated, and their bodies have not yet penetrated the true. When summoning and governing the ten directions, their majesty does not yet govern the celestial administration.

Shǎowēi says: The celestial administration refers to the sun, moon, five planets, and the seven celestial bodies of the heavenly patterns. Their virtue can only subdue and govern the earthly deities, binding and restraining demonic spirits, merely averting death but unable to restore life.

Yōuqī says: *Ěr* means "thus." Those of utmost learning, their names and conduct having ascended to the standard of the true, their merit and efficacy surpassing those of ordinary people—yet because their physical forms are not yet true and impure qi still lingers, they cannot yet summon and govern the ten directions, nor can they manifest majesty before the various heavens. They can only subdue and govern evil demons, avert imminent death, but cannot restore form to withered bones and dry skeletons—this is the standard of the utmost scholar.

Shǎowēi says: The learned scholar is the one of utmost learning. Their spiritual power is not vast, their merit not yet complete, so they cannot majestically govern celestial phenomena but can only subdue and govern earthly deities. Their power can avert death at the brink of dying but cannot revive withered bones.

To recite this chapter lightly brings calamity upon oneself.

Shǎowēi says: The Five Thearchs and their majestic spirits attend and guard the *Numinous Treasure*, overseeing those who treat it with irreverence—truly a perilous path. To offer reverent veneration brings prosperity to one’s household, flourishing generation after generation, forming good karmic connections, warding off the ten thousand disasters, and securing the protection of divine spirits.

Yōuqī says: To recite lightly means to do so without proper attire or adherence to ritual protocols, or to recite carelessly while walking, standing, sitting, or lying down. Not only does this bring retribution upon oneself, but it also implicates one’s ancestors. If one instead reveres and honors it with utmost respect, it brings prosperity to one’s household, blessings to oneself, flourishing descendants, the eradication of evil roots, and constant association with goodness. Since the thousand spirits come to protect, how could the ten thousand disasters intrude? From this, it is clear that to recite without true understanding is not as good as not reciting at all while maintaining reverence. Those who uphold this scripture should examine this carefully.

This scripture is exalted and wondrous, unmatched in the Jade Capital.

Shǎowēi says: This means that by employing this wondrous Dao alone, one can traverse the Jade Capital. The *Scripture of Original Appearance* states: Above the Great Canopy Heaven is the Jade Capital Mountain, which grows without roots and stands suspended in the void. Within it is the Supreme Palace of the Purple Tenuity, spanning three hundred thousand miles in each direction. Its towers and terraces are adorned with gold and jade, embellished with the radiance of the seven treasures. Above the Jade Chamber are thirty-six precincts, each eight thousand miles in circumference, filled with true writings in large characters. It delivers countless beings and serves as the origin of the ten thousand Daoist paths. Its towering and majestic model is so vast that its virtue is difficult to surpass.

Shǎowēi says: The *Erya* states: *Fàn* means "model."

Yōuqī says: Since it is revered by all heavens and not transmitted to the lower world, it is kept in the secret treasury of the Purple Tenuity and employed uniquely in the Dark Capital. It is the foremost means of delivering beings and the foremost among all Daoist paths. Its towering and sagely model rivals the Kunlun in piercing the clouds; its virtue and capacity are as unfathomable as the vast ocean. This is its wondrous Dao.

The Dao says: Whenever one recites this scripture ten times, all heavens arrive in unison. The suffering souls of the billions of ancestors, from the most distant to the nearest, all receive deliverance and ascend to the Vermilion Palace.

Yōuqī says: This refers to all who recite it, regardless of their rank or standard, as long as they recite it ten times with focused devotion and in accordance with the method. Then the multitude of sagely beings from all heavens descend and gather in the ancestral temple, delivering the suffering souls of ancestors and remote kin. They depart from the Northern Mansion and enter the Southern Palace. The Vermilion Palace is the Southern Palace. After nine years of refinement, they receive transformation and are reborn, becoming noble persons. Those who diligently study this scripture, their merit complete and virtue perfected, all attain transcendence, ascend to the Golden Gates, and roam and feast in the Jade Capital.

Yōuqī says: "Nine years of refinement" refers to the nine-year standard, meaning the number of the three fires—three times three makes nine. The Vermilion Palace is in the south, associated with fire. Refining the form with fire is called the three fires. After nine years of refinement and transformation, they are then reborn as noble persons. Once born, they immediately cultivate this scripture, for the influence of past practice remains. When the merit of ten thousand recitations is complete and the virtue of three thousand deeds is fulfilled, they transcend and ascend directly, attaining transcendence.

Ascending the Golden Gates to pay homage to the Sacred Sovereign, roaming the Jade Capital to audience with the Primordial Beginning—this is the standard of ten recitations.

○ The Lesser Florescence says: This clarifies the deliverance of one’s ancestors.

According to the *Three Primes’ Precepts of Ranks*, the standards for deliverance by the Vermilion Mansion comprise three grades. Nine years mark the middle blessing; great blessing requires but three years, while lesser blessing demands twenty-four. All are reborn in the lower realms as noble persons. By virtue of their former affinities, they cultivate with devotion, escape the cycle of birth and death, and attain transcendence. Those of superior learning who recite this scripture are immediately delivered, ascending to the Southern Palace.

○ Yōuqī says: Those of superior learning are they who, upon hearing the Dao, practice diligently, and upon encountering the Dharma, study without cease. Unyielding through cold and heat, these are they whose names are recorded among the transcendents below the Nine Palaces of Grand Clarity. Having recited this scripture, they attain the Dao in body, ascend to the immortal realms, and undergo refinement in the Southern Palace. When the hun and po ascend as transcendents, the ghostly substance is refined by fire; when the living body attains the Dao, the filth and defilements are refined by fire. All first enter the Southern Palace, then ascend to their proper stations—this is the standard for the superior adept.

For those of the world who recite it, life is prolonged and years extended; afterward, all attain the Way of corpse-liberation. The hun-spirit temporarily perishes, yet they escape the hells, swiftly regain their form, and roam the Great Void.

○ Yōuqī says: The people of the world are those of the common path, not the elect. As their ancestral affinities are shallow and their personal karma slight, they enjoy long life while living, and after death, their forms dissolve temporarily. Yet they are not bound by the regulations of the Three Offices nor suffer the trials of the Nine Bureaus. When the appointed time arrives, their spirits return and their forms are restored. Having transformed their appearance in the halls of the Three Offices and exchanged their youthful countenances for the ninefold-refined corpse, they do not enter the Southern Palace above but traverse the realms of the Great Void. The Great Void lies above the Three Domains of Grand Clarity—this is the standard for the people of the world.

From the perfected to the common, there are five grades, each distinct in rank.

○ The Lesser Florescence says: This further clarifies that even the people of the world, by reciting it, may deliver themselves. Though their virtue is meager and their merit incomplete, they may not ascend with flesh and bone together, yet they attain deliverance through corpse-liberation. The *Scripture of Original Appearances* states: "If prior merit is not established, then afterward, flesh and bone do not ascend as transcendents; thus, they attain the Dao through corpse-liberation."

According to the superior scriptures, corpse-liberation has four kinds:
1. **Martial liberation**, as when Jikang entrusted his execution to the marketplace, or Huainan transformed his form in prison;
2. **Literary liberation**, as when Ciqing exchanged his essence for shoes, or Changfang dissolved his form in bamboo;
3. **Refinement by water and fire**, as when Feng Yi drowned in the great river, or Fengzi was consumed by the fire-tree;
4. **Refinement by Grand Yin**, wherein one appears dead—feet uncyanosed, skin unwrinkled, eyes undimmed—yet limbs remain pliable, and the corpse does not decay for a hundred years before reviving as a full-grown person.

The *True Sayings* records: Master Pei said: "Those who attain corpse-liberation as transcendents may not ride the flowered canopy, mount the flying dragon, ascend the Grand Ultimate, or roam the Nine Palaces—they merely escape death. Liberation by bow and sword is martial; by bamboo staff, literary; together with water, fire, and Grand Yin, these make four kinds of liberation."

This scripture is subtle and wondrous, universally delivering without end; all celestial and human beings receive its blessings. Boundless merit extends grace to the living and the dead.

○ Yōuqī says: The efficacy of this scripture’s power is vast and profound, difficult to fathom. Ten recitations align the ten thousand qi, and all ascend as transcendents; five grades deliver countless beings. Celestial and human beings bathe in the joy of liberation, while the living and the dead rely on its grace for deliverance.

This treasure of the heavens is not transmitted to the lower world.

○ The Lesser Florescence says: When the Heavenly Worthy expounded the scripture, it was not transmitted to the lower world. When the Queen Mother entreated its preservation to avert the calamity of the *jiǎ-shēn* year, it began to circulate, and thus the world first received it.

Master Song says: This scripture delivers beings in four ways:
1. Ascending to heaven in broad daylight, delivered in the body;
2. Delivered through transformation by corpse-liberation;
3. Dying yet not decaying, later reviving;
4. The hun-spirit temporarily perishing, then ascending to the Southern Palace for refinement.

As karma varies in weight, so too do the rewards differ. It delivers even one’s great-grandparents, hence it is said that both the living and the dead receive its grace.

Those of utmost sincerity offer gold and treasures, swearing oaths to the heavens before transmitting it. To leak or profane it lightly brings misfortune upon nine generations, condemning them to long servitude as ghostly officials.

○ Yōuqī says: As it is called a secret of the Mystic Metropolis, it was rightfully not transmitted to the lower world. Now, by the Most High’s dissemination, it has descended to humanity. Thus, those of utmost sincerity offer gold and treasures to pledge their devotion, proclaiming solemn vows. To violate the oath is to invite punishment upon nine generations; to guard its secrecy is to align the merit of a hundred ancestors.

○ The Lesser Florescence says: The sacred text is profound and weighty; its transmission is no trifling matter. How could one lightly disseminate it and bring calamity upon nine generations?

Five Emperors, with twenty-four Jade Lads and twenty-four Jade Maidens each, attend the scripture, safeguarding its divine text and protecting the bodies of those who receive it.

○ Yōuqī says: The Five Emperors’ Jade Lads and Jade Maidens refer to the Jade Lads and Maidens who attend the Five Emperors—not that the Five Emperors and the Jade Lads and Maidens all attend together. The Five Emperors are the Five Elder Sovereigns, not the emperors of the five directions. Together, the lads and maidens number forty-eight. They constantly guard the divine text of the scripture and also protect those who recite it, commending their sincere merit and scrutinizing transgressions of leakage or profanation. Those who receive and recite it must be cautious.

When going out or traveling, one should carry it, so that the text may shield the body, avert disasters, and dispel worries.

The Dao says: In the first month, observe a prolonged fast and recite this scripture to sever the earthly servitude of past lives’ souls and deliver them to the Southern Palace above.

○ Yōuqī says: The first month is the great celebration of the Upper Prime.

Thus, blessings extend to one’s ancestors and forebears of past generations, delivering the suffering souls of the departed from the servitude of ghosts and spirits, and granting them the joy of salvation by the immortal officials. As for the term "fast," it means that the body is free from miscellaneous affairs, the mind is not distracted by external thoughts, both inner and outer are pure and empty, and one embraces the Origin and guards the One throughout this month—hence the term "prolonged fast." In the seventh month, observe a prolonged fast and recite this scripture, and the body shall attain immortality; the names of the adept shall be inscribed in the heavens on yellow registers and white tablets, erasing death and ascending to life.

Yōuqī says: The seventh month is the great celebration of the Middle Prime.

Thus, the Middle Prime extends to one’s own person, and the names ascend to life in the heavens; recorded on white tablets, they are stricken from the registers of Mount Feng and Mount Tai, and inscribed in the black ledgers, the body attains immortality and the rank of a celestial official in the Heavenly Palace. The "yellow registers" and "white tablets" are written in gold on yellow paper and inscribed on white jade slips. Here, the Lower Prime of the tenth month is not mentioned because the Upper Prime extends blessings to ancestors, the Middle Prime to oneself, and the Lower Prime to one’s descendants. Now, since all have been made clear that the foremost task is cultivation, and cultivation above concerns ancestors while below it does not involve descendants, the Lower Prime of the tenth month is thus omitted. The scripture also does not speak of the merits or transgressions of the Lower Prime. Those who pursue cultivation must examine and consider this carefully.

Shaowei says: When the Celestial Officials review the seasons, it is fitting to deliver one’s ancestors; when the Earthly Officials examine the months, it is proper to deliver oneself. This distinction in sequence reflects the order of precedence and hierarchy. The yellow registers and white tablets are the records of immortals. The *Scripture of the Recorded Characters and Extended Years* states: "Names inscribed in the Emperor’s register arise from past karmic affinities, all through diligent devotion—it is not by chance."

Xuanying says: According to the *Three Primes’ Grades and Ranks*, the first month is when the three yang qi arise, corresponding to the time when the Upper Prime’s celestial officials review and determine destinies, making it fitting to deliver one’s ancestors. The seventh month is the Middle Prime’s month of review, the time when the Earthly Officials examine and assess, making it proper to deliver oneself. This, too, reflects the distinction in sequence and the order of precedence and hierarchy. The method of cultivating the Dao universally delivers the boundless, universally saves the living and the dead, and moistens all things, whether moving or still; above, it benefits the imperial ancestral temples, and below, it aids the suffering souls of the Five Pains—how could it be limited to the salvation of the seven generations of ancestors? This is to inspire filial devotion in people, hence it is said to be for the souls of past generations. In the tenth month, observe a prolonged fast and recite this scripture for the sake of emperors, kings, lords, ministers, fathers, and sons, to secure and stabilize the nation’s destiny, preserve the heavens’ enduring existence, ensure unbroken generations of rulers, and maintain eternal sovereignty over their domains, so that the people may call it the Great Peace. On the eight nodal days, recite this scripture to become a Perfected One of the Nine Palaces.

Yōuqī says: The eight nodal days refer to the four beginnings (the starts of the seasons), the two equinoxes, and the two solstices.

These are all days of grand celestial celebrations and auspicious gatherings, when the merits and transgressions of cultivators are reviewed. If one can fast and recite on these days, one shall become a Perfected One of the Nine Palaces. The reason for this is that the Nine Palaces, excluding the central honored position, encircle the eight palaces corresponding to the eight nodal days. Since they align with these days, recitation allows one to ascend to this realm.

Shaowei says: One Prime has three palaces, and three Primes have nine palaces. Another explanation: On the eight nodal days, eight scribe-spirits descend to observe people’s good and evil deeds, which is why one must cultivate and recite on these days. Why does recitation on the eight nodal days make one a Perfected One of the Nine Palaces? It is because the eight nodal days correspond to the eight trigrams, and when the three on the left and the seven on the right are combined, adding the central palace makes nine palaces—hence the name Perfected One of the Nine Palaces. On one’s natal day, recite this scripture to purify and rectify the soul and spirit, ensuring the eternal preservation of the myriad qi, sparing one from suffering and affliction, and bestowing a radiant light upon the body.

Yōuqī says: The natal day is the day of one’s year and cyclical sign, when only the merits and transgressions of the individual are reviewed—hence the need to fast and recite on this day. Moreover, for a person, qi is the root and spirit is the foundation. When qi is preserved, the spirit is rectified; when the foundation is firm, the root runs deep. When inner spirit and qi harmonize, external radiance naturally manifests. Thus, myriad worries do not arise, and suffering and affliction cannot enter. Since one cultivates and recites on one’s natal day, one can preserve one’s own spirit and qi. The sages established these principles for a reason, and by extension, the principles of cultivating the real become self-evident.

Shaowei says: When the spirit is harmonious, qi flows smoothly; thus, hearing the numinous sounds, one’s spirit becomes pure and clear, and perceiving emptiness and whiteness, one’s radiance shines forth.

The Commentary says: On the natal day, the Lord of Life descends to examine people’s good and evil deeds, which is why one must cultivate this scripture. If one does evil, perverse qi enters the body; if one does good, upright qi returns to oneself, ensuring eternal preservation and sparing one from suffering and affliction. The Three Realms provide guardianship, the Five Emperors oversee reception, the myriad spirits pay homage, and one’s name is inscribed in the heavens. When merit is complete and virtue perfected, one ascends in broad daylight to the Upper Clarity.

Yōuqī says: The guardianship of the Three Realms refers to the attendants of the demon kings of the Three Realms. The Five Emperors’ oversight of reception refers to the Five Celestial Emperors’ welcoming and sending off. Thus, when one sits in audience with the host of spirits, one’s name is inscribed in the Emperor’s register. When the merit of ten thousand recitations is fulfilled and the thousand practices of virtue are perfected, one ascends to heaven in broad daylight and flies to the Upper Clarity.

Shaowei says: Master Lu states: The Upper Clarity is the Central Capital. According to the *Scripture of the Dragon’s Ascent*: Above the Four Brahma Heavens lie the Three Clarities. The Great Clarity has twelve heavens, where the Nine Immortals dwell; next is the Upper Clarity with twelve heavens, where the Nine Perfected reside; and the Jade Clarity has twelve heavens, where the Nine Sages reside. These thirty-six heavens are all indestructible realms. The *Scripture of the Cavernous Spirit* states: The Three Clarity Heavens are naturally transformed, standing in the void, with palaces of the seven treasures, neither arising nor perishing, and attended by a hundred spirits.

The Dao says: On the days of practicing the Dao, one should bathe with fragrant water, fast, enter the chamber, and face east.

Yōuqī says: The days of practicing the Dao are the days of reciting this scripture.

Fearing that one may fail to maintain this practice over time, it is thus said: "the days of practicing the Dao" are precisely the auspicious days mentioned earlier. Each time, one should bathe with fragrant water, then enter a separate chamber to purify the heart and cleanse the self, abiding in clarity and non-action. For those dwelling in the mountains with limited means, one may also use one’s own sleeping chamber, keeping it always tidy and clean. First, don fresh garments, rinse the mouth, and place the scripture upon the reading stand. Then, in the scripture hall, light incense, bow in reverence, kneel, and make one’s entreaty.

The purpose of recitation and cultivation is to take the scripture into the chamber, sit upright facing east, light incense, and unfold the text. Focus the mind and let the eyes follow the words, chanting softly. If one merely recites hastily, errors in the text will abound; in such cases, one should return to the previous thirty characters and read them again, avoiding haste. To rush through the repetitions for the sake of quantity is to squander merit and risk grave harm. Modulate the voice in recitation, harmonizing the spirits and invigorating the soul, ensuring that the fragrant qi lingers unbroken in the chamber.

Upon reaching this passage, perform the prescribed visualization and knock the teeth thirty-two times, corresponding to the thirty-two heavens. Bow thirty-two times in the heart. Shaowei says: *The True Sayings* state: "Knock the teeth to gather the spirits; swallow the saliva to harmonize the true." The *Book of Changes* says: "The Supreme emerges from Zhen." Zhen is the direction of long life, the honored quarter of all heavens—hence facing east.

First, visualize the Heaven of Huangcen and bow to it; then proceed to each Heavenly Emperor in turn, bowing once for each. Close the eyes and meditate, envisioning the body seated amidst clouds of three colors: azure, yellow, and white. Shaowei says: "Mysterious qi is azure; primordial qi is yellow; original qi is white." Visualize these three qi. Within and without, all is dim and profound, with the Azure Dragon, White Tiger, Vermilion Bird, Black Tortoise, lions, and white cranes arrayed to left and right, while sun and moon illuminate the chamber. The room shines resplendently, a radiant orb rising from the crown, its light pervading the ten directions—all must be vividly imagined.

The secret incantation says: Youxi says: Light incense again and half-open the eyes. Place the hands together upon the knees, then knock the teeth thirty-two times, each knock resonating with one heaven. When finished, visualize oneself rising to bow to the thirty-two Heavenly Emperors, beginning from the east and proceeding counterclockwise through the four directions, bowing once to each. After completing the bows, close the eyes and visualize oneself seated, naturally enveloped in clouds of azure, yellow, and white, filling the chamber in dense, billowing profusion. To the left is the Azure Dragon, to the right the White Tiger; before is the Vermilion Bird, behind the Black Tortoise. Lions stand in two rows on either side, eight in each, facing one another. White cranes accompany the lions. The sun is before, the moon behind, their light illuminating the chamber. A radiant orb rises from the crown, its brilliance penetrating the ten directions. After completing this visualization, review it once more, ensuring all is as clear as if seen with the eyes.

The secret incantation is spoken with the mouth moving but without sound. The Supreme Mysterious Primordial Most High Dao Lord summons forth from within my body the Three and Five Merit Officials, the Left and Right Attendant Envoys, the Jade Lads who tend the incense, the Jade Maidens who transmit words, the Five Thearchs’ Direct Talismans, and the Incense Officials of the Day—thirty-two of each—opening and declaring the following: "Today is an auspicious and joyous occasion, a day of prolonged purification and clarity in the hall, of cultivating and reciting the scripture to deliver boundless beings. May what I and those born under the cyclical signs of *jia* and *yi* now declare ascend directly to the august presence of the Most High Thirty-Two Heavens’ Primordial Thearch, the Supreme Honor."

Shaowei notes: The Primordial Thearch is another title for the Heavenly Venerable.

This done, draw in *qi* thirty-two times.

Shaowei notes: "Drawing *qi*" means inhaling it through the mouth, not expelling it.

Then visualize the *qi* of each of the Thirty-Two Heavens in its respective color, inhaling them in sequence, beginning with the Heaven of Imperial Might.

Face east to recite the scripture.

Youxi observes: Once the furnace invocation is uttered, there is no need for exhaustive detail; only the essentials are stated here. The Incense Officials of the Day are one for each of the Thirty-Two Heavens. They descend to oversee and later ascend to report. "Today is an auspicious occasion" refers to the propitious days of the Three Primes and Eight Festivals. Each time it is said, "Today, such-and-such a day, is auspicious," and since prolonged purification is repeatedly mentioned, one must indeed fast. "I and those born under *jia* and *yi*" later encompasses the sun, moon, heaven, earth, stars, the sovereign, and all living beings. In ordinary times, it refers to oneself and one’s ancestors. The Primordial Thearch is not the same as the Primordial Heavenly Venerable. The Thearch is exalted and ranks equal to the Primordial, hence the title is fitting. Thus, the name "Primordial" is not exclusive to one honorable being.

After the invocation, inhale the three-colored clouds of *qi* through the nose, draw them into the mouth, and swallow. After thirty-two repetitions, the entire body becomes thoroughly permeated. After a long while, recite the scripture.

Offer incense and recite the scripture. For the first recitation, begin from the preface and proceed with visualization; in subsequent recitations, start directly from the title *Primordial Penetrating Mystery*. Each visualization should be repeated ten times for optimal effect. If urgent matters arise, one may briefly rise; if the interval is somewhat prolonged, one must return to the beginning, resume from the preface, and renew the visualization.

Shaowei notes: The text from *Primordial Penetrating Mystery* onward is the scripture proper.

*Primordial Boundless Deliverance of Beings, Supreme Wondrous Scripture: Annotated Edition, Scroll the First* concludes.
*Primordial Boundless Deliverance of Beings, Supreme Wondrous Scripture: Annotated Edition, Scroll the Second* begins.

Annotations by Qi Yan of the Northern Qi, Tang-era Xue Youxi, Li Shaowei, and Cheng Xuanying; compiled by Chen Jingyuan of the Song.

*Primordial Boundless Deliverance of Beings, Supreme Wondrous Scripture*

Youxi notes: The earlier title also includes *Supreme Penetrating Numinous Treasure*, while this one simply reads *Primordial Boundless Deliverance of Beings*. The preface is titled *Supreme* to clarify that it is the Supreme who prefaces the scripture. The former encompasses the entire corpus by rank, while the latter specifies the name of this single scripture. *Supreme Wondrous Scripture* shares the same meaning as the first annotation.
