Shaowei notes: The earlier section is the Dao Lord’s preface to the scripture, hence it begins with *Dao*; this is the Heavenly Venerable’s own discourse, so it bears *Primordial* as its title. The portion before *Naturally* is the Dao Lord’s brief preface; from *Chaos* onward is the Heavenly Venerable’s original text.

*Primordial Penetrating Mystery, Numinous Treasure Original Text*

Dong observes: *Primordial* means "first." It exists before heaven, hence "first." It also means "great," for it encompasses all without exception, hence "great." It also means "*qi*," for it permeates all that is subtle, hence "*qi*." It also means "none," for it is formless and shadowless, hence "none." It also means "numinous," for it can transform and change, hence "numinous." It also means "Dao," as the scripture says: "The Dao that can be spoken is not the constant Dao." It clarifies that the constant Dao is formless and cannot be named, so its nature is only briefly described. *Beginning* means "to congeal," for the *qi* congeals at the outset, hence "congeal." It also means "initial," for the jade script first opens, hence "initial." It also means "transformation," for it gives birth to heaven and earth, hence "transformation." It also means "origin," for it is the head of the myriad things, hence "origin." It also means "end," for it ends without ending, hence "end." The scripture says: "Nameless is the beginning of heaven and earth"; it also says: "The world has a beginning, which serves as the mother of the world"; and further: "When the beginning first established names," hence "the beginning gives birth to the One." The One is heaven. Heaven is born from the beginning, thus the beginning is also primordial. All returns to the primordial.

When the primordial was born, there was no heaven, no earth, no gods, no ghosts—only vast, indistinct chaos, without distinction. The primordial *qi* first congealed to form the jade script. Jade is the essence of the natural. When essence emerges, it radiates light to form heaven and earth, the sun and moon, and the stars. Thus, the numinous Primordial Venerable is transformed, revealing its spirituality. Thus, heaven and earth, the sun and moon, and the stars are transformed to nurture the myriad beings. After heaven, earth, and the myriad beings are born, they receive names, demonstrating the creative power of the Primordial. The name *Primordial* is given to show people the return to the beginning and end.

*Penetrating* means "illuminating." It shines boundlessly, hence "illuminating." It also means "pervading," for it reaches all without limit, hence "pervading." *Mystery* means "emptiness." Profound and empty, hence "emptiness." The primordial *qi* congeals to form the jade script within the empty mystery, pervading and illuminating the four directions, manifest in the Dragon Han, concealed in the Yan Kang, preceding the Crimson Clarity, shining in the Kai Huang, and extending to the Shang Huang.

*Numinous* is the general term for all sages. *Treasure* is what all sages cherish. *Scripture* means "patterned writing." When the jade script first emerged, its original form resembled a seal, with eight corners radiating light, its patterns and colors resplendent, penetratingly responding without end.

In heaven it is called *numinous*, on earth it is called *treasure*; in empty mystery it is numinous, when stored within it becomes treasure—hence the term *Numinous Treasure*. The Most High Dao Lord expounded its origin.

○ The *Lesser Mystery* states: The primordial subtle words, universally pervading the wondrous mystery, numinous script and precious writ, their sounds and rhythms forming patterned writing. The supreme wondrous beginning, ten revolutions to deliver humanity.

The East says: The *supreme* refers to the primordial *qi* first congealing into the green, yellow, and white *qi*, placed within the Three Palaces of the Upper Primordium. The first palace is named the *Mystic Capital Primordial Yang Seven Treasures Purple Tenuity Palace*. The *qi* of the incipient yang governs all perfected beings of the upper realm by nature, the Jade Void Lofty August Thearch, all celestial thearchs and kings, and the great divine sages of the upper realm—its officials number fifty-five million, five hundred fifty-five thousand, five hundred fifty-five myriad layers. The *qi* of the green yang, its officials and attendants likewise numbering fifty-five million, five hundred fifty-five thousand, five hundred fifty-five myriad, all congeal the natural green yang *qi* to form humans, their robes being green feathered flying garments. Within the palace lies the *Longevity-Extending Talisman*; when the *qi* of the eight directions suddenly arrives, it instantly forms a person. If the talisman is destroyed and the body burned, it immediately transforms into *qi* and disperses with the smoke.

The *Great Mystery Upper Treasury Purple Tenuity Palace* contains three treasuries: left, right, and central. The left treasury governs the Palace of Life, where the Great Yang Fire Officials examine; the right treasury governs the Palace of Death, where the Great Yin Water Officials examine; the central treasury governs the records of life, death, and transgressions, where the Wind Blade examines. Each of the three treasuries commands ninety million officials and attendants, collectively overseeing the twelve bureaus of life, death, transgressions, and blessings. The left palace is named the *Great Mystery Capital Primordial Yellow Great Ultimate Left Palace*, where the primordial yellow *qi* governs all perfected beings—those who have attained the Dao and those who have not, male and female cultivators of the true—recording their lives. Within this palace lies the *Summoning Numinous Talisman*. The right palace is named the *Great Mystery Cavern White Great Ultimate Right Palace*, where the celestial primordial cavernous white *qi* governs all perfected beings who have attained the Dao and those who have not, male and female cultivators of the true—recording their deliverance, immortal registers, transgression ledgers, and death records. Within the palace lies the *Clarifying the True Treasury*, its officials and attendants’ ranks and protocols identical to those of the Purple Tenuity Palace.

The Three Palaces of the Upper Primordium collectively contain three treasuries, each palace overseeing twelve bureaus, the three palaces together comprising thirty-six bureaus. All govern the upper realm of primordial yang and the midst of the great void, bearing natural designations and universally overseeing all perfected beings who have attained the Dao. On the Three Primordial Days, they assemble to review the yin and yang, water, fire, and Wind Blade treasuries, examining the thirty-six bureaus, the green and black ledgers, and present their reports to the Purple Tenuity, Supreme Tenuity left, right, and central palaces. These matters are fully expounded in the *Precepts of the Three Primordia*; here, only a corner is briefly presented.

In the era of Dragon Han, the jade script first emerged, the sun and moon first shone, heaven and earth became distinct, and the multitude of perfected beings took their places. The Primordial Beginning issued the Dharma to deliver humanity. Reciting the scripture ten times, circling the ten directions, it delivered an immeasurable number of beings. The Primordial Beginning thus composed the ten sections of wondrous scriptures, inscribing them with purple brush upon the *kongqing* forest. Revered by all sages as the ancestral origin of scriptures, it is called the *supreme wondrous beginning*.

○ The *Hidden Dweller* says: This was the time of scripture’s unfolding, hence the comprehensive exposition of its themes and purport. Reciting it ten times enables the deliverance of beings, so the Primordial Beginning recited it ten times to summon the ten directions, each time taking ten recitations as the method. Thus, the preceding preface states: Whoever recites this scripture ten times delivers all their ancestors across billions of kalpas—this is also the meaning of the Dharma Wheel revolving ten times.

○ The *Lesser Mystery* says: These verses, though few in words, encompass vast matters. They are called the *supreme true scripture*, the beginning of the wondrous Dao. Ten revolutions of the wheel broadly deliver celestial and human beings.

○ The *Mystic Splendor* says: Among the ranks of all scriptures, this is the foremost. *Wondrous beginning* refers to this scripture containing the method to deliver humanity, serving as the origin of all wonders—hence the name *wondrous beginning*. *Ten revolutions to deliver humanity* means the Heavenly Worthy’s recitation of the scripture to deliver beings follows a set number of repetitions: ten recitations make one revolution, one hundred recitations make ten revolutions.

The *hundred demons* conceal their *rhythms*, parting and uniting by nature.

The East says: The *hundred demons* are the Divine Empyrean Kings and the like. *Concealed* refers to the jade script; *rhythm* means modulation. The demon kings arise with the various *qi*, intermingling with the cavernous scriptures, concealing their rhythmic modulations to harmonize with the natural writ, forming the scriptures.

○ The *Hidden Dweller* says: This refers to the demon kings concealing their names and the secret scriptures of the three realms, their concealment and revelation, parting and uniting, all in accord with nature.

○ The *Lesser Mystery* says: At that time, none among celestial beings, humans, ghosts, or spirits failed to submit to transformation. Thus, the great demons of the three realms led their demonic hosts to conceal and refine their sounds and rhythms, coming to pay homage to the Primordial Beginning. Parting from the *qi* of flying mystery, uniting with the sounds of nature, stirred by the numinous wind, they all became songs and chants. The Most High treasured them, incorporating them into the scriptural text.

○ The *Mystic Splendor* says: This describes how the Heavenly Worthy’s recitation of the scripture moved the demonic hosts of the three realms to fly through the air, singing the concealed rhythms, all coming to pay homage. *Concealed rhythms* means these numinous scriptures are the natural, hidden sounds of the celestial perfected beings above—unknown to the world, hence called *concealed rhythms*. *Rhythm* refers to the formation of parallel lines into patterned writing; *sound* is the harmony of the five tones. Together, they are called *concealed rhythms*. *Natural* means these numinous scriptures are the wondrous *qi* of the celestial realms, stirred by the numinous wind to spontaneously form songs and chants, not artificially composed—hence called *natural*. *Parting and uniting* means the demon kings of the three realms each sing the natural wondrous *qi* of their heavens as songs and melodies—this is called *parting*. Their sounds intermingle with the cavernous scriptures, their principles harmonizing with the wondrousness of nature—hence called *uniting*. *Intermingling* means mixing; though their sounds and words are mixed, their principles accord with nature—hence called *parting and uniting by nature*.

Further explanation states: *Parting* means the Heavenly Worthy speaks, and the demon kings also speak, each expounding their own—hence called *parting*. Though their sounds differ, their principles accord with true wondrousness—hence called *parting and uniting by nature*.

The *Hun-dong Red Script* is the Supreme Perfected of the Non-None.
Dong says: *Hun* means great; *dong* means penetrating. The *Red Script* and *Red Writ* are the scriptures of the Great Cavern, illumining the Dragon Han and pervading the Yan-kang. When the Primordial Beginning opened the kalpa in the Cavern Yang Palace, it forged jade characters in fire, and the *qi* of Cavern Yang was red—thus named *Red Script*. It emerged to ordain humanity, refining the Perfected within the Perfected in the Jade Clarity realm—hence called the Supreme Perfected of the Non-None.

You-xi says: *Hun* is the name of primordial chaos; *dong* is the *qi* of Cavern Yang. *Red Script* refers to the true writ of red script. This true writ of red script, coeval with the inception of chaos, predates heaven and earth, congealing above the empty cavern and coalescing within the Great None. The *none* of the Great None is itself non-none; having no none, it is called the Non-None. Thus it is called the Supreme Perfected of the Non-None. The Primordial Beginning refined it with the *qi* of Cavern Yang and tempered it in the Flowing Fire Court; the *qi* of Cavern Yang was red—hence called *Red Writ*.

Shao-wei says: *Hun-dong* is the nine hundred million *qi* of the Highest Jade Emperor. The *qi* of the Jade Emperor, primordial and all-pervading, formed the true writ of red script, which at the time of the Non-None and the Not-Yet-Had was distributed across the five directions. The Primordial Beginning employed it to deliver humanity, all ascending to the rank of the Supreme Perfected.

The Primordial Beginning, the ancestral kalpa, gave birth to the myriad heavens.
Dong says: *Ancestral* means prior. Before the Primordial Beginning received its title, it had already given birth to heaven and earth. Yet the Dragon Han was remote and boundless; the kalpic cycle first unfolded, and heaven and earth were divided. All that preceded this cannot be recorded or known. Thus, observing the ancient allows one to know the present—ancient and present are no different.

You-xi says: The true writ of red script, at the inception of the ancestral kalpa, gave birth to the thirty-two heavens. The *ancestral kalpa* is the kalpa of Red Clarity.

Shao-wei says: *Ancestral* means beginning. The mysterious primordial *qi* at the dawn of the first kalpa suddenly brought forth transformation, generating the five hundred million heavens. As heaven and earth undergo one completion and one destruction, this is called one kalpa. The *first kalpa* refers to the world’s initial arising, before any completion or destruction. The *illumination of the three luminaries* is called the root of heaven.

Dong says: The *three luminaries* are the three lights. Once the three lights were bright, heaven and earth divided, the myriad things were born, and the spirits gained governance—thus becoming the eternal root of heaven. It also illumines the sun and moon and brightens the host of stars.

Shao-wei says: When the two modes took form, the three lights hung in radiance, all receiving the primordial *qi*—hence the root of heaven.

Xuan-ying says: *Luminaries* means light. This describes the formation of the heavens’ positions, whereupon the three lights arrayed their radiance, universally illuminating the cosmos—hence called *illumination*. All were formed by wondrous *qi*, thus the root of heaven.

Above, there is no further ancestor; only the Dao is its body.
Dong says: *Ancestor* means origin. Above, there is no origin; only the *qi* of the Dao coalesces into essence and thereafter forms its body.

You-xi says: Having equaled the things of primordial chaos and predated heaven and earth, it is said that above, there is no further ancestor. The substance of the true writ is the body of the Dao’s truth as writ—hence only the Dao is its body.

Xuan-ying says: This presents the true writ’s essence as the root of the myriad heavens, receiving the spontaneous wondrous *qi* of the Primordial Beginning and transforming into the Dharma-body of the Great Dao. The wondrous *qi* forms itself; there is no further prior ancestor. The *Scripture of Western Ascension* states: “The Void gives birth to spontaneity; spontaneity gives birth to the Dao.” Here, it says *above, there is no further ancestor*: the Dao takes the Void as its origin, spontaneity as its root, and the Dao as its body. Yet these three are all without form or appearance. Tracing their principle, one finds true emptiness. Within the true is essence, fundamentally without name. When the sage established the teachings, their traces could not lack an origin—thus the Void was taken as the Dao’s ancestor. In truth, the three bodies all converge in the One True, utterly without form or appearance, yet able to penetrate the myriad wonders—hence: *above, there is no further ancestor*. *Further* means distinct; there is no distinct prior ancestor.

The five writs open and expand, universally planting the divine spirits.
You-xi says: The *five writs* are the five chapters of the true writ, corresponding to the five directions and the five elders who record them. Having illuminated the three lights, they also opened and expanded the five chapters of the jade-character true writ, each planting the divine spirits.

Shao-wei says: The wondrous root forms itself, without further prior ancestor. All-encompassing and boundless, it is entirely the Dao’s body. The five chapters of the true writ open and expand their forms, universally generating heaven and earth and establishing the divine spirits.

Without writ, there is no light; without writ, there is no clarity.
Dong says: *Light* refers to the three lights; *clarity* means distinctness. If the jade characters do not emerge, the sun and moon have no light, and heaven and earth are indistinct.

Without writ, there is no establishment; without writ, there is no completion.
Dong says: *Establishment* means form; *completion* means generation. If the jade writ does not emerge, heaven and earth have no form, and the myriad things have no generation.

Without writ, there is no deliverance; without writ, there is no life.
Dong says: *Deliverance* means ascent; *life* means transformation. If the true writ does not emerge, the hun-souls have no ascent, and the myriad things have no transformation.

Shao-wei says: Without the true writ’s expansion, the sun and moon would not shine, the stars would not be bright, heaven and earth would not stand, the world would not be completed, the hidden souls would not be delivered, and the dry bones would not live.

Xuan-ying says: The three paths, eight difficulties, and five sufferings of the hidden souls—without this true writ, they cannot transcend the three realms. It also clarifies that those who cultivate and study without this true writ cannot attain perfection and enter the Dao.

This is the Great Brahma, the Heaven among Heavens.

Dong says: The *Great Brahma* refers to the primordial qi of the vast Wind-and-Marsh Brahma coalescing to form heaven. Suspended within the void, it rises in clarity, lofty and boundlessly floating, hanging yet never falling, above all other heavens—thus it is called the Heaven among Heavens. Yu-xi says: Since its creative power is vast and its transformative work all-encompassing, it is called the Great Brahma. *Brahma* is the Dao within the Dao. The Dao is the mysterious writ, hence it is called the Dao within the Dao, the Mystery within the Mystery. *Heaven* is the profound.

Shao-wei says: *Fan* means model. By its power, it illuminates the Three Radiant Ones and establishes the Five Writs—all through the Primordial Heavenly Worthy’s enactment of the great law, which abides above all heavens, hence it is called the Heaven among Heavens.

The Yu-luo Xiao Terrace, the Jade Mountain’s Upper Capital.

Dong says: *Yu* means flourishing; *luo* is the Great Luo. Above the Great Luo Heaven stands the Jade Capital Mountain, upon which rests the Seven Treasures’ Mystic Terrace. The terrace lies within a seven-jeweled city, and within the city stands the Jade Clarity Palace, where the Most High Jade Emperor governs. Yu-xi says: Above the Jade Clarity are nine-tiered terraces, reaching the utmost heights, merging with the Great Void—thus they shine resplendent above the flourishing Great Luo, the nine-tiered Xiao Terrace. The *Great Void* is the Great Luo. As the mountain is of jade, it is called the Jade Mountain. Above the mountain lies the capital, hence the Upper Capital; it is also named the Jade Capital, or Jade Clarity, all derived from jade. This is commonly called the Mystic Capital Jade Capital.

Shao-wei says: These ten lines all describe the splendor of the palaces within the Mystic Capital. The Jade Capital Mountain stands above all realms, hence the Upper Capital. The mountain bears a jade city, and within the city lies a terrace named the Xiao Terrace. The city gates, towers, and forests flourish in ordered array—all the domain where the Most High Jade Emperor governs.

Xuan-ying says: *Yu-luo* refers to the city gates, towers, and forests surrounding the Xiao Terrace, lush with radiant splendor, spreading in ordered brilliance—hence it is called Yu-luo.

Supreme beyond the supreme, the Great Luo Jade Clarity.

Dong says: The Great Luo Heaven stands above all heavens; the Purple Tenuity Palace rests above the Jade Clarity, resplendent within the Purple Void. When the luminous Dao is manifest, the Great Luo Heaven becomes serene and clear, its seven-jeweled trees each growing in one direction, covering one heaven; eight trees cover eight heavens, enveloping all heavens—thus it is called the Great Luo.

Yu-xi says: The Jade Capital ascends to the utmost limit, exhausting the boundless—only the Great Luo’s Jade Clarity remains. The *Great Luo* is the Void’s radiance; the *Jade Clarity* is its palaces.

Shao-wei says: The realm of the Great Luo Jade Clarity reaches the utmost heights and distances, with nothing above it to encompass all heavens—hence it is said: above the Great Luo, dustless and vast, lies the Dao’s realm of non-action.

Xuan-ying says: The *Original Form Sutra* states: above the Great Luo, there is no color, no dust—this is the supreme.

Vast and distant, the kalpa’s measure, as if absent, as if present.

Dong says: *Vast and distant* describes its height. One *kalpa* is like a colossal stone, four hundred leagues in each direction; or like an empty city, four hundred leagues in each direction, equal in height and breadth, filled with mustard seeds. Every hundred years, a heavenly being removes one mustard seed. When the stone is worn away by a silk robe and the mustard seeds are exhausted, this is called one kalpa. The seven-foot *ren* blade exists or does not exist. The seven-jeweled mystic terrace stands as high as countless *ren* of mustard seeds—this is the Terrace of Kalpa Measures, seen in the floating clouds above. The seven-jeweled terrace is unseen even by earthbound immortals, let alone mortals! Those who behold it say it exists; those who do not say it is absent—hence it is said to be as if absent, as if present.

Yu-xi says: *Ren* is a measure. Ancient script had few characters, so *ren* was used for *ren*. Heavenly perfected ones measure *ren* by kalpas, while mortals measure *ren* by feet—this is the nine-tiered terrace of Jade Clarity, also called the Terrace of Kalpa Measures. Since it is vast, distant, and mysteriously transformed without fixed form, it is said to be as if absent, as if present—not a definite appearance. Though it has form, it lacks substance; the true essence’s transformations arise naturally.

Shao-wei says: According to the *True One’s Natural Scripture*, the Jade Mountain is also called the Terrace of Kalpa Measures. Its height is measured like the kalpas, hence the term *kalpa-ren*. It has form yet does not obstruct, as if present, as if absent.

The Three Flowers depart from the Three Conveniences, the Great Existence’s wondrous court.

Dong says: The *Three Flowers* refer to the names of the gates of the Supreme Ultimate Palace’s Azure Flower Gate. The *Three Conveniences* are the names of the Three Realms’ gates. The Three Flowers lie above the Three Realms, where Brahma-heaven’s divine beings soar above the Supreme Ultimate, singing boundless cavernous hymns. The qi of the numinous wind brushes and lifts the melodies of the cavernous hymns. Jade Maidens of Great Harmony harmonize the divine beings’ songs at the Flower Capital’s gates, celebrating the Great Existence before the Primordial Beginning and rejoicing in the multitude of perfected ones within the wondrous court. Not departing from the Three Realms, it is called *departing from the Conveniences*.

Yu-xi says: To enter the feasting halls of the Three Clarities’ palaces, one must first depart from the Three Conveniences’ gates—the gates of the Three Realms. The *Three Flowers Palace* is the Jade Clarity’s Three Origins Palace. The Upper Origin’s Jade Flower, the Middle Origin’s Golden Flower, and the Lower Origin’s Nine Flowers are all the abodes of the Three Origins’ August Lords of the Dao. The *Great Existence* is the Great Dao, its meaning akin to the Great Mass, its principle equal to all things. Since the Three Flowers Palace is the abode of the Heavenly Worthy of the Great Dao, it is called the Great Existence’s wondrous court.

Golden gates and jade chambers, arrayed in purity and clarity.

Dong says: Within heaven lie golden gates and jade chambers, which mark the boundaries of the Three Conveniences’ gates.

Verdant and towering, vast as the Great Net. Above stand the *Qian* Forests’ trees, their canopies shading the Eastern Florescence Palace. The leaves of the *Qian* Forests bear the script of the Great Cavern, inscribed in purple on jade, resplendent in the Upper Clarity. *Jingying* is the inner name of the Supervising Deity of the Capital, who governs the Purple Tenuity Palace. Within its winding chambers below grows the Fusang tree, above flourish the *Qian* Forests’ groves. Azure fowl cry beneath their boughs, blue mists and emerald vapors crown their peaks. Divine winds stir the fragrant grasses of reversal, setting the hundred reeds of the Mulberry Grove to music. When the divine wind stirs once, the void births the sound of Cavern Script.

Dong says: The realm of Jade Clarity is walled in yellow gold and roofed in white jade. Its golden gates stand tall and radiant, arrayed about the white jade chambers, which are pure, solemn, and lustrous as crystal.

Shaowei says: Encircling the Three Conveniences’ halls and tracing the Great Existence’s palace, one finds golden gates, jade chambers, *Qian* Forests, purple trees—all verdant, towering, and arrayed in pristine clarity.

Xuanying says: *Que* means gate. This describes the wondrous adornments within the Jade Capital’s walls: gates wrought of amassed gold, chambers built of heaped jade, encircling the Great Existence’s palace and the Three Conveniences’ halls. Planted throughout stand the *Qian* Forests and purple trees, verdant and towering, pure and crystalline. Dwelling therein is surpassingly sublime—hence *jingying*.

The Great Conduct’s *fanqi* pervades the ten directions.

Dong says: The Great Conduct is the Heavenly Origin’s guiding principle. It binds the eight poles, unifying the Great Brahma’s *qi*, and illumines the Dragon Han’s gates. The Dragon Han unfolds by reckoning, while the Crimson Clarity awaits its turn to spread the celestial bodies. Once the Crimson Clarity opens, the thirty-two heavens all bear divine spirits, and the Middle Origin’s second-rank Earth Officials are established. The *qi* of the Primordial Cavern’s mixed numina, the essence of congealed yellow, establishes the Middle Origin’s Three Offices. The first palace is named the Cavern Numen’s Pure Void Palace, which governs the Five Thearchs, the Five Marchmounts, all Perfected Ones, and the earthly immortals who have attained the Dao. Another name is the Luminous Dawn’s Martial Accomplishment Palace, which houses the left, right, and central bureaus. The left bureau is called the Enduring Transgression Luminous Dawn Bureau, governing the life offices and the Great Yang Fire Officials’ examinations. The right bureau is called the Execration-Cutting Yin Heaven Bureau, governing the death offices and the Great Yin Water Officials’ examinations. The central bureau is called the Seven Wrongs’ Tranquil Illumination Bureau, governing the records of life-and-death transgressions and the trials of the Wind Blade. Each bureau commands fifty million officials, overseeing fourteen departments of life, death, transgression, and fortune. They all reside within the hollows of mountains and caverns, sustained by the Great Brahma’s *qi*.

Youxi says: The Jade Clarity’s true Dao’s *fanqi* flows through the ten directions’ realms and circulates through all the heavens’ domains.

Shaowei says: Encompassing the five hundred million heavens and blending the eight spheres’ warp and weft, it descends to the nine earths’ depths and ascends to the Great Net’s bounds. Everywhere the *fanqi* flows ceaselessly, so that the myriad worlds, though lofty and floating, remain suspended without falling. Its form resembles wind yet is not wind, resembles water yet is not water. It upholds and sustains as if sentient and trustworthy. Within it dwells the spirit of delivering people from death.

Dong says: The spirit who delivers people and grants rebirth is called the Flying Life Scholar, who recites the Cavern Script. All the heavens rejoice, and the Flying Life opens the gate of deathlessness, streaming the *qi* of eternal life to refine the three *hun*. When the three *hun* spirits are refined, the Eight Effulgences abide within. Once the Eight Effulgences are complete and guard the body, they together uplift the person to ascend the nine-tiered terrace, wander amid the *Qian* Forests, and ascend to the Mystery Capital’s palace.

Youxi says: This refers to the spirit in the ten directions’ heavens who oversees the deliverance of the world from death—not that the spirit itself is deathless.

Within it dwells the Southern Culmen’s Lord of Eternal Life.

Dong says: The Southern Culmen is the Perfected of the Southern Culmen. The Middle Origin’s second rank includes the left palace, named the Cavern Yang Palace, also called the Ancestral Heaven Palace, which governs the Nine Lands’ Earth Thearchs and the spirits of the four corners and eight poles. The *qi* of mixed yellow therein, the Central Earth Bureau, and the earthly officials examine ninety-nine billion, nine hundred ninety-nine million, nine hundred ninety-nine thousand souls—all the spirits of the deceased who have meritorious deeds, who receive deliverance and fill their ranks. This palace houses the left, right, and central bureaus. The left bureau is called the Veracious Affairs Bureau, the right bureau the Ancestral Numen Bureau, and the central bureau the Numinous As-If-Divine Bureau. The three bureaus’ examining officials follow the above method, governing the fourteen departments of life and death. The Middle Origin’s second rank includes the right palace, named the Northern Feng Palace, also called the Yin Heaven Palace, which governs all the earthly spirits. It houses the left, right, and central bureaus. The left bureau is called the Linked Bay’s Winding Springs Bureau, the right bureau the Grand Execution’s Nine Darks Bureau, and the central bureau the Transgression *Qi*’s Celestial Pool Bureau. They govern life and death as the Middle Origin’s second rank. The earthly Three Offices’ left, right, and central bureaus each have three bureaus, overseeing fourteen departments, all residing within the hollows of mountains and caverns—all naturally designated titles. On the eight seasonal days, the Five Marchmounts’ earthly gods, the spirits of the four corners and eight poles, the immortals, and the Perfected Ones descend to the Pure Numen’s Cavern Yang and Northern Feng Palaces to assemble and review the earthly records of life and death, merit and transgression, fortune and misfortune. When all the officials arrive, the three palaces’ nine bureaus and forty-two departments summon their subordinates to examine life and death. Blue and black registers list the three palaces’ affairs. The Perfected of the Southern Culmen governs the Cavern Yang Palace, below which lies the Flowing Fire’s Court. Those who attain the Dao all proceed to the Flowing Fire’s Court to receive refinement and become Perfected, then enter the Cavern Yang Palace among the eternally living. Within the palace dwells the Lord of Delivering Destiny, named Xu Yuanyuan. Those who enter the Southern Palace’s Xu Yuanyuan are refined and have their decayed bones delivered.

Youxi says: The south governs life, hence the Southern Culmen’s additional title as the overseer of eternal life.

Shaowei says: The Flowing Fire’s Court spans eight hundred thousand li. Within it resides the Great Divine Marshal of Delivering the World. Dong says: In the Southern Palace dwells the Great Divine Marshal of Delivering the World, where the Flying Heavenly Divine Kings of the ten directions all govern within the palace. Youxi says: The Great Divine Marshal oversees the registers of delivering the world. *Simā* is an official rank.

Shaowei says: The Southern Palace also has a Marshal of Delivering the World, as well as a Great Divine One of Delivering the World, both governing within the palace, attaining eternal life without death. Within it dwells the Venerable Lord Han of Cherishing Life. Dong says: The Lord of Cherishing Life, whose taboo name is You, governs within the Southern Upper Palace. Lord Han oversees life and registers, ruling the Nine Dark Hells of Fengdu. For those who have accumulated virtuous merit, the Great Sage opens the Gate of the Dark Night, and Fengdu delivers them from the Eight Perils’ realm. Their seven ancestors thus return, and their dark souls are illuminated. The Supreme Emperor nurtures and fosters the newly born spirits, while the Registrar calculates their deliverance in the Southern Palace.

Youxi says: There is also the Venerable Lord Han who oversees the registers of eternal life, his duties akin to those of the Southern Culmen. Among the divine, he is called *Zhangren* (Venerable Elder). *Han Jun* is the title of his official post. Shaowei says: Lord Han is the Registrar of Immortal Registers beneath the Supreme Emperor’s threshold, delivering people in the Southern Palace. Xuanying says: *Zhangren* is a term of respect for elders. *Hao* means "to delight in." This clarifies that within the Southern Palace there is also a Lord who delights in people’s eternal life without death, recording their virtuous merit and delivering them from the suffering of the Three Realms.

Within it dwell the Southern Upper Registrars of Life and Records. Dong says: The Southern Upper Palace is its name. The Nine Radiance Perfected governs within it, presiding over the karmic retribution of dead souls in the Nine Dark Hells. The Registrar of Life oversees the spirit of lifespan, while the Registrar of Records oversees the recording of merits. Both are officials of the Southern Supreme Emperor, constantly reviewing the names of those who cultivate immortality. As mentioned earlier, among the officials of the Mysterious Capital, those who know the eight-character resonance of deliverance—when the time of calamity and kalpa converges—the Registrar of Life dispatches the Bird Mother to welcome them with a phoenix chariot, ascending to the Kunlun wastes.

Xuanying says: The Southern Upper Palace is another name for the Cavern Yang Palace. It extends lifespan and increases destiny. Dong says: *Yan* means "to extend," and *suan* means "to record." The Mother of the Nine Numinous Ones governs the Abyss of Fusang and Tanggu in the Eastern Sea, constantly overseeing the turning of the Earth’s Mechanism, with primordial *qi* ascending to respond to the Celestial Pass. When the Celestial Pass turns and the Earth’s Mechanism moves through one revolution of the heavens, the waters surge three thousand three hundred times. The Nine Seas merge, and the Mother of Earth emerges above the Eastern Sea to summon the Bird Mother, extending the kalpa’s convergence before the Emperor. She prolongs lifespan and increases its record, delivering those who cultivate immortality.

The Venerable Divine One of Delivering from Calamity. Dong says: Within the Southern Upper Palace dwells the Venerable Divine One of Prolonging Life and Extending Years, the Divine One of Delivering from Calamity, the Supreme Emperor’s Lord. His taboo name is Yuchang. He rides a chariot of elephant wheels, traversing the Nine Mysterious Gates, turning the Nine Mechanisms’ measures to respond to the kalpa’s convergence and the end of heaven’s revolution. When the Sun Child halts its light, he delivers those who cultivate immortality, bathing them in the essence of the Water Mother and guiding them with the *qi* of Great Harmony. He delivers them from calamity and refines the corpses of the Long Night.

Youxi says: There are also the two Venerable Divine Ones of the Southern Registrars of Life and Records. The Venerable Divine Registrar of Life oversees extending lifespan and increasing destiny, while the Venerable Divine Registrar of Records oversees transcending calamities and delivering from peril. They revive skeletons and raise the dead, delivering countless people. Dong says: The Immeasurable One is the primordial spirit of the great multitude, governing the hosts of Flying Heavenly Beings. Within the Heaven of Delight, there are immeasurable ranks of great sages, all of whom receive their measure and ascend, delivering the dead skeletons, receiving *qi*, and being reborn as humans.

Youxi says: Those who extend lifespan, increase destiny, transcend calamities, deliver from peril, revive the forms of the dead, and restore the corpses of the deceased all rely on the two Lords of Life and Records. Thus, it is said they deliver countless people. Shaowei says: All those Perfected Officials, each governing their duties, can revive skeletons and restore life, raise the dead and complete rebirth. As kalpas repeatedly converge, they deliver countless people. Xuanying says: These two lines summarize the preceding text. From "Within it dwells the Marshal of Delivering the World" to all these Perfected Officials, they can revive skeletons and raise the dead, delivering living beings. *Bones become skeletons; skeletons are forms.* They can cause the dead skeletons and white bones to rise again and become human. *Raising the dead* refers to those newly deceased, enabling them to live again. *Delivering countless people* means that in kalpa after kalpa, they deliver people to attain the Dao, beyond calculation. Thus, it is called delivering countless people. This illustrates how the Primordial Beginning extends compassion, connecting life and death, establishing golden palaces and jade halls. All those Perfected Officials illuminate the Three Realms, broadly delivering the Nine Heavens. People, whether living or dead, receive blessings; all things, whether moving or still, bear gratitude. In kalpa after kalpa, they attain eternal life and long vision.

Today, the records are reviewed, and the various heavens descend to the imperial terrace. Dong says: *Reviewing records* means examining the records of life and death. *Descending to the imperial terrace* means holding a banquet. The Jade Emperor, within the Southern Prosperity Palace, reviews and delivers the registers of life and death, universally granting amnesty. Youxi says: *Today’s review of records* refers to assessing the names of those who uphold recitations and establish meritorious conduct, whose records should be elevated and delivered. Thus, the immeasurable divine Perfected of the ten directions ride their carriages and wield their brushes, ascending before the Emperor.

Shaowei says: *Today* refers to the day when the Crimson Clarity unfolds the chart. *Reviewing records* means examining the registers of life and death. On the day of reviewing records, one may refer to it as "today." At this time, the Primordial Heavenly Venerable reviews the registers of life and death, and the sagely hosts of the various heavens all descend to the imperial terrace to pay court.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Eastern Infinite. Dong says: The Most High spoke of the Mysterious Capital’s Jade Capital Mountain, where the eight directions’ various heavens contain three thousand great thousand-worlds. The Eastern Infinite Heavens of the Eastern Direction are the Great Thousand World of Accepting Goodness in the Peaceful Hall Village.

Youxī says: As stated in the preceding preface: when the scripture is recited once, the great deities of the Eastern Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Southern Infinite.
Dong says: The Southern Infinite Heavens of the Southern Direction are the Great Thousand World of Abandoning Worthies in the Wondrous Pear City.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited twice, the great deities of the Southern Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Western Infinite.
Dong says: The Western Infinite Heavens of the Western Direction are the Great Thousand World of Universal Practice in the Blessed Hall Continent.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited thrice, the great deities of the Western Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Northern Infinite.
Dong says: The Northern Infinite Heavens of the Northern Direction are the Great Thousand World of Cool Purity in the Fragrant Sandalwood Wilds.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited four times, the great deities of the Northern Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Northeastern Infinite.
Dong says: The Northeastern Infinite Heavens of the Northeastern Direction are the Great Thousand World of Eternal Peace in the Blessed Assembly Capital.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited five times, the great deities of the Northeastern Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Southeastern Infinite.
Dong says: The Southeastern Infinite Heavens of the Southeastern Direction are the Great Thousand World of Employing Worthies in the Primordial Blessed Field.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited six times, the great deities of the Southeastern Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Southwestern Infinite.
Dong says: The Southwestern Infinite Heavens of the Southwestern Direction are the Great Thousand World of Benevolent Stillness in the Extended Blessing Village.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited seven times, the great deities of the Southwestern Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Northwestern Infinite.
Dong says: The Northwestern Infinite Heavens of the Northwestern Direction are the Great Thousand World of Extending Worthies in the Blessed Virtue Wilds.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited eight times, the great deities of the Northwestern Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Upper Infinite.
Dong says: The Upper Infinite Heavens of the Upper Direction are within the Purple Tenuity of the Jade Treasury of the Mysterious Capital’s peakless summit, where the boundless hosts of Flying Heavenly Divine Kings reside.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited nine times, the great deities of the Upper Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Deliverer of People, the Great Sage of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine King of the Lower Infinite.
Dong says: The Lower Infinite Heavens of the Lower Direction are among the Five Marchmounts and Five Thearchs, within the Northern Fengdu of the Cavernous Yang and Pure Numinosity, and the various bureaus therein.

Youxī says: When the scripture is recited ten times, the great deities of the Lower Direction arrive floating through the air.

The Immeasurable Great Deities, the Great Sages of Eternal Life, the Flying Heavenly Divine Kings of the Ten Directions’ Perfected Realized Ones.
Dong says: In the Great Veil Heavens of the Ten Directions, there is the Jade Capital Mountain, which has eight directions; above and below together make ten directions. Each contains infinite and boundless Flying Heavenly Divine Kings, Lords of Eternal Life and Deliverance, Immeasurable Great Deities, and boundless hosts, all arriving before the Emperor.

Youxī says: These Perfected Deities of the Ten Directions all preside over and oversee the affairs of attaining the Dao, achieving realization, eternal life, and deliverance—hence they are called the Great Sages of Eternal Life and Immeasurable Deliverers of People.

All ride upon flying clouds, crimson chariots, green carriages, feathered canopies, and jade wheels.
Dong says: Flying clouds are of three kinds: white clouds, crimson clouds, and green clouds.

Feathers are pennants; canopies are coverings; *qiong* is jade. The Great Sages of the Ten Directions and the Flying Heavenly Divine Kings each ride upon crimson-cloud chariots and azure-cloud carriages, with Vermilion Birds and phoenixes as the canopies for their chariots and carriages, and seven-jeweled wheel hubs.

Xuan Ying says: Crimson is the rosy glow of dawn, and green is the azure *qi* of the heavens. This clarifies that when the Great Sages of the Ten Directions come to pay homage to the Primordial Beginning, they all form the Supreme Three Pure flying clouds, crimson dawn clouds, and azure celestial clouds into their vehicles—hence the terms "crimson chariots" and "green carriages." They harness Vermilion Phoenixes and five-colored Dark Dragons.

Dong says: *Can* means "to intermingle." They intermingle their harnesses with Vermilion Birds, phoenixes, five-colored dragons, White Tigers, and Dark Warriors.

Youxī says: Feathered canopies shade the chariots and carriages above, while flying clouds race beneath the wheel hubs. Vermilion Phoenixes intermingle with the carriages, and Dark Dragons draw the chariots. Thus, phoenix carriages, cloud chariots, and cloud-*qi* advance in tandem. Feathered canopies are made from the feathers of immortal birds and numinous fowl. Jade wheels are crafted from precious jades such as *gui*, *bi*, *wan*, and *yan*.

Xuan Ying says: Dragons come in five colors, yet they are called "Dark" because *xuan* signifies Heaven—referring to Heavenly Dragons. It is also said that *xuan* is the master of all colors, hence it is specifically mentioned to clarify this.

They erect nine-colored standards and ten *jue*-spirit banners.

Dong says: *Jie* are canopies; *fan* are ornate banners. The nine colors are blue-green, crimson, white, yellow, black, green, red, purple, and deep blue. Perfected Ones hold nine-colored feathered standards, while Jade Maidens grasp ten *jue*-spirit banners.

Youxī says: The Perfected Ones all erect three, seven, or nine-colored standards—purple-feathered standards and spirit-banner standards—interspersed with ten colors, each color forming one *jue*, hence the term "ten *jue*." The standards are held before the banners, grasped in both hands to lead the way.

Shaowei says: The Great Sages of the Ten Directions all ride upon Three Pure flying clouds and crimson-cloud carriages, with phoenix-feathered canopies and jade wheels. *Can* means "to intermingle," and they further intermingle their harnesses with Vermilion Phoenixes and Dark Dragons, their radiance displaying five colors. Jade Maidens erect nine-light standards, while Perfected Ones hold ten *jue*-spirit banners. Their regalia and majestic decor are uniform across all directions.

Xuan Ying says: The ten *jue*-spirit banners are made by cutting horizontal strips of ten-colored silk, each strip severed to form a *jue*, then interspersed and sewn together. When the strips are continuous, ten segments form ten *jue*. They are affixed to the tops of poles and called banners. *Fan* (banners) derive their name from "turning," turning misfortune into fortune. Holding standards ensures that punishments are measured, and no excessive penalties are meted out. Grasping banners enables repentance and cultivation of the Dao, transforming evil into good. The standards and banners erected by the Great Sages enlighten the foolish and deluded. Perfected Ones hold the banners, while Jade Maidens grasp the standards. The rank and status of these insignia follow the regulations, with distinctions in height. For instance, Perfected Ones of the Highest Clarity erect purple-feathered standards, while other ranks are detailed in the ritual codes—this will not be elaborated here.

Ahead, nine phoenixes whistle in unison; behind, eight *luan*-birds sing in harmony.

Dong says: Males are called phoenixes, females *luan*-birds; crimson and five-colored ones are *luan*-birds. Nine divisions of phoenixes lead the way, while eight divisions of *luan*-birds follow. At the first whistle of the dawn, nine phoenixes sing in unison. When the Western Numinous Perfected Ones play the nine-phoenix flutes, the eight *luan*-birds harmonize in response.

Youxī says: Ahead, whistling and singing are met with phoenixes joining in unison; behind, the playing of flutes and pipes is answered by eight *luan*-birds singing in harmony.

Xuan Ying says: The front division belongs to *yang*, and *yang* numbers are odd, hence nine. The rear division belongs to *yin*, and *yin* numbers are even, hence eight.

Lions and white cranes whistle and sing in harmonious resonance.

Dong says: *Yongyong* describes harmonious singing. Phoenixes sing and *luan*-birds call, with all sounds arising together.

Youxī says: Lions roar like tigers, and white cranes sing like phoenixes. Their harmonious resonance blends two sounds in perfect accord.

Shaowei says: This is the music of Heavenly Harmony. The front division whistles and sings, and nine phoenixes join in unison; the rear division plays flowing melodies, and eight *luan*-birds sing in harmony. The *Scripture of Cavernous Divinity* states: "In the left palace of Heavenly Unity, there are instruments of Heavenly Harmony. On the *zi* day, Jade Maidens play the *sheng* and *yu*; on the *chou* day, Jade Maidens whistle and sing; on the *yin* day, Jade Maidens play the *se*; on the *mao* day, Jade Maidens strike the *zhu*; on the *chen* day, Jade Maidens play the *qin*; on the *si* day, Jade Maidens ring bells and strike chimes; on the *wu* day, Jade Maidens play the flute; on the *wei* day, Jade Maidens play the *jia*; on the *shen* day, Jade Maidens sing the nine-tone songs; on the *you* day, Jade Maidens perform the six-variation songs; on the *xu* day, Jade Maidens imitate the cries of a hundred beasts; on the *hai* day, Jade Maidens compose new celestial melodies." Heavenly Harmony is the name of a musical instrument. Its name is the same as those in the world, but its sound differs from the vulgar. Worldly music is mournful and hastens life, while celestial music is harmonious and prolongs life.

Xuan Ying says: This describes lions and white cranes following the procession. When celestial music begins, a hundred beasts dance in unison, hence their voices join in harmonious song.

The Five Elders clear the path, and hosts of immortals flank the shafts.

Dong says: The Five Elders are the Five Emperors. *Qi* means "to open," and *tu* means "path." *Yi* means "to attend," and *yuan* refers to the carriage shafts. When the boundless Flying Heavenly Divine Kings of the Ten Directions arrive at the Azure Beginning Heaven, the Five Emperors clear the path, and hosts of immortals attend and guide them.

Youxī says: The Five Elders clear the path ahead, while hosts of immortals attend to the shafts on either side. The Five Elders are the Five Elderly Emperor Lords, who preside over the Five Chapters of the Perfected Writ.

Shaowei says: The Five Elders are the Five Emperors. The exalted positions of the Great Sages of the Ten Directions move the Five Emperors to lead the way, with hosts of immortals harnessing the five talismans. The *Scripture of Fundamental Conduct* states: "In the east, the Azure Numinous Beginning Elder of the Treasure-Fragrant Flower Forest is called the Azure Emperor. His surname is *He*, his taboo name is *Kai*, and his style is *Lingwei Yang*. He favors the color azure, rides a Dark Dragon, raises a green banner, and is accompanied by a retinue of ninety myriad spirits. He harmonizes the spring *qi* and generates the myriad things."

In the south, the Vermilion Numinous True Elder of the Brahma-Treasure Flourishing Yang is called the Vermilion Emperor. His surname is *Dongfu*, his taboo name is *Jiyan*, and his style is *Chibiao Nu*. He favors the color vermilion, rides a Red Dragon, raises a crimson banner, and is accompanied by a retinue of thirty myriad spirits. He harmonizes the summer *qi* and nurtures the myriad things.

At the center, the Jade-Treasure Primordial Numinous Elder is called the Yellow Emperor. His surname is *Tongban*, his taboo name is *Yuanshi*, and his style is *Han Shuniu*. He favors the color yellow, rides a Yellow Dragon, raises a yellow banner, and is accompanied by a retinue of twelve myriad spirits. He harmonizes the *qi* of earth and upholds the Nine Heavens.

In the west, the August Numinous Elder of the Seven-Treasure Golden Gate is called the White Emperor. His surname is *Shangjin*, his taboo name is *Changkai*, and his style is *Yaopo Bao*. He favors the color white, rides a White Dragon, raises a plain banner, and is accompanied by a retinue of seventy myriad spirits. He harmonizes the autumn *qi* and ripens the myriad things.

In the north, the Mysterious Elder of the Profound Yin, Solitary Darkness, and Five Numinosities is called the Black Emperor. His surname is *Heijie*, his taboo name is *Linghui*, and his style is *Yin Houju*. He favors the color black, rides a Black Dragon, raises a dark banner, and is accompanied by a retinue of fifty myriad spirits. He harmonizes the winter *qi* and stores the myriad things.

The Five Elderly Emperor Lords are all celestial perfected spirits of spontaneous origin, hence called the Primordial Beginning. The Five Elders are not formed through later study; the perfected receive their mandates directly, each governing one direction. When great kalpas complete their cycles, their positions still shift.

A hundred million chariots and ten thousand riders arrive floating through the void. The East says: "A hundred million is ten thousand myriad." The chariots are phoenix carriages, the riders are dragon-unicorns. Flying immortals together ride dragon-drawn hosts without number, their phoenix carriages and feathered canopies floating through the void to arrive.

The Recluse says: "A hundred million chariots and ten thousand riders—this clarifies their multitude. Floating through the void, they do not tread upon the earth."

Their radiance tilts, their chariots turn back, overseeing the perfected and delivering the living. The East says: "Tilting is like a canopy. Radiance is the sun. Delivering the living refers to the perfected one, whose style is *Fu Xi*, who constantly oversees the registers of the Nine Dark Regions and the causes of good and evil. Those who are good receive his deliverance; those who are evil face the roots of their transgressions."

At that time, the Great Sages of the Ten Directions tilt the heavens to come, descending to shield the sun’s brilliance. They turn their chariots back to the realms of the various heavens, tilting their radiance before the Supreme Emperor, overseeing those adepts who have cultivated and recited to attain perfection, and delivering the souls of ancestors who are due to be reborn.

The Mysterious Splendor says: "Tilting means moving. Radiance refers to the splendor of chariots, carriages, and vestments. Turning back the chariots means that once the hosts of sages have received the Heavenly Worthy’s mandate, they then tilt their luminous regalia, turn their chariots, and each returns to their own realm, overseeing the hosts of perfected and delivering those who have attained immortality. Thus it is called overseeing the perfected and delivering the living."

The Prime Ministers of the Various Heavens reside in the Southern Prosperity Upper Palace. The East says: "The Prime Ministers are the divine lords of the Great Luo Heaven. The Upper Palace is the Vermilion Numinous Palace. The Prime Ministers serve as guests for those who receive deliverance and rebirth, determining their destinies in the Vermilion Palace and excising the roots of their transgressions in the Three Bureaus."

The Recluse says: "The Nine Palaces have the positions of the Two Perfected Upper Ministers, who assist in the affairs of the various heavens. Thus they reside in the Southern Prosperity Upper Palace, which is the south of the Nine Palaces, within the Heaven of Crimson Clarity and Harmonious Yang."

Han presides over the registers. The East says: "Han is the Controller of Destiny."

Those who are destined for deliverance—it is the Controller of Destiny who, holding the register of life-calculations, conducts their refinement and deliverance in the Southern Palace, thereby enabling them to undergo the alchemical refinement and attain deliverance.

The Great Divine Overseer of Birth.
The East says: "The Great Divine Overseer of Birth presides over the Palace of the Endless Night, examining the ledgers of Dao-cultivators and delivering the souls of the Nine Dark Realms. The Great Divine Ones are the Flying Heavenly Divine Kings of the Ten Directions. They ever abide above the Flying Mystery, reciting the scriptures of the Cavernous Mystery, and by means of the spontaneous qi, they rescue and deliver those who cultivate the Dao."

The Recluse says: "The Han Controller is the same as the Controller of the former Han Lord. The 'Main Register' refers to the register that oversees and monitors longevity, hence it is called the Great Divine Overseer of Birth. Holding the registers and grasping the ledgers, they assemble together before the Emperor."

The East says: "The Great Divine Ones of the Ten Directions each oversee their respective registers, holding the ledgers as they present themselves before the Jade Emperor. The Jade Emperor’s tabooed name is Kuoyi, and he governs within the Mysterious Terrace of the Jade Capital. Born together with the Primordial Beginning, he is the model of the Mysterious Origin, opening the gate of extinction and deliverance to teach those who study immortality."

The Recluse says: "The Perfected Ones of the Ten Directions, together with the Prime Ministers of the Various Heavens and the Great Divine Overseer of Birth, all carry the registers of deliverance calculations and assemble before the Emperor to promote and elevate the worthy."

The Lesser Mystery says: "The Han Controller is the registrar under the Main Register Office, responsible for the ledgers of human destinies, hence called the Main Register. The Great Divine Overseer of Birth is the Perfected One of Rebirth, named Fu Xi, who presides over the Palace of the Endless Night and delivers the souls of the Nine Dark Realms. At that time, the lords of the various heavens, each leading their prime ministers, assemble before Your Majesty to examine and assess life and death."

The Emperor is the Heavenly Worthy speaking of himself. One of the Heavenly Worthy’s titles is Jade Emperor. According to the *Scripture of the Dragon’s Ascent*, the Primordial Beginning has ten titles: the Spontaneous, the Boundless, the Great Dao, the Utmost Perfected, the Supreme, the Venerable Lord, the August Sovereign, the Heavenly Worthy, the Jade Emperor, and the August Thearch. As each is to be delivered, the heavens are strictly examined.

The East says: "If a scholar can clearly enunciate the eight-character incantation, then the Divine Lords will open the Gate of Eternal Light, and the souls of the Ten Directions will all attain deliverance, entering the Gate of Rebirth. Ascending to the Terrace of the Jade Capital, they will rejoice in the Purple Ultimate Palace. Within it, the Divine Infant sings the hymn of the Immeasurable, and immediately they regain their forms in the Chamber of Triple Refinement, their bodies receiving the spontaneous qi, rejoicing in boundless longevity."

The Recluse says: "Wherever there are those who recite and cultivate, those who are destined for deliverance are assessed according to the ledgers of the various heavens, their merits tallied and their records complete."

The Lesser Mystery says: "All are delivered according to the weight of their merits and the circumstances of their karmic conditions. The heavens are strictly examined, with nothing omitted or lost. A universal proclamation is made to the Three Realms and the Boundless Divine Regions."

The East says: "The Three Realms are the Realm of Desire, the Realm of Form, and the Formless Realm. The Boundless refers to the boundless worlds of the Ten Directions. A universal proclamation is made to the gods of the Ten Directions, the boundless and infinite, so that all may know and hear."

The Recluse says: "A decree is issued to the demon kings of the Three Realms and the Five Emperors, extending even to the boundless and infinite divine domains, ensuring that no hidden place remains uninformed."

The Lesser Mystery says: "This is the Jade Emperor’s proclamation. The Three Realms consist of the six heavens of the Realm of Desire, the eighteen heavens of the Realm of Form, and the four heavens of the Formless Realm. The divine regions are without limit, hence called the Boundless Divine Regions. The Subterranean Palace of the Yellow Springs and the Northern Capital of Fengdu."

The East says: "The Northern Capital is the Jade Capital."

Fengdu is the name of a mountain. The Mountain of Fengdu lies north of Heaven and Earth, beyond the Northern Sea. Its height is two thousand six hundred li, and both its interior and exterior are adorned with palaces of the seven treasures, where the gods and spirits of Heaven and Earth reside. Within it, the Six Heavens of the Three Realms and the Great Demon King of the Northern Emperor hold dominion. Each of the six palaces governs the ghosts and spirits of the Six Heavens, and within the cavern are six palaces, all mirroring one another.

The Three Lesser Water Officials of the Lower Prime condense the qi of wind and marsh, coagulating the essence of the vast and luminous, establishing the Three Offices of the Lower Prime. The first is named the Tanggu Cavern Spring Palace, also called the Qinghua Fangzhu Palace. It governs the Water Emperor, the Divine King of Tanggu, the Nine River Water Courts, the River Earls, the immortals, the perfected ones, and all the great spirits within the waters who have attained the Dao, as well as the souls of the past and those who, though yet to attain the Dao, have accrued merit, receiving deliverance and ascension. This palace comprises three bureaus: left, right, and central. The left is named the Azure Origin Numinous Abyss Bureau; the right, the Ninefold Ice Cold Night Bureau; and the central, the Solitary North Azure Numinous Bureau. They register and seal the caverns of the Nine Rivers.

The Lower Prime’s left palace is named the Qingling Palace, also called the Southern Water Assembly Palace. It governs the myriad spirits within the waters—jiao dragons, whales, and leviathans—with five hundred million each of the Water Mother and Dragon Gate, all enveloped in the qi of ten thousand layers of wind-marsh vajra. This palace also comprises three bureaus: the central is named the Numinous Treasure Kalpa Blade Bureau; the left, the Ling Kalpa Bureau; and the right, the Long Night Cold Court Bureau, which oversees the myriad spirits of the waters.

The Lower Prime’s right palace is named the Northern Fengdu Palace, also called the Fengdu Palace. It governs the accumulated souls of the dead in eternal night, condemned to penal servitude. Its left bureau is named the Liberation and Kalpa Measure Bureau; the right, the Spring Cavern Ghosts and Spirits Bureau; and the central, the Numinous Passage Great Kalpa Bureau.

The Three Lesser Water Officials of the Lower Prime oversee three palaces, each governing fourteen departments, totaling forty-two departments across the three palaces. Together, they administer the caverns of the Nine Rivers, all bearing natural designations, and command all the spirits of the Three Rivers, Four Seas, and Nine River Water Courts—both those who have attained the Dao and those who have not—as well as the perfected immortals and jade maidens of the Five Sacred Peaks upon the earth. On the days of *gengshen* in the sexagenary cycle of the Great Year, they descend to the Three Offices of Tanggu, Qingling, and Northern Fengdu to review and compile the registers of life and death of the Nine Bureaus.

In ancient times, when Heaven and Earth underwent transformation and sank into the era of Yankang, all was dark and unopened until the Flying Celestials illuminated the light. Thereupon, they scattered radiance across the heavens, receiving qi and sprinkling numinosity. The former name of the Mysterious Capital was the Jade Capital, also a title of the Great Sage. The Supreme Perfected of the Northern Emperor governs the Palace of Mysterious Numinosity, beneath which lies the Cold Ice Night Court, and further below, the realm of the Eight Difficulties. Thus, it is called the Spring Cavern Palace.

The Recluse says: "The Spring Cavern Palace is the ghostly court of the Ninefold Dark and Eternal Night, while the Northern Capital of Fengdu is Fengdu, the ghostly capital of the Northern Emperor. Fengdu is the mountain of the Ninefold Dark in the Northern Sea, named the Ghost Capital, situated atop the dark mountain of Fengdu."

The Lesser Mystery says: "This is the right palace of the Lower Prime. According to the *True Instructions*, the Northern Fengdu lies in the outer *gui* region north of Heaven and Earth, also named the Fengdu Spring Cavern Palace, the right bureau of Fengdu. Fengdu is the name of the mountain in the Northern Capital, towering two thousand six hundred li in height, with a circumference of thirty thousand li. Beneath it lies a cavern-heaven with a circumference of fifteen thousand li. Both its interior and exterior are adorned with palaces of the seven treasures. There are the Upper, Middle, and Lower Offices, each with eight prisons, totaling twenty-four prisons, all dwelling places of the gods and spirits of Heaven and Earth. The Three Offices and Nine Bureaus correspond to the Twelve River Sources."

The East says: "The Three Offices are the Offices of Heaven, Earth, and Water. The Upper Prime’s Celestial Office comprises three offices, each governing twelve departments, totaling thirty-six departments. The Middle Prime’s Terrestrial Office also comprises three offices, each governing fourteen departments, totaling forty-two departments. The Lower Prime’s Water Office likewise comprises three palaces, each governing fourteen departments, totaling forty-two departments. Together, the Three Offices comprise one hundred twenty departments, overseeing ghosts, spirits, and humans. The Offices of Heaven, Earth, and Water form the Nine Bureaus. Within the Nine Seas, Three Rivers, and Twelve River Sources, the registers of life and death are boundless and fathomless. All the infinite immortals and spirits are universally proclaimed."

The Recluse says: "The Three Offices are the Three Offices of Fengdu. Fengdu has six palaces, with two palaces constituting one office, hence six palaces form three offices. Each office has three bureaus, so three offices have nine bureaus. The left is the Fire Office, the right the Water Office, and the central the Female Office, each following the source of affairs, overseeing examinations and punishments, akin to the Six Ministries of the mundane world. The Twelve River Sources are the Water Courts, their affairs corresponding to the Three Offices and Nine Bureaus. The Three Offices and Nine Bureaus also number twelve, and since they belong to the north, which is a yin position, the number twelve is adopted to establish the twelve offices. This merely designates the principal authorities; lesser positions are not mentioned."

The Lesser Mystery says: "The Three Offices are the Upper Prime’s Celestial Office, the Middle Prime’s Terrestrial Office, and the Lower Prime’s Water Office. They govern the Nine Bureaus, the administrative bureaus of the Nine Courts. The Twelve River Sources refer to the moon as the essence of the Great Yin and the mother of all waters. The Well is the source of the Celestial River and the fountainhead of all waters. Each month, the moon completes a circuit of the heavens, and each year, twelve months pass, with the moon traversing the Eastern Well each month, irrigating the blossoms of the Yellow Waters and bathing the countenances

According to the *Scripture of the Three Primes’ Precepts and Commandments*, the Upper Prime’s Celestial Office is subordinate to the Jade Clarity Realm, where the qi of blue, yellow, and white coalesce to establish the Three Offices of the Upper Prime. The Mysterious Qi forms the Central Palace; the Primordial Qi, the Left Palace; and the Original Qi, the Right Palace. The Central Palace is named the Purple Tenuity Palace of the Seven Treasures of Primordial Yang, where the qi of the Blue Primordial and Primal Yang coalesce. It presides over the Supreme Thearch of the Jade Void of the Upper Realized Ones, the Thearchs of the Myriad Heavens, and the Great Spirits of the Upper Sages. Its offices number fifty-five myriad, five thousand five hundred fifty-five myriad myriad layers, and among its divine and immortal officials, there are likewise fifty-five myriad, five thousand five hundred fifty-five myriad myriad beings, all coalesced from the natural Blue Primordial Qi to form humans. Their robes are feathered flying garments of blue. Within the Purple Tenuity Palace resides the Talisman of Prolonged Life; when this talisman is issued to the eight directions, the qi of the eight directions responds with immediate resonance, and all instantly become human. When the talisman is concealed, they revert to qi. The palace establishes three bureaus—left, right, and central. The Left Bureau governs the Office of Life, overseen by the Fire Official of Grand Yang; the Right Bureau governs the Office of Death, overseen by the Water Official of Grand Yin; and the Central Bureau governs both life and death, examining transgressions and blessings with the Wind Blade. The term "examine" means to verify matters: great blessings are reviewed every three years, middling blessings every nine years, and minor blessings every twenty-four years. Each of the three bureaus commands ninety million officials, collectively overseeing the twelve departments of life, death, transgressions, and blessings.

The Left Palace is named the Palace of the Great Mysterious Primordial Yellow and Supreme Ultimate of the Left, also known as the Left Ministerial Palace of Jade Clarity. It coalesces from the Primordial Yellow Qi and presides over the thousand perfected ones who have attained the Dao, as well as the registers of male and female lives. Its palace numbers and officials do not differ from the Central Palace; they, too, coalesce from the natural Primordial Yellow Qi to form humans, and their robes are feathered flying garments of yellow. Within the Supreme Ultimate Palace of the Left resides the Talisman of Summoning Spirits, used in the same manner as the Talisman of Prolonged Life. The Left Palace also establishes three bureaus, which examine transgressions and blessings in the same manner as the Central Palace.

The Right Palace is also named the Palace of the Great Mysterious Cavern White and Supreme Ultimate of the Right, which is the Palace of Pure Tenuity. It coalesces from the Cavern White Qi of the Celestial Primordial and presides over the Upper Realized Ones who have attained the Dao, as well as the registers of the common people—both male and female—who have not yet attained the Dao, along with their records of transgressions. Its palace numbers and officials likewise do not differ from the Central Palace. Its inhabitants coalesce from the natural Cavern White Qi to form humans, and their robes are feathered flying garments of white. Within the palace resides the Talisman of Illuminating the Realized, used in the same manner as the Talismans of Prolonged Life and Summoning Spirits. The three bureaus—left, right, and central—examine transgressions and blessings in the same manner as the Central Palace.

The Three Palaces of the Upper Prime each govern three bureaus, and each bureau governs four departments, so that the nine bureaus collectively oversee thirty-six departments. Those who have accumulated sufficient merit and virtue and are destined for immortality are recorded in the Purple Tenuity Palace; those who revere and uphold the Great Dao are recorded in the Supreme Ultimate Palace of the Left; and those destined for death are recorded in the Right Palace.

The Terrestrial Office of the Middle Prime’s second rank is subordinate to the Supreme Clarity Realm, coalescing from the Cavernous Mixed Spirit Qi and condensing the essence of the Ultimate Yellow. Its Central Palace is named the Palace of Cavernous Spirit and Pure Tenuity, presiding over the Five Thearchs, the Five Marchmounts, and all the perfected terrestrial immortals who have attained the Dao. Its palaces number fifty-five myriad, five thousand five hundred fifty-five myriad myriad layers, and among its divine and immortal officials, there are ninety-nine myriad, nine thousand nine hundred ninety-nine myriad beings. These are the souls of the deceased who possessed merit and virtue, not coalesced from natural qi. Having received deliverance, they assume the duties of the Terrestrial Office of Immortals, each with a fixed term. When their merit is complete and their virtue advanced, they ascend to become officials of the Celestial Bureaus; those whose merit is incomplete return to be reborn among humans.

The Central Palace establishes three bureaus—left, right, and central. The Left Bureau is named the Bureau of Enduring Transgressions and Bright Dawn; the Right Bureau, the Bureau of Yin’s Termination and Heaven’s Severance; and the Central Bureau, the Bureau of the Seven Wrongs and Tranquil Illumination. They examine transgressions, blessings, yin and yang, and the reckoning of years in the same manner as the Upper Prime. The Left Palace is named the Palace of the Southern Culmen and Cavernous Yang, presiding over the Nine Earths’ Earthly Thearchs, the myriad spirit officials of the Eight Poles, and the registers of lives. Its palace numbers and officials do not differ from the Palace of Pure Tenuity. The palace establishes three bureaus: the Left Bureau is named the Bureau of the Winding Dark Springs; the Right Bureau, the Bureau of the Great Execution of the Nine Netherworlds; and the Central Bureau, the Bureau of the Punitive Qi of the Salty Pond. They examine transgressions and blessings, and the reckoning of years does not differ from the Left Palace. The three palaces and three bureaus of the Middle Prime collectively oversee fourteen departments, and the nine bureaus together govern forty-two departments. They all reside within the caverns of mountains, where they memorialize good and evil in the same manner as the Upper Prime.

The Water Office of the Lower Prime’s third rank is subordinate to the Grand Clarity Realm, coalescing from the qi of wind and marsh and condensing the essence of the Vast Dawn. Its Central Palace is named the Palace of the Scalding Valley and Cavernous Springs, also called the Palace of Azure Florescence and the Square Cauldron. It presides over the Divine Kings of the Scalding Valley, the Water Bureaus of the Nine Rivers, the River Earls, the water immortals, and the great spirits of the waters, as well as the registers and records of immortals. Its palace numbers and officials are the same as those of the Middle Prime. Its officials are also filled by souls possessing merit and virtue. The palace establishes three bureaus: the Left Bureau is named the Bureau of the Azure Primordial and Numinous Springs; the Right Bureau, the Bureau of the Nine Springs and Frigid Night; and the Central Bureau, the Bureau of the Northern Solitude and Azure Numinosity. They examine the reckoning of years, transgressions, and blessings in the same manner as the Middle Prime.

The Left Palace is named the Palace of Pure Numinosity, presiding over the myriad essences of the waters, the jiao dragons, whales, and salamanders, as well as the assembly of the Water Mother and Dragon Gate, the cycles of deliverance, and the registers of human lives, deaths, merits, and transgressions. Its qi is the adamantine qi of wind and marsh, and its palace numbers and officials do not differ from the Central Palace. The Right Palace establishes three bureaus: the Left Bureau is named the Bureau of the Numinous Kalpa; the Right Bureau, the Bureau of the Long Night; and the Central Bureau, the Bureau of the Numinous Treasure and Kalpa Blade. They examine transgressions and blessings in the same manner as the Central Palace. It collectively presides over the essence-souls of the waters, the hundred ghosts, and the myriad spirits, all coalesced from the qi of the wind-marsh’s Brahman conduct. Its palace numbers and officials are also the same as those of the Middle Prime.

The Right Palace is named the Fengdu Palace, establishing three bureaus: the Left Bureau is named the Bureau of Opening Deliverance and Kalpa Measure; the Central Bureau, the Bureau of Communicating with Spirits and the Great Kalpa; and the Right Bureau, the Bureau of the Winding Springs and Ghostly Spirits. They examine transgressions and blessings in the same manner as the Middle Prime.

The Lower Prime comprises three palaces, each governing three bureaus; the nine bureaus together oversee forty-two departments, with each set of three bureaus jointly administering fourteen departments and nine chambers. They collectively govern the Water Emperors and Divine Kings of the Eight Seas and Four Watercourses, as well as all numinous spirits within the waters. The Three Primes in total comprise nine palaces, twenty-seven bureaus, and one hundred twenty departments.

The Left governs matters of life, the Right governs matters of death. Meritorious deeds are recorded in the green registers of the Left Bureau, while transgressions are inscribed in the black registers of the Right Bureau. If transgressions are intermingled with blessings, or blessings with transgressions, they are not assigned to a single department.

Those who attain the Dao are reported to the Central Palace; those with merit are memorialized to the Left Palace; those with transgressions are memorialized to the Right Palace. On each of the Three Primes and Eight Festivals, the roots of evil are severed.

**Xuan Ying states:** This elucidates the matter of refining and delivering deceased souls with the Yellow Waters and Moon Essence. The "twelve" refers to the twelve months of the year. The "River Source" is the Celestial River.
