The heavens possess the Twenty-Eight Constellations, and the Well Star of the Eastern Quadrant is the source of the Celestial River, the fountainhead of all waters. The Moon is the essence of the Great Yin and the mother of all waters. As the Moon traverses the heavens each month, it passes through the Well Star, exhaling water to irrigate the earth—hence the term "Twelve River Sources." When deceased souls receive rebirth, they are all refined by the Yellow Waters to become perfected immortals. This passage expounds on the deliverance of deceased souls, thus invoking the Twelve River Sources to clarify the matter. Moreover, the Three Primes and Eight Festivals serve as exhortations for cultivation. Should practitioners attain swift ascent, they may also deliver their ancestors, as referred to in the following text:

*Liberating ancestors and progenitors, kin of kalpas innumerable.*

**Youxi states:** This means freeing the imprisoned souls of ancestral generations and pardoning the karmic bonds of clan relatives across countless kalpas.

**Shaowei states:** Whenever the Three Officials conduct their reviews, if descendants have accrued great merit, the Jade Emperor will immediately grant liberation to their ancestors, progenitors, and all clan relatives across kalpas, delivering them to be reborn in the heavens.

*Swiftly erasing the ledgers of transgression, severing the roots of evil.*

**Dong states:** *Ji* means swift; *bu* means record. To swiftly expunge the records of transgression and sever the roots of evil.

**Youxi states:** To swiftly erase the black ledgers of karmic retribution and promptly uproot the deep-seated causes of malevolent consequences.

*No longer detained, nor forced to mingle with ghostly multitudes.*

**Dong states:** *Ju* means to confine; *bi* means to compel. No longer confined or bound, nor forcibly gathered within the courts of ghosts, obstructing the true teaching.

**Youxi states:** Having relied on the merit of scriptural recitation for deliverance and bathed in the grace of the Dao for liberation, how could there remain any hardship of confinement or stagnation, or mingling among the throngs of ghosts?

**Shaowei states:** By the edict of the Three Officials, those with merit shall not be detained or compelled to mingle with ghostly multitudes.

*By the talismanic command of the Primordial Beginning, they ascend in due time. In the Frigid Pool of the Northern Capital, their forms and souls are marshaled and guarded.*

**Dong states:** When the Primordial Heavenly Worthy expounded the scriptures, He issued a command summoning the officials of the Nine Bureaus from the hells of the ten directions and boundless worlds, from the darkest hour of the night, and from the icy courts of the Northern Capital. In an instant, each marshaled their ghostly legions to escort the delivered souls forth from the Palace of Eternal Night, allowing them all to behold the light.

**Youxi states:** By the talismanic decree of the Primordial Beginning, they ascend in the daylight hours. The Northern Emperor instructs the souls of the Frigid Pool—those who received form—to be marshaled forth from the Bureau of Winding Springs. The Frigid Pool is the pool of punishment.

**Shaowei states:** Beneath Fengdu lies the Frigid Pool. Should any ghost or spirit grow lax, the Jade Emperor issues a talismanic command, and in an instant, the icy courts of the night, the Three Officials and Nine Bureaus, each marshal the imprisoned souls to be moved from the Palace of Eternal Night, all receiving deliverance and beholding the light.

*Subduing demons and safeguarding promotion, they are delivered to the Southern Palace by rank.* **Dong states:** The demon kings of the Three Realms constantly compose deceptive songs to disturb the minds of cultivators.

The steadfast of heart—these the demon kings escort directly to ascend within the Yellow Reed Heavens, where they proceed to Golden Flower Mountain to receive the token of the Great One, thereby subduing the trials of the great demons; only then are they delivered. At that moment, talismans restrain the demon kings, commanding them to safeguard the promotion to the Southern Palace.

**Youqi states:** Once the Northern Emperor is commanded to release the ghostly souls from the Northern Bureau, the demon kings are then restrained to promote the immortal ranks to the Southern Palace. The dead souls undergo refinement, and the immortals are transformed into human form.

**Dong states:** The Southern Palace is the Palace of Longevity. The Lord of Deliverance governs within it, named Xu Yuan, who is admitted into the Southern Palace. Xu Yuan refines the decayed bones, while the Vital Youths irrigate them with the essence of life, inscribing the contract of existence upon the Four Poles and bestowing the natural Feathered Youths. The Vital Youths are the numinous youths of the sun’s midst.

**Youqi states:** When the dead souls are promoted within the Southern Palace, their ghostly substance is refined with the unguent of flowing fire, and from this transformation, they attain immortality. The living form receives deliverance, enduring for kalpas without end.

**Dong states:** The living form refers to the soul that, having undergone refinement and deliverance, regains human existence. When the Primordial Beginning initiates transformation, the body ascends to the Palace of Longevity, enduring for countless kalpas. Revolving through kalpas, it shares the age of Heaven.

**Youqi states:** If in this very life one receives ascension and deliverance, one’s years equal those of Heaven, and one’s form merges with the Dao, enduring from the beginning to the end of kalpas, from kalpa to kalpa, while kalpas themselves rise and fall, yet one alone remains. When the world of Heaven and Earth completes one cycle of its destiny, this is called a kalpa.

**Xuanying states:** "Revolving through kalpas" refers to kalpas of varying magnitudes. When a great kalpa reaches its cycle, it is the time when Heaven and Earth decay and the kalpic fire arises. A lesser kalpa marks the completion of one cycle of human birth and death, termed a kalpa. "Revolving through kalpas" means that the dead souls, refined and transformed into human form, cannot escape death; after death, they are reborn as humans, thus revolving through kalpas. Kalpa after kalpa, they are reborn in the human realm, hence it is said they share the age of Heaven. They forever transcend the Three Paths, the Five Sufferings, and the Eight Difficulties.

**Dong states:** "Forever" means eternally. The Three Paths are the names of the three evil gates. The first is the Gate of Sensual Desire, also called the Upper Corpse Path or the Heavenly Path Realm. The second is the Gate of Attachment, also called the Middle Corpse Path or the Human Path Realm. The third is the Gate of Greed, also called the Lower Corpse Path or the Earthly Path Realm. These are the Three Evil Gates, also termed the Three Corpse Paths or the Three Path Realms, which constantly dwell within the human body, blocking the three passes of the body, severing the three roots of life, obstructing the path to immortal learning, and suppressing the soul’s ascent.

The Five Sufferings are also called the Five Path Gates. The first is the Gate of Sensual Affliction, also called the Hell of Mount Tai; the second is the Gate of Attachment’s Affliction, also called the Path of Wind and Blades; the third is the Gate of Greed’s Affliction, also called the Path of Carrying Stones and Mountains; the fourth is the Gate of Vanity’s Affliction, also called the Path of Filling the Sea to Make Rivers; the fifth is the Gate of Bodily Affliction, also called the Path of Swallowing Fire and Eating Coals in Cauldrons of Boiling Water. Thus, the scripture says: "The reason I have great suffering is because I have a body; if I had no body, what suffering would I have?" These Five Sufferings and Five Paths constantly reside within the human body, binding the root of life, obstructing the path to summoning the true, and severing the gate to immortal cultivation. The Three Paths and Five Sufferings together form the Eight Difficulties, the root of transgression. Without dissolving one’s form above the Five Paths and erasing one’s traces beneath the Five Sufferings, the myriad afflictions remain unsevered, and one sinks into the fields of transgression. Those who study the supreme Ways must first sever all afflictions, extinguish the paths of suffering, so that true qi naturally descends, and immortality naturally manifests. Only then can one transform one’s form, wander through the Three Clarities, enter the Palace of Longevity, and be forever free from the Eight Difficulties.

They transcend and rise above the Three Realms, roaming carefree in the Upper Clarity.

**Dong states:** "Transcend" means to ascend; "rise" means to soar high. Upon ascending to the Southern Palace, the Divine King commands the Feathered Forest Inspector to review the Register of the Living, receive the talisman, and ascend as an immortal, roaming amidst the Cloud Palaces, clad in garments woven of clouds, proceeding directly to the Vermilion Mound Palace to receive blessings in the Heavenly Hall, merging with the Flying Celestials in radiance, soaring through the clouds. The Divine King is the Wondrously Accomplished Heavenly King, named Yu Sheng, who governs the Flying Celestial deities of the ten directions. The Feathered Forest Inspector, named Miao Xue, knows the celestial sounds of Heaven, and is called the Earth’s Only One in the Three Realms. He attends to the luminous spirits and ghosts, naturally perceiving all, flying through the Three Realms, and roaming in the Upper Clarity.

**Youqi states:** Having equaled the years of Heaven and merged form with the Dao, one forever escapes the servitude of the Three Paths and the exile of the Five Sufferings; one transcends the Eight Difficulties in the demonic realms and ascends to the true domain of the Nine Heavens. The Three Paths are: first, the Path of Eternal Night; second, the Path of the Frigid Pool; third, the Path of Carrying Stones. The Five Sufferings are: first, the Suffering of Knife Mountains; second, the Suffering of Sword Trees; third, the Suffering of Cauldrons of Boiling Water; fourth, the Suffering of Furnace Coals; fifth, the Suffering of Interrogation and Exile. The Eight Difficulties comprise the Three Paths and Five Sufferings.

**Shaowei states:** The Three Paths are the servitudes of the Three Officials. The first is the servitude of the Heavenly Official, racing thunder and lightning; the second is the servitude of the Earthly Official, carrying mountains and stones; the third is the servitude of the Water Official, hauling and drawing from the dark seas. The Five Sufferings are: climbing knife mountains, treading sword trees, entering cauldrons of boiling water, embracing bronze pillars, and swallowing fire and eating coals. The Eight Difficulties are the eight gates of profound and desolate hardship, which the Dao Lord inquired about and the Flying Celestials answered. The Heaven of Upper Clarity is where the Heavenly Emperor and Jade Perfected dwell, in the colorless radiance of ascetic practice.

**Dong states:** In the Heaven of Upper Clarity, there resides the Heavenly Emperor Jade Perfected, whose name is Tuoyu. The Five Chapters of True Writ, bound with luminous qi, dwell upon the Cloud Alas Ridge, known as the Heaven of Wondrous Completion.

The Jade Perfected in the Heaven of Upper Clarity does not partake in the realm of form, riding the great qi of Brahman to roam and enter the Heaven of Supreme Yellow Emperor Zeng.

**Youxi remarks:** In the Heaven of Upper Clarity, the Heavenly Emperor occupies the most exalted position among the thirty-six Heavenly Emperors, his Dao equal to that of the Primordial Beginning, his rank aligned with the Jade Clarity. Thus he is called Jade Perfected, and this is the Upper Clarity. Below this lie four realms, each containing nine heavens, four nines combining to form thirty-six heavens—distinct from the thirty-two heavens. The formless heavens possess radiance without color, hence termed "Brahmanic practice." Following this are the heavens of the four subsequent directions, each direction comprising eight heavens, four eights combining to form thirty-two heavens, called the Four Brahman Heavens. *Jing* refers to the body; *se* refers to substance. Speaking of the thirty-two heavens, the Supreme Thearchs, though lofty and revered in form, possess radiance without substance. Though they bear true appearances, they move through the void without obstruction, unobstructed by things, hence termed "Brahmanic practice." Brahman is the Dao within the Dao. These Three Clarities, five realms, and thirty-six heavens are called the Great Luo of the Four Directions. Within the Four Brahman and thirty-two heavens, the Four Heavens of Seed People are called the Middle Luo. The three realms of desire, form, and formlessness, comprising twenty-eight heavens, are called the Lesser Luo.

**Shaowei states:** The Heavenly Emperor of Upper Clarity is named Jade Perfected, styled Tuoyu, and titled the Purple Dawn Heavenly Thearch. He does not partake in the realm of form, possessing no Three Radiance, hence called "radiance without color." Only the great qi of Brahman flows and blends, mapping the heavens in clouds. Each heaven possesses its own sun and moon. From Upper Clarity to the Great Luo, nine-colored luminosity arises spontaneously, independent of sun and moon, thus termed "radiance without color in Brahmanic practice."

In the Heaven of Supreme Yellow Emperor Zeng, the Emperor is Yulan Yuming.

**Dong states:** The first heaven of the East belongs to the Heaven of Pure Tenuity, where the Emperor’s position is the Black of Primordial Yang.

**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is yellow in color, its qi linked to the Brahman qi of the northwest. The Emperor’s taboo name is Guanjue, overseeing the Register of Life. The people of this heaven live for nine million years, their six roots all tainted—this is called the Realm of Desire.

**Xuanying states:** Whenever Brahman qi is mentioned, it refers to the heavens of the four corners. *Wei* means "corner." The heavens of the four cardinal directions are named after the qi of the twenty-eight constellations; the heavens of the four corners do not belong to the cardinal constellations but borrow the qi of the adjacent constellations to form, hence termed Brahman qi. Brahman is a name denoting mixture and lack of fixed attachment. For example, the Heaven of Emperor Zeng draws upon the qi of the Kui and Bi constellations, hence called Brahman qi. The three heavens below follow this pattern. Among the thirty-two heavens, the lifespans of heavenly beings increase by onefold with each ascent from this heaven upward—this pattern is self-evident. Furthermore, in the scriptures of the thirty-two heavens from Emperor Zeng downward, the text preceding "heaven" denotes the name of the heaven, while the text following "Emperor" denotes the title of the Heavenly Emperor.

In the Heaven of Great Brilliance and Jade Perfection, the Emperor is Xu’anatian.

**Dong states:** The second heaven of the East belongs to the Heaven of Yu Remnant, where the Emperor’s position is the qi of Upper Yang.

**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is green in color, its qi linked to the Bi constellation of the north. The Emperor’s taboo name is Lanjue, overseeing the rebirth of souls. The people of this heaven live for eighteen million years, one desire-root roughly purified, five desire-roots roughly tainted.

In the Heaven of Luminous Clarity and Harmonious Youth, the Emperor is Yuanyu Qijing.

**Dong states:** The third heaven of the East belongs to the Heaven of Great Red, where the Emperor’s position is the qi of Great Yang.

**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is black in color, its qi linked to the Shi constellation of the north. The Emperor’s taboo name is Dajue, overseeing the propagation of governance and teachings, liberating heavenly beings. The people of this heaven live for thirty-six million years, two desire-roots roughly purified, four desire-roots roughly tainted.

In the Heaven of Mysterious Womb and Peaceful Nurturance, the Emperor is Liu Dunneixian.

**Dong states:** The fourth heaven of the East belongs to the Heaven of Primordial Radiance, where the Emperor’s position is the First Clear Yang of the Nine Heavens.

**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is red in color, its qi linked to the Wei constellation of the north. The Emperor’s taboo name is Yuwang, overseeing the summoning of demons and elevation of immortals. The people of this heaven live for seventy-two million years, three desire-roots roughly purified, three desire-roots roughly tainted.

In the Heaven of Primordial Brilliance and Literary Elevation, the Emperor is Chou Falun.

**Dong states:** The fifth heaven of the East belongs to the Heaven of Immeasurable Longevity, where the Emperor’s position is the Second Cavernous Yang of the Nine Heavens.

**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is blue-green in color, its qi linked to the Xu constellation of the north. The Emperor’s taboo name is Fanyun, overseeing the circulation of primordial qi. The people of this heaven live for one hundred forty-four million years, four desire-roots roughly purified, two desire-roots roughly tainted.

In the Heaven of Upper Brilliance and Seven Luminaries’ Ma Yi, the Emperor is Tian Huaiyan.

**Dong states:** The sixth heaven of the East belongs to the Heaven of Upper Surveillance, where the Emperor’s position is the qi of Pervading Yang.

**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is black in color, its qi linked to the Xunü constellation of the north. The Emperor’s taboo name is Yuzhen, overseeing the liberation of those in profound difficulty. The people of this heaven live for two hundred eighty-eight million years, five desire-roots roughly purified, one desire-root roughly tainted.

The above six heavens are called the Realm of Desire. The *Canons of the Supreme Perfected* state: In the first two heavens below, karmic retribution remains coarse, and desire is still expressed through bodily union; in the next two heavens, desire is expressed through holding hands; in the fifth heaven, through speech; and in the sixth heaven, through gaze. Now, due to the six desires, these six heavens are thus manifested. With one desire-root roughly purified, one ascends to the next heaven; when all six desires are wholly purified, one transcends the Realm of Desire and ascends to the Realm of Form.

**Zongjun states:** To speak of the Realm of Desire is to speak of beings with form and desire, who engage in the union of yin and yang, and are born of wombs—hence it is called the Realm of Desire.

The Void-Transcending Balance Heaven, where the Emperor governs the Radiance of True Stability.
**Dong states:** The seventh heaven of the East, belonging to the Tuṣita Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yang.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is jade-green in hue, its qi linked to the Northern Dipper constellation. The Emperor’s name is "Supreme None," and he presides over the illumination of the supreme Dao. Beings here live for 576 million years, their six sensory dusts still tainted—having just emerged from the Realm of Desire, they remain stained by the dusts of form.

The Primordial Obscurity Veiling Heaven, where the Emperor nurtures the Nine Prosperities.
**Dong states:** The eighth heaven of the East, belonging to the Heaven of Joy Without Arrogance, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of extreme yang.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is purple in hue, its qi linked to the Dipper constellation of the North. The Emperor’s name is Xu Yuan, and he governs the refinement and deliverance of decayed remains. Beings here live for 1,152 million years, with one sensory dust roughly purified and five still tainted.

The Vermilion Brilliance Harmonizing Yang Heaven, where the Emperor governs the Forbidden Realms of the Supreme Perfected.
**Dong states:** The first heaven of the South, belonging to the Heaven of Responsive Transformation, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of incipient yang.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is white in hue, its qi linked to the northeast’s Brahmanic qi, situated between the Winnowing Basket and Dipper constellations. The Emperor’s name is Huan Ming, and he governs the refinement of immortals into perfected beings. Beings here live for 23,040 million years, with two sensory dusts roughly purified and four still tainted.

The Mystic Brilliance Reverent Splendor Heaven, where the Emperor chants the Hymns of Obscure Sound.
**Dong states:** The second heaven of the South, belonging to the Heaven of Brahmā’s Treasure, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yang’s radiance.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is yellow in hue, its qi linked to the Winnowing Basket constellation of the East. The Emperor’s name is Shiyuan, and he responds to and transforms all things. Beings here live for 460,800 million years, with three sensory dusts roughly purified and three still tainted.

The Radiant Brilliance Ancestral Whirlwind Heaven, where the Emperor embodies Double Brilliance.
**Dong states:** The third heaven of the South, belonging to the Māyā Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of penetrating yang.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is green in hue, its qi linked to the Tail constellation of the East. The Emperor’s name is Luojue Wang, and at the kalpa’s end, he gathers those who study immortality. Beings here live for 9,216 million years, with four sensory dusts roughly purified and two still tainted.

The Bamboo Grove August Drum Heaven, where the Emperor masters the Wondrous Eloquence of Māyā.
**Dong states:** The fourth heaven of the South, belonging to the Heaven of Sorrowful Harmony, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yang’s brilliance.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is blue-green in hue, its qi linked to the Heart constellation of the East. The Emperor’s name is Shao, and he tests those who study immortality through demonic trials. Beings here live for 18,432 million years, with five sensory dusts roughly purified and one still tainted.
**Xuanying states:** These preceding six heavens are the heavens of sensory dusts. If a practitioner cultivates to the utmost in these heavens, all sensory dusts are exhausted, and they ascend to the heavens of subtle dusts, as described below.

There are six heavens of subtle dusts.
The Void Brilliance Illuminating Hall Heaven, where the Emperor is named A’lou Lou Sheng.
**Dong states:** The fifth heaven of the South, belonging to the Heaven of Brahmā’s Brilliance, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yang’s evolution.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is red in hue, its qi linked to the Chamber constellation of the East. The Emperor’s name is Yun Shang, and he governs the deliverance of heaven and earth. Beings here live for 3,686,400 million years, with six sensory dusts roughly purified and six subtle dusts still tainted.

The Contemplative Brilliance Upright Stillness Heaven, where the Emperor is named Yumi Luo Qian.
**Dong states:** The sixth heaven of the South, belonging to the Heaven of Mixed Harmony, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yang’s brilliance.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is dark green in hue, its qi linked to the Root constellation of the East. The Emperor’s name is Jing Sheng, and he governs the deliverance of practitioners’ bodies. Beings here live for 7,372,800 million years, with one subtle dust purified and five still tainted.

The Mystic Brilliance Reverent Celebration Heaven, where the Emperor is named Long Luo Bodhi.
**Dong states:** The seventh heaven of the South, belonging to the Yiluo Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yang’s vastness.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is black in hue, its qi linked to the Neck constellation of the East. The Emperor’s name is Jing Zhu, and he delivers those who attain the Dao. Beings here live for 14,745,600 million years, with two subtle dusts purified and four still tainted.

The Supreme Radiance Ultimate Jade Heaven, where the Emperor is named Wan Li Wu Yan.
**Dong states:** The eighth heaven of the South, belonging to the Heaven of Na Shou Brilliance, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yang’s extremity.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is jade-green in hue, its qi linked to the Horn constellation of the East. The Emperor’s name is Kuo Yi, and he instructs those who study immortality. Beings here live for 29,491,200 million years, with three subtle dusts purified and three still tainted.

The Primordial Vessel Ascending Perfection Heaven, where the Emperor governs the Radiance of True Stability.
**Dong states:** The first heaven of the West, belonging to the Heaven of Stained Pearls, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of lesser yang.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is purple in hue, its qi linked to the Brahmanic qi of the southeast, situated between the Chariot and Horn constellations. The Emperor’s name is You, and he governs the refinement and deliverance of the dead to be reborn. Beings here live for 58,982,400 million years, with four subtle dusts purified and two still tainted.

The Supreme Peace August Cliff Heaven, where the Emperor is named Polou A Tan.
**Dong states:** The second heaven of the West, belonging to the Heaven of Arriving Heads, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of great yang.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is white in hue, its qi linked to the Chariot constellation of the South. The Emperor’s name is Wan, and he governs the deliverance of the virtuous. Beings here live for 117,964,800 million years, with five subtle dusts purified and one still tainted.
**Xuanying states:** These preceding six heavens are the heavens of subtle dusts. If a practitioner cultivates to the utmost in these heavens, all subtle dusts are exhausted, and they ascend to the heavens of light dusts, as described below.

There are six heavens of light dusts.
The Manifest Stability Ultimate Wind Heaven, where the Emperor is named Zhao Zhen Tong.
**Dong states:** The third heaven of the West, belonging to the Heaven of Arriving for Inquiry, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of vast yang.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is yellow in hue, its qi linked to the Wings constellation of the South. The Emperor’s name is Liu, and he governs the deliverance of souls with meritorious virtue.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 235,929,600,000,000 years, with six subtle dusts purified and six light dusts tainted.
**Yellow Filial Flourishing Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Saluo Louwang.
**Dong states:** The fourth heaven of the West, belonging to the Anaboluojia Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of penetrating yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is green in hue, its qi linked to the Zhang constellation of the South. The Emperor’s name is Yi Miao, and he governs the unveiling of night and the opening of darkness.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 471,859,200,000,000 years, with one light dust purified and five light dusts tainted.
**Great Yellow Converging Floating Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Min Ba Kuang.
**Dong states:** The fifth heaven of the West, belonging to the Pololihe Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of unfolding yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is blue in hue, its qi linked to the Xing constellation of the South. The Emperor’s name is A Lan, and he governs the summoning of demons and the gathering of the perfected.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 943,718,400,000,000 years, with two light dusts purified and four light dusts tainted.
**Thought-Free River Source Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Ming Fan Guang.
**Dong states:** The sixth heaven of the West, belonging to the Fan Ming Yuan Huang Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of mysterious yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is red in hue, its qi linked to the Liu constellation of the South. The Emperor’s name is A Qiu, and he governs the deliverance of virtuous souls.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 1,887,436,800,000,000 years, with three light dusts purified and three light dusts tainted.
**Upper Shaking Joyous Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Bobo Jian.
**Dong states:** The seventh heaven of the West, belonging to the Cai Ning Yuan Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of vast yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is gray in hue, its qi linked to the Gui constellation of the South. The Emperor’s name is Wu Liang, and he governs the ranking of heavenly and human beings.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 3,774,873,600,000,000 years, with four light dusts purified and two light dusts tainted.
**Xuanying states:** Ranking refers to nobility and humility, wealth and poverty, and lifespan.
**Boundless Cloud Vow Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Piaonu Qiong Long.
**Dong states:** The eighth heaven of the West, belonging to the Tian Alihe Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of ultimate yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is black in hue, its qi linked to the Jing constellation of the South. The Emperor’s name is Tan, and he governs the deliverance of all immortals.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 7,549,747,200,000,000 years, with five light dusts purified and one light dust tainted.
The above eighteen heavens are called the **Form Realm**.
**The Great Perfected Regulations** states: Within the Formless Realm, the utmost perfected are without attachment, do not engage in yin and yang, and their people are born through transformation. They only consume fragrant qi and are no longer troubled by form and substance.
**Xuanying states:** These preceding eighteen heavens are collectively called the Form Realm. Ascending beyond this heaven, one reaches the Formless Realm, where form and appearance are entirely absent, and one may attain the same lifespan as the inhabitants of that realm. The preceding discussion of the Form Realm heavens shows that even light dusts remain as encumbrances. Here, in the Formless Realm, form and appearance are entirely absent. When a practitioner cultivates to this heaven, only the mind and consciousness remain, entering into qi observation.

**Luminous Court Cloud Crossing Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Hui Jue Hun.
**Dong states:** The first heaven of the North, belonging to the Adahe Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yin generation.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is jade-green in hue, its qi linked to the southwest’s Dao qi, situated between the Shen and Jing constellations. The Emperor’s name is Yu, and he governs the deliverance of cultivators.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 15,099,494,400,000,000 years, with all dusts of form purified, and their forms and appearances become as empty space. Only the mind and consciousness remain, entering into qi observation. When qi observation and the Dao are accomplished, one ascends to the **Primordial Cavern Heaven**.

**Abyssal Primordial Cavern Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Fan Xing Guan Sheng.
**Dong states:** The second heaven of the North, belonging to the Shan Ming Min Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of yin transformation.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is purple in hue, its qi linked to the Shen constellation of the West. The Emperor’s name is Shang, and he governs the deliverance of those who cultivate immortality.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 30,198,988,800,000,000 years. Though the mind and consciousness still labor, one may relinquish the mind and consciousness to cultivate, thereby attaining birth in the **Wondrous Accomplishment Heaven**.
**Xuanying states:** The mind and consciousness are still considered a hindrance. If one can relinquish the mind and consciousness to attain non-action, one may ascend to the Wondrous Accomplishment Heaven.

**Great Literary Flourishing Wondrous Accomplishment Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Nayuchou Ying.
**Dong states:** The third heaven of the North, belonging to the Liye Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of luminous yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is white in hue, its qi linked to the Zi constellation of the West. The Emperor’s name is Tuo, and he governs the governance of spirit kings.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 60,397,977,600,000,000 years. All former causes are forgotten, and the mind and consciousness reside in this heaven. This heaven does not require complete forgetting; thus, when needed, they are present, and when not, they are absent. In this state of being as if present and as if absent, one ascends to the **Forbidden Upper Heaven**.
**Xuanying states:** This heaven does not require complete forgetting. If emptiness and existence were both absent, the true response within the real would be lost. Within emptiness, there is the real; within the real, there is response. The myriad phenomena arise from emptiness; the myriad dharmas reside in the mind, yet without form or appearance. When applied, they exist; when existing, they are not non-existent. Guiding practitioners to observe the mind as if present and as if absent, one is born into the Forbidden Upper Heaven.

**Great Primordial Elegant Joy Forbidden Upper Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Long Luo Jue Chang.
**Dong states:** The fourth heaven of the North, belonging to the Ming Fan Kuo Da Zhao Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of penetrating yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is yellow in hue, its qi linked to the Bi constellation of the West. The Emperor’s name is Wei, and he governs the recording of demon kings.

The inhabitants of this heaven live for 1,207,959,552,000,000 years. Qi observation becomes increasingly wondrous, and all habitual tendencies are forgotten. If one thoroughly enters into spontaneity, one ascends to reside in the **Seed People Heaven**.

The above four heavens are called the Formless Realm. *The Great Perfection Regulations* states: In the Formless Realm, human bodies are subtle and wondrous, no longer possessing form or color. Some may grow hundreds of *zhang* in height yet remain unseen by ordinary people—only perfected beings can perceive them. Since no visible form exists, it is called the Formless Realm. However, beings within the Three Realms have not severed the root of birth and death, and the qi of yin and yang still lingers, thus their lifespans remain finite. Some ascend to higher realms, while others descend into the human world, endlessly revolving according to the depth of their merit until they attain the Dao.

**Xuan Ying remarks:** These four heavens constitute the Formless Realm. If cultivators reach this realm and continue their practice, they may be reborn into the Four Seed People Heavens.

**Great Void Supreme Constant Fusion Heaven**, where the Emperor oversees the supervision of ghosts and spirits.
**Dong states:** The fifth heaven of the North, belonging to the Anigou Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of numinous yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is green in hue, its qi linked to the Yi constellation of the West. The Emperor’s name is Ji, and he governs the assessment of cultivators’ merits. The inhabitants of this heaven live for 2,415,919,104,000,000 years. Having just emerged from the Three Realms, they are pure and unstained, delighting in effortless non-action.

**Great Release Jade Ascension Soaring Victory Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Miao Miao Xing Yuan.
**Dong states:** The sixth heaven of the North, belonging to the Xuda Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of ethereal yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is blue-green in hue, its qi linked to the Wei constellation of the West. The Emperor’s name is Fu Li, and he governs the summoning of immortals and sages. The inhabitants of this heaven live for 4,831,838,208,000,000 years.

**Dragon Transformation Brahman Passage Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Yun Shang Xuan Xuan.
**Dong states:** The seventh heaven of the North, belonging to the Yuanfan Xudai Taihun Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of congealed yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is crimson in hue, its qi linked to the Lou constellation of the West. The Emperor’s name is E Yi, and he governs the advancement of immortals to sagehood. The inhabitants of this heaven live for 9,663,676,416,000,000 years, ascending and descending with the qi, free from all habitual tendencies.

**Great Ultimate Nurturing Jia Yi Heaven**, where the Emperor is named Da Ze Fa Men.
**Dong states:** The eighth heaven of the North, belonging to the Shichan Ziran Heaven, where the Emperor’s throne is established by the qi of ultimate yin.
**Shaowei remarks:** This heaven is dark green in hue, its qi linked to the Kui constellation of the West. The Emperor’s name is Jing Shang, and he governs the deliverance of cultivators’ bodies. The inhabitants of this heaven live for 19,327,352,832,000,000 years.

The above four heavens are the Four Seed People Heavens, also called the Seed People Heavens. Some say the inhabitants of these four heavens exist beyond the dual qi of yin and yang, unbound by lifespan limits, delighting in purity and tranquility. *The Sutra of Original Boundary* states: "When habitual tendencies are exhausted, one transcends the rank of the Seed People." Here, "entanglements" refer to afflictions, and "habits" to learned practices. *The Great Perfection Regulations* states: "Ascending to these four heavens, one thoroughly enters the realm of the Dao, rising and falling with the qi, beyond the reach of calamity."

The thirty-two qi, their corresponding constellations, the Emperors’ names, and their governance are all recorded in *The Scripture of Cavernous Spirit*. The lifespans of the inhabitants and the purity or defilement of their roots and senses are found in *The Scripture of the Dragon’s Stride*.

Thirty-two heavens, thirty-two Emperors.
**Dong states:** Four times eight makes thirty-two heavens. Their names and taboo titles are often similar, difficult to interpret in Sanskrit, with separate oral instructions. Each of the thirty-two heavens has its own Emperor, totaling thirty-two Emperors. The taboo titles and hidden names of the heavens—
**Dong states:** What is spoken of in the scriptures are the hidden names and taboo titles of the heavens.
**Youxi remarks:** These heavens of the four directions are: the Nine Qi Blue Heaven of the East, the Three Qi Boat Heaven of the South, the Seven Qi White Heaven of the West, and the Five Qi Mysterious Heaven of the North. Each direction has eight heavens, making four times eight, thirty-two heavens. They reside above the Three Luminaries and below the Nine Palaces. The four cardinal directions, four corners, above and below together form the Ten Directions. Since the names of the heavens and the titles of the Emperors are termed "hidden names" and "taboo titles," they cannot be annotated.

Within the heavens, the numinous chapters arise spontaneously in the void.
**Dong states:** "Void" means profound; "cavernous" means empty. "Numinous chapters" are jade scripts. Within the profound emptiness exist spontaneous jade scripts, hence called "numinous chapters."
**Youxi remarks:** This scripture is the true word of the Great Ultimate’s emptiness and cavernousness, the numinous mystery of spontaneity and non-being.
**Shaowei remarks:** The "cavernous numinous chapters" are the Eightfold Convergence of Numinous Writings, the spontaneous jade scripts. In their origin, they coalesce from the qi of emptiness and cavernousness, forming spontaneously—not the language of the mundane world, but the tonal rhythms of the heavens.
**Xuan Ying remarks:** "Cavernous" refers to the vast emptiness within the heavens. "Numinous" denotes the Eightfold Convergence of Numinous Writings and the spontaneous jade scripts. "Chapters" are the harmonious convergence of words, their radiance interweaving into patterns. The "Eightfold Convergence" refers to the qi of the eight directions. "Spontaneous" clarifies that the origin of these numinous chapters lies in the coalescence of the true and wondrous qi of the eight directions within the emptiness and cavernousness, where the numinous winds stir and play, naturally forming these words and chapters—not crafted by deliberate effort, hence called "spontaneous numinous chapters."

The hidden rhythms of the heavens are the celestial sounds.
**Dong states:** "Rhythms" are melodies; "sounds" are chapters. Each heaven possesses an eight-character chapter, its melodies and rhythms concealed. The text is profound and abstruse, difficult to trace in detail, hence called "hidden rhythms."
**Youxi remarks:** These are also the subtle hidden rhythms of the heavens, the esoteric sounds of the Ten Directions.
**Xuan Ying remarks:** "Sounds" are echoes. A single emission is a voice; the interweaving of the five tones forms patterns, called "sounds."

The *Records of Music* in the *Book of Rites* states: "When sounds form patterns, they are called *yin*."

The exalted ones of the heavens, the gods of the heavens.
**Dong states:** Among the heavens there are also the most exalted, as well as great gods.
**Youxi remarks:** The exalted are the imperial lords of the thirty-two heavens; the gods are the divine kings of the flying immortals of the Ten Directions.

The great demons of the heavens, the numinous ones of the heavens.
**Dong states:** The great demons are the demon kings of the Three Realms; the numinous ones are the various numinous officials such as the Controllers of Destiny, Recorders of Deeds, and Overseers of Ascent.

Nine harmonies and ten unions transform and ascend to the Upper Clarity.
**Dong states:** "Harmony" means dissolution; "union" means convergence. In the era of Dragon Han, when all karmic conditions were exhausted, the Heavenly King transcended the courts of the Three Realms, entered the halls of the Great Void, and received the ninefold refinement of immortal transcendence, thereby attaining the title of Great Sage. When the Kalpa of Red Clarity began, the Primordial Beginning bestowed upon him the title of Brahma-Transcendence Heavenly King. Radiant, he ascended through the numinous gates and mounted the Jade Clarity Palace.
**Youxi remarks:** This clarifies that the gods and numinous ones of the heavens, as well as the great demons, are all masters of ascent and recorders of destinies. If the nine harmonies and ten unions mutually uphold one another, one can instantly transform and ascend to the Upper Clarity.
**Shaowei remarks:** The exalted are the lofty sages of the highest rank; the gods are the divine kings of the flying immortals; the great demons are the demon kings of the Three Realms; the numinous ones are the numinous chapters of the Five Emperors.

The jade characters emerge from the essence of the ninefold *qi* harmonized and the sounds of the ten directions united, transforming to ascend to the heavens of the Upper Clarity and flowing throughout the thirty-two realms.
The *Jade Instructions* states: The numinous chapters of the Five Emperors, the true texts of the Five Emperors, and the Five Elders arise together, governing the *qi* of the Nine Heavens.
**Xuanying remarks:** This elucidates the origin of the true texts and jade characters, which all derive from the exalted sages of the heavens, the divine kings of the flying immortals, the demon kings of the Three Realms, the Five Great Emperors, and the like. Harmonizing the essence of the ninefold *qi* and uniting the sounds of the Ten Directions, they transform into the wonders of the Upper Clarity Heaven and flow throughout the thirty-two heavens, forming the numinous chapters.

The nine *qi* are the *qi* of the Nine Heavens. Their boundless mysteries are profound and unfathomable.
**Dong states:** "Mysteries" means hidden; "fathom" means to examine in detail. The boundless texts are recondite in meaning, difficult to scrutinize.
**Youxi remarks:** This scripture can transform the mortal into the sagely, refine the coarse into the wondrous, transcend the Five Turbidities, and tread the Three Clarities—its mysteries are unfathomable, its principles beyond words.

The divine perfected are arrayed, universally delivering heavenly and human beings.
**Dong states:** "Array" means to spread; "place" means to establish. The Primordial Beginning, following the kalpic cycles, delivers beings by spreading and establishing the divine perfected, founding the thirty-two heavens, stabilizing the Five Peaks, and universally delivering heavenly and human beings.
**Youxi remarks:** "Array" means to unfold; "place" means to expand. The manner of unfolding and establishing is vast and boundless, signifying that this scripture’s divine perfected and immortal transformations are arrayed and expanded, universally delivering beings without end between heaven and earth.
**Xuanying remarks:** This speaks of the Heavenly Worthy arraying the jade strategies and true texts to universally deliver heavenly beings, humans, gods, and ghosts.

Today, rejoicing in the reception of deliverance, we traverse the passes of all heavens.
**Dong states:** Formerly, in the Heaven of Beginning Azure, within the Jeweled Pearl, the Dao Lord received the ten divisions of wondrous scriptures. At that time, the Primordial Beginning led the great sages of the Ten Directions, the divine kings of the flying immortals, and their boundless hosts into the Jeweled Pearl. When the scriptures were fully expounded, the perfected ones oversaw the deliverance and bestowed them upon the Dao Lord. At that moment, the joy was ineffable, and the thirty-two heavens universally passed through the covenantal gates. The lands of the Ten Directions all received deliverance, and the roots of karmic offenses and sins were simultaneously absolved.
**Youxi remarks:** Having bathed in the oversight of the divine perfected, one forever relies upon the grace of ascent. Above, the thirty-two heavens are passed; below, the nine dark realms are informed. At this time, the rejoicing is beyond words.

We beseech the eradication of the Three Evils and the severance of the roots of the earthly.
**Dong states:** The Three Evils are the three paths. The first is sensual desire, the second is craving, and the third is greed—these are the Three Evil Gates. The "roots of the earthly" refers to hell. We beseech the eradication of the path of the Three Evils and the severance of the roots of hell.

We fly through the Five Gates and inscribe our names in the Great Mystery.
**Dong states:** The Five Gates are the five paths of rebirth, as previously explained, now reiterated. The first is the suffering of the mind from sensual burdens; the second, the suffering of the spirit from craving; the third, the suffering of the body from greed; the fourth, the suffering of essence from floral competition; the fifth, the suffering of the soul from bodily burdens. One exits through the gate, hence called "gates." The Great Mystery is the Great Mystery Capital. Humans, endowed with nature and harmonious *yin-yang*, free from desires and untouched by the Three Evils or Five Desires, fly through the gates of the Five Sufferings and ascend directly to the palaces of the Mystery Capital.
**Youxi remarks:** The Five Gates are the portals of the five paths. The five paths consist of the previous Three Evils with the addition of the paths of *qi* and humanity, totaling five. Having severed the tendencies toward the Three Evils and transcended the gates of the five paths, one’s name is stricken from the ghostly registers of Fengdu and inscribed in the immortal ledgers of the Great Mystery. The Great Mystery is the Nine Palaces of the Mystery Center, the realm of the Upper Clarity.

The demon kings oversee and recommend, unhindered at the gates of heaven.
**Dong states:** "Hindered" means obstructed. When one receives the demon kings’ protection and recommendation, one ascends directly to the Three Clarities, passes through the gates of heaven without obstruction, and roams freely in the Upper Clarity.
**Shaowei remarks:** The Heavenly Worthy bestows the celestial passport for ascent, and the demon kings protect and recommend it. At every gate of heaven, none dare obstruct or interrogate.
The *Divine Scripture of the Cavernous Spirit’s Celestial Passport* is the sixty-eighth character in the "Human Sovereign Text," inscribed on azure silk and worn on the body. On the day a Daoist ascends to heaven, without this passport, the Five Peaks will detain their soul and prevent their ascent.

Without this passport, the rivers and seas will detain one’s blood and fluids, preventing their ascent. Without this passport, the Earthly Officials will detain one’s form, preventing their transcendence. Without this passport, the Heavenly Officials will bar the gates of heaven, preventing their advance. The officers and soldiers at the gates of heaven demand and inspect the passport; once obtained, one proceeds directly into the Purple Court of the Great One, meets the Lord of the Great Dao, and thereafter all spirits dare not detain or restrain them.

The Eastern Dipper governs lifespan, the Western Dipper records names.
**Dong states:** In the Heavenly Center of the Eastern Flower, there is the Terrace of Scattered Blossoms, where the Four Dipper Perfected govern, overseeing the recording of lifespans and merits of life and death. Those with merit have their names recorded by the Western Dipper.
**Youxi remarks:** The Eastern Dipper is the first star of the Dipper, governing the augmentation of lifespan. The Western Dipper is the second star of the Dipper, governing the recording of merits and names.

The Northern Dipper casts down death, the Southern Dipper elevates life.
**Dong states:** The Southern and Northern Dippers govern life and death. Those with good deeds are reported by the Three Officials, and the Southern Dipper delivers them from the trials of the Three Realms, rescues them from the sufferings of the Nine Darks, and proclaims to the demon kings, preventing them from disrupting the practitioner’s evil deeds. The Three Officials then report to the Northern Dipper, which commands the demon kings to seize the person’s soul and consign it to the servitude of the Nine Darks for ten thousand kalpas, eternally mired in evil affinities. At that time, without good deeds or response, the Northern Dipper removes their name from the register of death, and the Southern Dipper inscribes their name in the register of life.
**Youxi remarks:** The Northern Dipper is the sixth star of the Dipper, governing the removal of names from the register of death. The Southern Dipper is the fifth star of the Dipper, governing the inscription of names in the register of life.

The Central Dipper, the Great Chief, oversees all spirits.
**Dong states:** *Kui* means great; *ling* means spirit. Within the Dipper resides the Spirit Youth, named Yu Fu, who constantly revolves the Wheel of Great Non-Being, turning the Ten Cycles to summon the Perfected. He governs the celestial passes of the ten directions. The Ten Cycles refer to the Great Saints of the ten directions ascending to the Jade Palace; when the myriad spirits and lofty perfected gather, Yu Fu intones.
**Youxi remarks:** *Kui* means chief. The Central Dipper is the seventh star of the Dipper, the head of the Four Dippers, overseeing all spirits of the body. These Five Directional Dippers are the five stars of the Northern Dipper, governing the five directions. Since they are Dipper stars, they are referred to as the Eastern Dipper and Western Dipper, not that each direction has its own Dipper.
**Shaowei remarks:** This clarifies that the Dipper lodges of the five directions each receive their offices from the Primordial Beginning. The seven lodges of the Eastern Direction govern lifespan; the seven lodges of the Western Direction record people’s transgressions; the seven lodges of the Northern Direction cast down names from the register of death; the seven lodges of the Southern Direction inscribe names in the register of life; the Central Direction refers to what people now call the Northern Dipper. The *Treatise on the Celestial Offices* states: "The Dipper is the Emperor’s chariot, revolving at the center, overseeing the four quarters, and examining portents." Zhang Heng’s *Spiritual Constitution* also says: "One resides at the center, thus it is known as the Dipper. The Dipper is the Central Ultimate." Since the people of the Divine Continent dwell south of the Ultimate, gazing northward, it is called the Northern Dipper and Northern Ultimate. In discussing this, it is truly akin to the royal mandate being issued to the four directions, thereby revealing the heart of heaven. It speaks of the Central Dipper as the great commander of *qi*, overseeing all spirits, life and death, transgressions and blessings.
**Commentary states:** The *Oral Instructions of the True One* says: "Within the Dipper itself are five Dippers: Yang Brightness is the Eastern Dipper, Yin Essence is the Western Dipper, Cinnabar Prime is the Southern Dipper, the Northern Ultimate is the Northern Dipper, and the Celestial Pass is the Central Dipper." This may not be the case. Now, the Eastern Dipper refers to the seven lodges of the Eastern Direction—Horn, Neck, and others—whose office is Lesser Yang, governing the calculation of lifespans, and where people inscribe their merits and names. The Western Dipper refers to the seven lodges of the Western Direction—Legs, Bond, and others—whose office is Greater Yin, governing the recording of people’s good names. The Northern Dipper refers to the seven lodges of the Northern Direction—Dipper, Ox, and others—whose office is also Greater Yin, and which also governs death, thus removing names from the register of death. The Southern Dipper refers to the seven lodges of the Southern Direction—Well, Ghost, and others—whose office is Greater Yang, and which also governs life, thus inscribing names in the register of life. The Central Dipper refers to the seven lodges such as the Chief and others, the so-called Central Dipper that oversees the Four Dippers and all matters of spirits, life and death, transgressions and blessings.

The Azure Emperor guards the *hun*-soul, the White Emperor attends the *po*-soul, the Vermilion Emperor nurtures *qi*, the Black Emperor circulates blood.
**Dong states:** The Lord Azure Emperor’s surname is Yan, personal name Kai Ming, style Ling Wei Yang, and he constantly governs the *hun*-soul. The Lord White Emperor’s surname is Shang Jin, personal name Chang Kai, style Yao Po Bao, and he constantly governs the *po*-soul. The Lord Vermilion Emperor’s surname is Dong Fu, personal name Ji Yan, style Chi Biao Nu, and he governs the expansive yang *qi*, residing in the Mansion of the Heart. The Lord Black Emperor’s surname is Hei Jie, personal name Ling Hui, style Yin Hou Ju, and he governs blood and *qi*, presiding over the kidneys.
The Perfected of the Upper Clarity state: The Lord Azure Emperor’s surname is Chang, personal name Jing Ming; the Lord White Emperor’s surname is Hun, name *Cao Ru Shou*; the Lord Vermilion Emperor’s surname is Yan, personal name Dong Dan; the Lord Black Emperor’s surname is Xuan, personal name Ming Meng.
**Youxi remarks:** The Azure Emperor’s position is in the East, governing Wood, overseeing the liver, where the *hun*-soul is stored, hence he guards the *hun*-soul. The White Emperor’s position is in the West, governing Metal, overseeing the lungs, where the *po*-soul is stored, hence he attends the *po*-soul. The Vermilion Emperor’s position is in the South, governing Fire, overseeing *qi*, and since *qi* is born of Fire, he nurtures *qi*. The Black Emperor’s position is in the North, governing Water, overseeing blood, and since blood returns to Water, he circulates blood.

The Yellow Emperor, central sovereign, is not surpassed by the myriad spirits.
**Dong states:** The Lord Yellow Emperor’s surname is Tong Ban, personal name Yuan Cheng, style Han Shu Niu, and he governs earthly *qi*, residing in the spleen.
The Perfected of the Upper Clarity state: His surname is Ma, personal name Zhong Shen.
**Youxi remarks:** The Yellow Emperor resides at the Golden Flower Mountain in the Heavenly Center, where the Five Emperors hold court.

The Five Emperor Divine Kings govern within their palaces, ever generating clouds of five colors, with the sun and moon flanking their sides, and flying immortals winging their chariots. The Five Emperors in Heaven preside over flying immortals; on Earth, they are enthroned upon the Five Peaks, governing ghosts and spirits; within humans, they rule the five viscera, presiding over the five spirits. The liver stores the *hun*-soul, the lungs store the *po*-soul, the heart stores *qi*, the kidneys store blood, and the spleen resides in the central palace, governing the flesh. Thus, humans emulate Earth, Earth emulates Heaven, Heaven emulates the Dao, the Dao emulates spontaneity, and spirits have their proper abode—hence it is said there is no transgression. The triad unites to perfect their virtue.

**Shaowei states:** This clarifies that the Five Elder Emperor Lords each receive the vermilion-script talismanic mandate. In Heaven, they govern the divine immortals of the five directions; on Earth, they govern the spirits and ghosts of the Five Peaks; within humans, they govern the spirits of the five viscera. Each has its proper governance, so there is no transgression. The sequence of decrees is fully set forth in the Perfected Writ.

The Azure Heaven Demon King is Bayuan Choubo.
**Dong states:** The Azure Heaven Demon King’s surname is Bin, personal name Chichengba. The Azure Heaven Demon King was born together with the Primordial Beginning, commanding the Nine Heavens. Choubo is also a Demon King of the Three Realms, presiding over their midst. If cultivators recognize his name, they enjoy blessings; if they fail to recognize it, they suffer calamity. Those who gain the Demon King’s protection ascend bodily into the Three Clarities.

**Youxi remarks:** This pertains to the Azure Emperor. The first four characters denote his title, the next two his personal name, and the last two his style. The rest follow this pattern.

The Vermilion Heaven Demon King bears Heaven and shoulders stone.
**Dong states:** The Vermilion Heaven Demon King’s surname is Fu, personal name Yousu. His might can lift the sky, his strength can topple mountains. He soars through the Three Realms, obstructing human merit and subduing the host of demons.

**Youxi remarks:** This pertains to the Vermilion Emperor.

The White Emperor Demon King overturns mountains with six eyes.
**Dong states:** The White Heaven Demon King’s surname is Chi, personal name Zhangshi. With one head and six eyes, he can shatter mountains and overturn stones, commanding the ghostly spirits of the Six Heavens and severing the paths of human rebirth.

**Youxi remarks:** This pertains to the White Emperor.

The Black Heaven Demon King is Jianchou Langfu.
**Dong states:** The Black Heaven Demon King’s surname is Xu, personal name Zhishi. His nature is fierce and ugly, delighting in slaughter.

**Youxi remarks:** This pertains to the Black Emperor.

The Yellow Heaven Demon King spans Heaven with his strength.
**Dong states:** The Yellow Heaven Demon King’s surname is Tianmen, personal name Bokuang, the Great Demon King. His body is clad in a robe of dark patterns, his head crowned with a Heaven-spanning diadem, his waist girded with a dragon-headed sword. He ever rides a feathered-wheel chariot, flying amidst the clouds.

They often compose ballads and songs of three thousand words, confounding and corrupting later students. The Most High therefore recorded their melodies in the *Precious Scripture for Dispelling Demons*.

**Youxi remarks:** This pertains to the Yellow Emperor. His position, title, and name are the same as the Azure Emperor, for he presides over the protection of Dao-seekers and the expulsion of demonic trials.

**Shaowei states:** Next are the demonic spirits who disrupt the destinies of the ordained, executing the patriarchs of lineages. Those called "Heavenly Demon Bodies" were all, in former lives, diligent in precepts, almsgiving, and vigorous cultivation—yet could not bear the success of others, and thus reaped this retribution.

The Five Thearch Demon Kings are the ancestors of the myriad spirits.

**Dong states:** The Azure Emperor Demon King’s surname is Poluo, personal name Wanxing. The Vermilion Emperor Demon King’s surname is Zhe, personal name Shangbai. The White Emperor Demon King’s surname is Deng, personal name Xuer. The Black Emperor Demon King’s surname is Xiao, personal name Gongsun. The Yellow Emperor Demon King’s surname is Wangong, personal name Chansheng. Each commands an official retinue of thirty-eight thousand, born together with the Six Heavens. They govern the Three Realms, their merit equal to that of the heavens, and serve as the ancestors of ghosts and spirits.

**Youxi remarks:** These Five Directional Heavenly Thearchs and Five Heaven Demon Kings together govern all the deities of the Five Heavens and Five Directions—hence they are called "ancestors."

They fly with drumming retinues, commanding ghostly armies.

**Xuanying states:** This describes the Five Thearch Demon Kings, who constantly lead ghostly troops in flight through the Great Void, their retinues resounding with drumming and music—hence "flying with drumming retinues."

Waving banners and beating drums, they roam and observe the vast firmament.

**Dong states:** Their ghostly and divine attendants bear curved canopies and banners of five colors—mystic yellow and dark—flying amidst the clouds, surveying the ten directions, circling through the boundless sky.

**Youxi remarks:** The Flying Celestial Numinous Demons ride the void and harness the floating, leading and following with ghostly troops, bearing banners and staffs, striking drums and brandishing pennants. They enter and exit the true realms, traversing the vast firmament.

**Shaowei states:** The *Hidden Writ of Jade Purity* says: Each of the Five Emperor Demon Kings wears a tiger-headed pouch, commands an official retinue of thirty-eight thousand, and is born coeval with Heaven. They constantly harass and disrupt students. Though they do not desire the Way’s fulfillment, they vaunt themselves as equal in sagely merit to the Heavenly Thearchs. Later, during the Dragon Han era when charts were revealed, they submitted to the transformation of the Primordial Beginning. Thus the *Hymn of Pacing the Void* says: "The Demon Kings respectfully receive their duties, and thus can ascend to the heavens."

**Xuanying states:** When the Great Sage travels, all ranks of his regalia and adornments are arrayed. The *hui* (pennant) derives its meaning from pointing and beckoning, with feathers affixed to the top of a pole, resembling a banner. Kings wield it to swear oaths, while those who administer oaths proclaim the commands and covenants—akin to a ruler issuing decrees today. The *chuang* (banner) resembles a flag or canopy. The *gujie* (drums and staffs) refers to the rhythmic music of drumming and piping. This describes the Five Heaven Demon Kings, each leading their legions, erecting banners, pennants, drums, and staffs, roaming and observing the Great Void. Their mounted retinues throng together, indulging every whim. They style themselves as resplendent and majestic, their merit equal to that of the heavens.

**Dong states:** Their attendants are resplendent, their majesty complete, their power rivaling that of the heavens—hence "equal in merit."

**Xuanying states:** Having arrayed such majesty, they further proclaim themselves resplendent and exalted, esteeming their own nobility.

When the heavens deliver humanity, they strictly govern Fengdu in the north.

**Dong states:** The Demon Kings, ruling the Three Realms from the Mystic Capital, constantly inspect the ghostly registers of Fengdu in the north, tallying the karmic debts of the dead. The above concerns the Mystic Capital’s protection of those worthy of deliverance.

**Youxi remarks:** Since they lead and follow with banners, drums, and staffs, they style themselves as resplendent. Yet they also assist in the deliverance of students, restraining and subduing demonic trials—thus their merit equals that of the heavens. *Hexi* describes their august and flourishing appearance.

**Shaowei states:** When the Heavenly Worthy delivers humanity in the Celestial Azure Heaven, he summons the Northern Thearch to proclaim to the Demon Kings, commanding them to behead and exterminate demonic spirits, forbidding them to inflict calamities. In every kalpa when humanity is delivered, the decree remains thus.

The Divine Duke receives the mandate and universally sweeps away inauspiciousness.

**Dong states:** The Divine Duke is the Prime Minister of the Great Luo Heaven, named Kuoyi, residing in the Terrace of Primordial Yang. He oversees the deliverance of divine and human beings across the great thousand worlds, ascending them to the Hall of Boundless Merit, expelling inauspiciousness and evil. At that time, he receives the Heavenly Worthy’s talismanic mandate to sweep away the essences of the myriad demons and inauspicious ghosts, rescue those bound in the Three Bureaus, deliver the guests of rebirth, establish life registers in the Vermilion Palace, sever the roots of death for nine generations, bestow luminous blessings upon perfected beings, dispel the dark nights of ten thousand kalpas, and grant rebirth through the Divine Duke.

**Youxi remarks:** The Divine Duke is the Divine Duke of the Great Luo. "Receiving the mandate" refers to the command to subdue the Five Thearch Demon Kings, enabling him to protect students and sweep away inauspiciousness.

The Eight Awes spew poison, fierce steeds gallop in four directions.

**Dong states:** The Eight Awes are the dragon scales, tiger leopards, lions, cinnabar serpents, heavenly horses, and ferocious beasts—their poison spewing in four directions.

**Youxi remarks:** The Eight Awes are the divine dragons of the Eight Awes. The fierce steeds are the celestial swift horses of the spirit realm. The divine dragons spew poison to subdue demonic vapors, while the swift steeds charge forth to pursue evil spirits.

Heavenly Ding advance as vanguard, great marshals wield banners.

**Dong states:** The Heavenly Ding are the Five Ding warriors. The great marshals are the generals who supervise killing and punishment. They lead heavenly troops with ceremonial canopies and banners, their majestic regalia arrayed before and behind, exterminating inauspiciousness and annihilating demonic and ghostly evils.

**Youxi remarks:** The Heavenly Ding are the armored soldiers of Heavenly Zou, hence they lead the advance to drive away evil. The great marshals are the demonic ghostly marshals, hence they wield banners to repel and expel.

Hurling fire for ten thousand leagues, ringing bells through the eight directions.

**Dong states:** The flowing golden fire bells on the left and right, when hurled, blaze for ten thousand leagues. Their radiant light interweaves through the eight directions, filling the empty void to dispel demons and annihilate ghosts.

**Youxi remarks:** The hurling of fire and flowing bells refers to the flowing golden fire bells. When cast, they resound through the Great Ultimate, their radiance shaking a thousand leagues. Thus, their blazing light extends for ten thousand leagues in interwoven splendor, surging through the eight directions in a crashing strike. The Perfected Ones constantly wield them to subdue and command demonic essences.

**Shaowei states:** As the *Dongzhen Sutra* says: "The fire bells possess radiance but no substance; with a single cast, they span ten thousand leagues. Should any dare to test them, they will be fiercely repelled by the Supreme Perfected." **Dong adds:** The myriad demons conceal their forms, and the hundred ghosts dare not resist. "Giant" here means resistance.

**Youxi remarks:** It means they do not repel the Supreme Perfected. Those who hold this scripture are thus counted among the Supreme Perfected.

**Execution with metal and iron proceeds ahead, while the Giant Heavenly Ones mete out punishment behind.**
**Dong states:** The *yue* resembles an axe. The Giant Heavenly Ones are the Heavenly Ding force-soldiers. Thus, metal *yue* and axes execute ahead, while the Giant Heavenly Ones wield blades to punish behind. "Metal" is also a general term for iron; some say the *yue* are adorned with gold, hence called "golden *yue*." It is also said that the Heavenly Ding force-soldiers execute ahead and behead behind to eradicate demonic and ghostly essences.

**Shaowei states:** If any ghosts or spirits dare to act recklessly, unleashing harm to obstruct our Supreme Perfected, the Heavenly Ding are dispatched to execute them ahead and behead them behind.

**Slaughtering ghostly souls, wind and fire never cease.**
**Dong states:** "Slaughtering" means to rend and shatter. "Souls" refers to the hun. "Wind and fire" are the wind-blades and fire-mountains. Ghostly souls are rent and shattered upon the wind-blades and fire-mountains.

**Youxi remarks:** Slaughtering the souls of ghosts and severing the essences of demons—swift as the wind, rapid as fire—hence it is said that wind and fire never cease.

**Severing a thousand thousand heads, shearing ten thousand ten thousand forms.**
**Dong states:** "Heads" are the skulls; "forms" are the bodies. Of the myriad sinful ghosts and souls, their heads are struck off, their bodies dissected and flayed.

**Youxi remarks:** "A thousand thousand, ten thousand ten thousand" expresses their multitude, not a fixed number. Some have their heads struck off, others their forms dissected. This is because where there is truth, there is falsehood; where there is goodness, there is evil. Thus, falsehood can obstruct truth, and evil can corrupt goodness.

**Demons dare not trespass, ghosts dare not manifest their malevolent essences.**
**Dong states:** The hundred demons cower in concealment, the myriad malevolent spirits lose their essences. Having slaughtered essences and severed souls, then struck off heads and flayed forms—how could any dare to trespass, or presume to offend again?

**Youxi remarks:** By wielding this mighty punishment to eradicate ghostly and demonic foes, the hundred demons are forced into hiding, and the host of malevolent spirits lose their essences.

**The Three Officials of the Northern Fengdu scrutinize the ghostly encampments.**
**Dong states:** The Three Officials are the Celestial, Terrestrial, and Aquatic Officials. The Northern Fengdu is the Northern Bureau for the Investigation of Treachery. Within the Nine Bureaus of Fengdu, there are nine divisions for investigating treachery. There are also the Nine Envoys of the Nine Capitals, originally nine beasts born from the nine *qi* after the final kalpa of the Dragon Han, who harmed the wicked. Once the kalpa unfolded, the nine beasts were renamed the Nine Ugly Ghosts. The Supreme Perfected of the Northern Emperor reside above Fengdu, establishing the Nine Ugly Ones to assist the Three Officials. Their numbers reach eighty-one myriad, measuring the celestial *qi*. The Nine Ugly Ones exchange titles to become the Nine Envoys of the Nine Capitals, constantly inspecting the Three Officials and Nine Bureaus. The souls of the good and evil cannot conceal themselves.

**Youxi remarks:** The Three Officials are the Three Officials of the Six Palaces, which lie above the Northern Fengdu. The Three Officials govern the host of ghosts, thus they are ordered to guard the encampments and domains, preventing them from trespassing against those who study the Dao.

**No concealment is permitted; the Golden Horse Post reports in haste.**
**Dong states:** The Golden Horse is the Golden Dragon. To inspect good and evil, the post-horses gallop swiftly to report the matters.

**Youxi remarks:** If any attempt to conceal or hide, the Golden Horse Post immediately arrives to report. The Golden Horse is said to be as unyielding as a vajra steed, hence the term "Golden Horse Post reports."

**Shaowei states:** Fearing their might, the ghostly encampments are openly scrutinized. Should any flee or hide, daring not to conceal themselves, each post and dragon-gate swiftly reports, hastening to present the matter—as with the time limits of post-horses in the mortal world.

**Universally proclaimed without end, the myriad spirits all heed.**
**Dong states:** Universally proclaimed to all divine spirits above and below heaven and earth, all are made to listen and submit.

**Youxi remarks:** From heaven above to heaven below, from the hidden to the obscure, all proclamations near and far are universally heeded.

**The Three Realms and Five Emperors, their names listed in the Supreme Clarity.**
**Dong states:** When the Divine Lords receive their mandate, they universally proclaim to the divine kings of the Three Realms and Five Emperors, and all spirits, releasing the evil and opposing dead souls from the earthly prisons. Their names are all listed in the Supreme Clarity.

**Youxi remarks:** The Three Realms are the demon kings of the Three Realms; the Five Emperors are the Five Emperors and the Great Demon, their names listed together. They are summoned to protect and deliver the students, ascending to the gates of the Supreme Clarity to present themselves before the Most High.

**Shaowei states:** The Divine Lords, steadfast and upright, universally proclaim without end. The Five Emperors and myriad spirits all come to heed their commands.

**The demonic armies are already vanquished; their names are listed and presented to the Supreme Clarity.**

**Xuanying states:** The Three Realms refer to the realms of desire and form among the heavens. *The Wondrous Scripture of the Supreme Ultimate for the Salvation of All Beings, with Four Commentaries, Volume Two* concludes here.
*Volume Three of The Wondrous Scripture of the Supreme Ultimate for the Salvation of All Beings, with Four Commentaries* begins.

The *Primordial Cavern Jade Chronicle*, Dong states: "Primordial" refers to the Primordial Beginning; "Cavern" means to penetrate. "Jade" signifies the jade script; "Chronicle" means to record. The Primordial Beginning condensed the essence of spontaneity, forming the eight-cornered, radiant script. The Mysterious Cavern pervaded the void, its light illuminating the four directions. The Two Modes divided, and the sun, moon, and stars thereby arrayed their brilliance. Treasured by all sages, it was named the *Jade Chronicle*, recording the kalpas of heaven and earth and reckoning the celestial reckonings. The Perfected Ones inscribed its affairs, compiling them into scripture—hence it is called the *Jade Chronicle*.

Shaowei states: The *Primordial Cavern* refers to the Primordial Lord of Heaven coalescing the primordial qi of the Cavern of True Perfection into the *Jade Chronicle*, to record meritorious deeds and inscribe the nine ranks of immortals. From the nine ranks of immortals, one ascends to the nine Perfected, and thence to the nine Sages, only then transcending the Three Realms, roaming freely in the Supreme Clarity, merging with the Dao in truth, forever immune to descent.

**Dragon Han and Yan Kang.**
Dong states: "Dragon" signifies the numinous; "Han" means great. The jade script first appeared, emerging to instruct the perfected, displaying divine marvels—thus it was named the Hall of Great Blessings, the Abode of Everlasting Joy in the Land of Felicity. Vast and boundless transformation was called the Dragon Han. "Yan" means long; "Kang" means peace. When the Dragon Han kalpa ended, the celestial jade script concealed its radiance, the sun and moon extinguished their light, heaven and earth plunged into darkness, indistinguishable—long-lasting tranquility, thus named Yan Kang.

Youxi states: The *Primordial Cavern Jade Chronicle* is the name of the celestial Cavern’s chronological records. *Dragon Han* and *Yan Kang* are the designations of kalpas in the boundless, obscure past. The Yan Kang kalpa preceded the Dragon Han—these are the two past kalpas.

Shaowei states: This chapter discusses the formation and dissolution of kalpas. *The Mysterious Record of Mount Gui* states that the *Primordial Sovereign of the Cavern* is qi. The Heavenly Worthy condensed the qi of the Primordial Cavern into the *Jade Chronicle*. This chronicle takes the Dragon Han kalpa as the first kalpa; the kalpa of the unfolding chart is called the Red Brightness kalpa, and its end is called the Yan Kang kalpa, cycling endlessly, concluding only to begin anew. "Yan" means long; "Kang" means peace. After a kalpa ends, the Three Realms become empty wastelands, the spirits of all beings abide in the Great Void in long-lasting peace—thus Yan Kang is the designation of the kalpa of dissolution, while Red Brightness is the name of the kalpa of unfolding. The alternation of these two constitutes the Great Kalpa, and thus all endings are called Yan Kang. The intervening unfolding is typically called Red Brightness. The remaining kalpas—*Primordial Sovereign* and *Supreme Sovereign*—are names of lesser kalpas. *The Numinous Chapters* states: The Dragon Han inherits the Yan Kang realm to inaugurate its era; Red Brightness unfolds its light, and heaven and earth resume their positions. This refers to the Yan Kang and Red Brightness following the Dragon Han.

Xuanying states: "Primordial" signifies the root and origin; "Cavern" signifies the empty and boundless. Jade is the most precious of treasures; "chronicle" takes its name from reckoning. This clarifies that the Primordial Lord of Heaven used this true script to record the great reckonings of past kalpas and their endings. As this true script is precious and its reckonings reliable, it is treasured and preserved—hence called the *Jade Chronicle*.

**In the boundless kalpas of the primordial chaos,**
Dong states: "Boundless" means lofty and distant.

The term "亿" (yì) denotes ten thousand myriad. As for "劫" (kalpa), as previously explained in the chapter on the Primordial Jade Characters sinking into the Yan Kang, one sinking spans a kalpa of myriad eons—truly a number as countless as grains of sand. "混" (hùn) means "to merge"; before heaven and earth were distinguished, all was chaos as one.

Youxi states: These two kalpas stretch so distant and remote that their reckonings defy all measure, shrouded in profound obscurity within the primordial darkness.

Shaowei states: Since the kalpa of the Ancestral Beginning, the kalpas have been as innumerable as dust and sand, impossible to recount in full—thus we speak broadly of "myriad kalpas." When the reckoning of myriad kalpas reaches its end, all returns to chaos, yet the essence and spirit of the myriad beings remain within.
