The *Scripture of the Dragon’s Leap* states: When the kalpa of the Three Realms collapses, chaos reigns without form. With each kalpa’s renewal, the Three Qi serve as its foundation. Above, there is no longer azure light; below, there are no longer abyssal depths.

Dong states: "Color" refers to the azure radiance; "abyss" refers to depth. The accumulation of emptiness forms azure; the accumulation of rivers forms abysses—thus heaven is high and azure, water is deep and abyssal, and human essence is spiritual. Heaven possesses the Three Lights to bestow illumination; earth possesses the Three Rivers to receive streams; humans possess the Three Palaces to house the spirit. When humans attain proper principle, heaven and earth are at peace, and the Yan Kang era arrives—then heaven no longer bears azure light, and all becomes chaos at once.

Youxi states: With the end of each kalpic cycle, the Three Lights darken, and the world of heaven and earth returns to primordial chaos. The Dao reverts to its root source, and the myriad beings lose their unity—then what azure light remains above, or what abyss below?

Shaowei states: At the end of each kalpa, the Twenty-Eight Heavens above are extinguished, leaving no radiance; the Nine Ramparts and Thirty-Six Earths below are exhausted, leaving no springs.

The Wind Marsh pervades the void; the Vajra bears up heaven.

Dong states: The Wind Marsh is the qi of the Primordial Beginning’s Brahma-wind. "Pervades" means to penetrate; "void" means nothingness. "Vajra" signifies truth; "strong" signifies firmness. The qi of the Wind Marsh is firmer than true metal—hence called the "Vajra Wind." Enveloping the Nine Ramparts and supporting the Nine Heavens, it permeates the void, lifting the essence of the limpid Han, floating high and unbounded, suspended yet unfallen. The true qi of the Vajra upholds heaven, governing the emptiness to sustain its suspension, while earth is bound to the Vajra qi.

Youxi states: The Wind Marsh is the qi of the Dao; the Vajra is the qi of essence. The qi of the Dao is supremely yielding, thus it pervades the void; the qi of essence is supremely firm, thus it forms the heavens. The kalpas unfold naturally, and the celestial realm endures—though without light, it is still called "heaven."

Shaowei states: The Wind Marsh is the qi of the Eighth Rampart. The qi of the Wind Marsh is as hard and firm as metal—hence called "Vajra" or "Vajra Wind." At the end of a kalpa, it fills the empty void, bearing up heaven without collapse.

According to the *Inner Tone of the Nine Earths and the Numinous Cinnabar Scripture*: Twenty billion myriad li beneath the earth lies the Moist Marsh Earth, its qi yellow; another twenty billion myriad li below lies the Firm Marsh Earth, its qi purple; another twenty billion myriad li below lies the Great Wind Marsh Earth, its qi azure. Beyond this stretch boundless depths—without end, without limit, without edge—forming the Nether Abyss Framework Earth, its qi green. All are sustained by the Brahma-wind’s framework. This qi upholds the earthly wheel, suspending it without fall. Each of the Nine Ramparts has Four Sovereigns, totaling Thirty-Six Sovereigns, corresponding to the Thirty-Six Heavens above. If a practitioner does not know the Inner Tone of Heaven, the Heavenly Emperor will not recognize their name; if they do not know the Inner Tone of Earth, the Earthly Sovereigns will not record their register—thus they remain forever barred from attaining immortality.

Between heaven above and earth below, there is no obscurity, no darkness, no form, no shadow, no limit, no end.

Dong states: "Obscurity" means distant; "darkness" means near. Between heaven above and earth below, there is no height or depth, no far or near—all is indistinct and dark. "Form" refers to heaven and earth; "shadow" refers to the Three Lights. "Limit" means exhaustion; "end" means termination. Heaven and earth have no form; sun and moon have no light—exhausting the inexhaustible, ending the unending.

Youxi states: Above heaven, there is no obscurity or darkness—it is unfathomable; below heaven, there is no shadow or form—it is unobservable. Existing between above and below, its end cannot be known; its limit is but the self-so, naturally independent.

The Primordial Darkness of the Great Brahma stretches boundless and vast, without light.

Dong states: "Primordial Darkness" means distant and enduring; "Great Brahma" refers to qi. "Vast" means empty and remote. When the Primordial Beginning sinks into the Yan Kang, the Primordial Darkness endures, vast and empty, for myriad kalpas without light.

Youxi states: The "Great Brahma" is the Great Dao. The qi of the Great Dao is darkly mysterious and undifferentiated—hence called the realm of Primordial Darkness and emptiness. Vast and indistinct, it has not yet brightened—hence said to be without light.

Shaowei states: Such is the state at the end of a kalpic cycle. Above the Three Realms and below the Four Peoples, there is no obscurity or darkness, no form or shadow, no limit or end—only the vast nothingness of the Great Brahma, the boundless expanse of Primordial Darkness, and the original light of the Three Radiances.

Xuanying states: "Primordial Darkness" describes the unfathomable emptiness; "vast" means distant and boundless; "expansive" means empty and without edge. This clarifies that within the Three Realms, there is no light of sun or moon—only the qi of the Great Brahma, filling the Great Void with Primordial Darkness and boundless vastness. Hence it is said to be vast and without light.

This describes the transition from the Yan Kang of the previous kalpa to the beginning of the Dragon Han of the present kalpa, when the Two Modes had not yet emerged, and chaos was undivided, with the Brahma-qi flowing through the void. Next comes the era of Red Brightness unfolding its destiny, as detailed below.

The Chart of Red Brightness unfolds; the kalpic reckoning proceeds naturally.

Dong states: "Red" signifies fire, the qi of the Primordial Beginning’s ninefold refinement.

"Opening" means to initiate; "chart" means image. Within the Yan Kang kalpa, the Primordial Beginning initiated the era of Red Brightness. Thereupon, in the Chanli world, the Most High and Great Sagely Jade Emperor refined the True Script with fire, causing radiant light to emerge, jade essence to flow, and forming the Cavernous Yang Palace. All things took form, and it was named Red Brightness.

Master Youxi states: At this time, the Red Script of True Text unfolded the brilliance of its chart and register, setting in motion the division and measure of yin and yang. Heaven thereby illumined the Three Luminaries, and earth thereby gave birth to the myriad things. Thus we know that heaven and earth have their cycles of formation and decay, not merely the initial unfolding of creation at this time. Thereafter, the four seasons succeeded one another, and the myriad transformations nurtured and reared—yet none knew their source, hence it is called "natural." For this reason, it was named the kalpa of Red Brightness.

Master Shaowei states: From this point onward, the kalpic reckoning of the Bright Era was to be fulfilled. The True Script refined by fire was thus named Red Brightness; the progression of kalpic measure followed the principle of naturalness.

Master Xuanying states: This clarifies the initial unfolding of the kalpic reckoning, succeeding the era of Dragon Han, when the cosmos was arrayed and the governance of the Three Luminaries established. "Red Brightness" refers to the True Script of the Jade Calendar from before. The Primordial Heavenly Worthy refined it with fire, and the True Script, luminous and crimson in hue, was thus named Red Brightness. With this True Script, heaven and earth were arrayed, the transformations of qian and kun were set in motion, and the Three Luminaries followed their constant measure—each according with the principle of naturalness, not the work of artificial craft. "Reckoning" means movement; "measure" means number. The *Red Script* states: The kalpic reckoning completes a full cycle of day and night in thirty days, forming one conjunction; twelve conjunctions make one degree. Three thousand three hundred degrees constitute a minor kalpa, and nine thousand nine hundred degrees a major kalpa. The *Chapter on the Generation of Spirits* further states: One degree corresponds to one year. The Primordial Beginning established and guarded the fivefold scriptures, spreading and placing them throughout.

Master Dong states: "Established" means to set up; "guarded" means to preserve; "spread" means to distribute; "placed" means to position. The fivefold scriptures are the jade characters of the Red Script.

Master Youxi states: "Spread" means to extend; "placed" means to expand. Thereupon, the Primordial Beginning, with the jade characters of the Red Script, extended the True Text, establishing the root of heaven and guarding the source of earth. He spread and placed the colored positions of the five directions, molding and casting the implements of yin and yang, extending the transformations of the Primordial Beginning—nothing was left unprepared. The jade characters of the Red Script are the Eight Might Dragon Script.

Master Dong states: Once the True Text received refinement by fire, it was named the *Red Script*. The *Eight Might* refers to the Eight Might Jade Tablets; the *Dragon Script* is the script for summoning dragons. The Primordial Beginning established the Five Marchmounts, arranged the fivefold scriptures, and stationed the True Text in the five directions, with the Five Emperors guarding them. He regulated spirits and summoned dragons to avert the appointed time of kalpic reckoning.

Master Youxi states: The *Red Script* is the fivefold True Text. The jade characters are the innate inner sounds. The Eight Might Dragon Script and the like are true talismans transmitted to the highest perfected. They regulate the kalpic reckoning, ensuring the heavens endure long.

Master Dong states: The Primordial Beginning established and guarded the Five Marchmounts, founding the roots of heaven and earth to repel all disasters; he regulated spirits and summoned dragons to extend the kalpic reckoning. Heaven, though high, does not topple; earth, though heavy, does not sink. From beginning to end, all stands firm—thus it endures long.

Master Youxi states: This Red Script, true talismans, and dragon scripts all serve to regulate and govern the kalpic reckoning, dispelling its adversities and endings, ensuring heaven and earth endure long without collapse.

Master Shaowei states: The *Red Script* is the fivefold True Text. The *Jade Characters* are the numinous writings of the Eight Assemblies and the Eight Might Jade Tablets. They command the might of eight kinds of beings, hence the name. The *Dragon Script* is the script for summoning dragons. At the outset of the Primordial Beginning’s practice of the Dao, he established the Red Script in the five directions, distributed the jade characters across the thirty-six heavens, employed the jade tablets to command the myriad spirits with might, and used the dragon scripts to summon dragons and safeguard the kalpa—thus heaven endures long without collapse.

The Brahma-qi pervaded and encompassed all, and the myriad patterns unfolded.

Master Dong states: "Brahma" refers to the qi of the Great Brahma. "Pervaded and encompassed" means to embrace all. "Pattern" means form. The Primordial Beginning raised the qi of the Great Brahma, initiating the era of Red Brightness, and heaven, earth, and the myriad things all received form at once.

Master Youxi states: Once the Primordial Beginning had established the two images and spread the fivefold scriptures, and further employed the jade characters and dragon scripts to regulate the kalpic reckoning, he then distributed the true Brahma-qi throughout the ten directions and unfolded the mysterious transformative script across the cosmos—thus all kinds under heaven arose in unison, touching all things.

Master Shaowei states: The Brahma-qi spread and filled all, molding and casting the myriad forms—curved and straight, square and round—each with its own pattern. The Primordial Net flowed and extended through the thirty-two heavens.

Master Dong states: The "Primordial Net" refers to the guiding principles of the Primordial qi, spreading through the thirty-two heavens.

Master Youxi states: "Primordial" refers to the stars; "net" refers to the stellar net. Once the Two Modes became bright and clear, and the Three Luminaries shone together, the stars arrayed themselves in flowing motion, illuminating the thirty-two heavens above; the sun and moon alternated in brightness, illuminating the hundred million worlds below.

Master Shaowei states: "Primordial" means great; "extended" means to spread. The Brahma-qi serves as the great guiding principle for the myriad things, flowing and spreading through the thirty-two realms. It revolves without form, circling through the ten directions.

Master Dong states: "Without form" means without shape. "Ten directions" refers to the eight directions plus above and below, making ten. The qi of the Great Brahma spreads everywhere without exception.

Master Youxi states: Its wheeling light illumines the Three Realms, circling and shining through the ten directions—thus no darkness remains unlit, and all things are illuminated. "Without form" refers to the realm above the Three Realms.

The Dipper revolved and the Winnowing Basket traversed.

Master Xuanying states: "Revolved the Dipper" means the name for turning; the Dipper and Winnowing Basket are star names among the twenty-eight lunar lodges.

The Dipper star resides in the northeast above the northern quadrant. "Traversing the Winnowing Basket" means *li* (历) as in "to tread." The Winnowing Basket star lies in the northwest above the eastern quadrant, hence the annotation: "The Dipper and Winnowing Basket stars flank the northeast corner." This clarifies how the qi of the Great Brahma flows and spreads, arising from the Whirlwind Terrace in the northeast corner. Its qi spirals upward like ram’s horns, moving leftward from the east toward the south, first passing through the Winnowing Basket star—thus called "traversing the Winnowing Basket." From the south it turns west, from the west it turns north, crossing through the Jiaoyi and Huangzeng heavens, then circling back eastward, passing through the Dipper star, and returning to the Whirlwind Terrace. This marks one full revolution of the Brahma qi through the heavens, nurturing the myriad things and accomplishing the work of a year—hence "revolving the Dipper and traversing the Winnowing Basket." The annotation states: The Jiaoyi Heaven lies to the left of the Horn star. The Horn star is positioned in the east, while the Jiaoyi Heaven is in the west; the Brahma qi moves leftward from east to west into the Jiaoyi. Jiaoyi is the supreme position among the thirty-two heavens, thus said to be "to the left of the Horn." Huangzeng lies to its right: Huangzeng is the first position among the thirty-two heavens, situated to the right of the Winnowing Basket star, thus marking the beginning of the Winnowing Basket’s domain. "Beginning of the Winnowing Basket" means the Brahma qi commences its movement from the Winnowing Basket star—hence "beginning of the Winnowing Basket." The meaning of "revolving the Dipper and traversing the Winnowing Basket" is roughly as such.

It revolves and measures the Five Constants.
Master Dong states: The Dipper is the Northern Dipper. The Winnowing Basket is the Winnowing Basket lodge. "Revolves and measures" means to circulate and guide. The Five Constants are the Five Phases. This refers to the natural qi circulating and guiding the Five Phases.
Master Youxi states: It turns the seven luminaries in the northern quadrant, following the sun and time with the Dipper’s handle pointing, traversing the revolutions of the Winnowing Basket and Net lodges, weaving through the measures of the Five Constants. The Five Constants are the five planets. The Winnowing Basket and Net are among the twenty-eight lunar lodges.
Master Xuanying states: This clarifies how the Brahma qi flows and spreads, coiling through the thirty-two heavens, revolving and circulating the qi of the Five Constants—thus the four seasons follow in order, transforming and generating life. The Five Constants are the Five Phases: metal, wood, water, fire, and earth. If arranged sequentially, wood belongs to the east, fire to the south, earth to the central palace, metal to the west, and water to the north. These Five Phases, in generating and completing the myriad things, all depend on the work of the Brahma qi, forming the constant Dao of heaven and earth—hence "revolving and measuring the Five Constants."

Thirty-five divisions, the primordial qi unites in the Upper Origin.
Master Dong states: The thirty-five divisions refer to the thirty-five heavens. "Divisions" means domains; "unites" means to govern. *Qi* is the primordial qi of the Origin. The Upper Origin is the supreme, luminous, and formless Dao of the Origin, governing all immortals, encompassing heaven and earth, dividing yin and yang, circulating the Five Phases, bestowing positions upon the heavens. Once the Three Images were separated and the nine-tiered terrace shone forth in brilliance, it abided on the Jade Capital Mountain, resplendent above the Dark Metropolis. Flying immortals perpetually scatter incense of a hundred harmonies and stream the blossoms of five clouds to bathe the perfected ones. Upon the terrace stands the Great Perfected Jade Youth, thrice daily unfurling the Ten Absolute Banners. With each full circuit, all heavens ascend to pay homage, circling the terrace thrice while reciting and chanting the cavernous scriptures. The thirty-two heavens are arrayed in the four directions, eight heavens to each direction, totaling thirty-two. Three heavens enclose them above, and above the Great Enclosure all is empty and vast, where five natural mists gather, their color azure-yellow, called the Yellow Heaven. Above the Yellow Heaven, its hue deep blue, is called the Azure Heaven. Above the Azure Heaven lies the Dark Void, where accumulated emptiness forms a green hue, called the Green Heaven. Altogether there are thirty-five heavens, each with its own domain, all governed by the primordial qi of the Origin and the supreme Dao—hence "the primordial qi unites in the Upper Origin."

The thirty-five divisions refer to the thirty-five stars.
Master Youxi states: The thirty-five divisions are the sun, moon, five planets, and twenty-eight lodges combined, totaling thirty-five. However, the twenty-eight lodges each comprise multiple stars, and the sun and moon are not stellar in nature, so they cannot be called thirty-five stars—thus termed thirty-five divisions. "Divisions" means positions, all receiving the qi of the Upper Origin. The Upper Origin is the source from which all are endowed.
Master Shaowei states: The Dipper and Winnowing Basket stars flank the northeast corner. The Jiaoyi Heaven lies to the left of the Horn, marking the domain where the Dipper revolves. The Huangzeng Heaven lies to the right of the Horn, marking the domain where the Winnowing Basket begins. The Brahma qi first arises from the Whirlwind Terrace in the northeast, spiraling upward like ram’s horns, circling leftward and rightward, traversing the Winnowing Basket and revolving the Dipper to complete its course. Coiling through the thirty-two heavens and revolving the qi of the Five Constants, the four seasons transform, and the myriad things take form. The *Taiyi Yijue* states: "Incense smoke arises naturally, the dark steps ascend the whirlwind." This describes the Brahma qi emerging from the Whirlwind Terrace like incense smoke.
Master Xuanying states: The thirty-five divisions are the boundaries of the thirty-five heavens. The Three Realms contain twenty-eight heavens, and the Northern Dipper’s seven stars each govern a heaven, making thirty-five heavens. The Northern Dipper’s Yang Brightness, Yin Essence, Cinnabar Prime, and North Culmen stars govern four heavens of the seed people. The Dark Obscurity, Perfected One, and Celestial Pass stars govern the three highest heavens, totaling thirty-five heavens. The three highest heavens are the Jade Clarity, Upper Clarity, and Grand Clarity. Another account holds that the Three Terraces’ three stars govern the three highest heavens, together with the preceding thirty-two heavens, forming the thirty-five heavenly divisions. "The primordial qi unites in the Upper Origin" means the Upper Origin is the Supreme Jade Clarity Dark Metropolis. It clarifies how the Brahma qi flows and spreads, revolving the Dipper and traversing the Winnowing Basket, pervading all thirty-five heavens.

Its qi ascends into the Upper Clarity Heaven, converging entirely within the precincts of the Dark Metropolis—hence it is called "the primordial qi unites in the Upper Origin." The Eight Effulgences merge in darkness, and qi enters the Profound Profundity.

The Eastern Master says: "The Eight Effulgences are eight colors. 'Merge in darkness' means penetrating the body with the qi of the Dao." "Profound Profundity" signifies the abstruse and recondite.

The Most High Dao Lord rides the jade chariot of the Eight Effulgences, urging the three-pure flying clouds, ascending above the Dark Metropolis and the Six Harmonies Terrace. He discloses the arcana of the Primordial Beginning and expounds the Great Dharma to deliver humankind. When qi reaches the subtlest mystery, the body of the Dao becomes spontaneous.

Master Youxi says: "In sum, they are called the Eight Effulgences. The twenty-eight lunar lodges are arrayed in the four directions, seven stars to each quarter. The lodges of the four directions, together with the sun, moon, five planets, and Northern Dipper, combine to form the eight effulgent qi, which naturally merge in darkness. The merged effulgent qi all enter the Profound Profundity. This 'Profound Profundity' is the Profound of the Upper Origin. Having first received the qi of the Upper Origin, the qi then returns to enter the Profound. The Profound is where the qi of above and below interflow, so the radiance of the numinous stream never ceases."

Master Shaowei says: "If one attains the Dao, the spirits of the Three Passages and Eight Effulgences merge indistinguishably, jointly raising the adept’s body to ascend above the layered heavens. 'Profound Profundity' refers to the heavens beyond heavens."

Master Xuanying says: "The Eight Effulgences are effulgent lights. The Upper Origin’s primordial qi forms one effulgence, and the seven luminaries combine to make eight. The seven luminaries are the sun, moon, and five planets. 'Merge in darkness' means that these eight entities, their lights and effulgences merging indistinguishably, illumine the myriad heavens—hence it is called 'merge in darkness.' Another explanation holds that the Eight Effulgences are the eight colors of the heavenly lights. 'Qi enters the Profound Profundity' means that the preceding Great Brahma qi, revolving and circulating, ascends into the Most High Heaven—hence it is called 'qi enters the Profound Profundity.' 'Profound Profundity' describes the boundless and infinite height. If a worldly person attains the Dao, the spirits of the Eight Effulgences jointly raise the adept’s body to ascend above the layered heavens. The 'layered heavens' are the heavens above the heavens of the various heavens, that is, the precincts of the Upper Clarity Dark Metropolis."

Within the Profound dwells the Grand August, the Celestial Emperor, and the Lofty Perfected.

The Eastern Master says: "The Grand August is named Yi Miao, who has come from the Dragon Han and emerged in the Crimson Brightness. He abides amid the primordial opening, within the void, roaming the vast expanse, dwelling in the silent court. His divine effulgence and jade splendor stand as the standard of the myriad Dao."

Master Youxi says: "The preceding 'Profound Profundity' is the Supreme Profound within the Profound. Here, 'within the Profound' refers to the realm of the Two Voids and Three Precincts. The Two Voids are the Great Void and the Hollow Void. The Three Precincts are Jade Clarity, Upper Clarity, and Grand Ultimate. The Grand August dwells in Jade Clarity, the Celestial Emperor in Upper Clarity, and the Lofty Perfected in the Grand Ultimate. Whenever one is called 'August,' it is a title of the Celestial Worthy, equal in rank to the Primordial Beginning—examples include the Supreme August, Lofty August, Void August, and Jade August. The Celestial Emperor is the Lord of the Grand Tenuity, the most exalted of the thirty-six celestial emperors. The Lofty Perfected is the most exalted title of the Yellow Elder of the Central Grand Ultimate."

Their effulgences drift upon the grand auroras, and they chant the cavernous chapters.

The Eastern Master says: "To 'drift upon effulgences' means to roam and soar. The 'grand auroras' are qi. They fly upon the mysterious qi and recite the cavernous scriptures, harmonizing with the qi of spontaneity to deliver those who study the Dao."

Master Youxi says: "To 'drift' means to float. 'Effulgences' means bodies. This describes the movements of these Three Worthies: they soar their bodies amid the clouds, drifting upon effulgences in the empyrean, and when they open their mouths, they intone the verses of the cavernous chapters and chant the lofty scriptures. The 'cavernous chapters' are the chapters of the Great Cavern; the 'lofty scriptures' are also names of chapters within the cavernous scriptures."

Master Shaowei says: "The Grand August is the Void August Dao Lord. The Celestial Emperor is the Celestial Emperor of the Golden Portal. The Lofty Perfected is the third-rank perfected. In the Upper Clarity Heaven stands the mountain of Void Effulgence, where the qi of grand auroras abides. The Void August Celestial Emperor and this Lofty Perfected ride the jade chariot of the Eight Effulgences, flying above the grand auroras, chanting the cavernous scriptures to receive adepts."

Golden perfection shines resplendently, its echoes flowing through the cloud encampments.

The Eastern Master says: "The 'golden perfection' is the spontaneous scripture. The divine beings of the Brahma Heaven fly and roam above the Grand Ultimate, singing the boundless celestial hymns. They stir the numinous winds of the spirit, wafting and spreading the melodies of the cavernous chapters. The Jade Maidens of Grand Harmony at the Gate of the Flowery Metropolis harmonize with the divine beings’ songs, their echoes flowing through the palaces of auspicious clouds—hence it is called 'cloud encampments.'"

Master Youxi says: "The 'golden perfection' is the golden perfection of jade light, which is the effulgence of the Celestial Worthy’s body. 'Resplendently' describes the radiance. 'Encampments' means congealing and gathering. Since they drift upon the grand auroras, the golden perfection shines brilliantly, and they intone the verses of the cavernous chapters amid the coalescing clouds and mist."

Master Shaowei says: "The 'golden perfection' is the golden-slip perfection scripture. Long ago, the perfection scripture first appeared, coalescing in the mysterious void, gleaming with radiance and inscribed upon golden slips—hence it is called 'shining resplendently.' The 'cloud encampments' are the cloud palaces. The Hundred Jade Countenance Hall stands upon Dragon Mountain in the Dark Metropolis. It speaks of the Celestial Emperor chanting the golden slips, his pure voice resonant and bright, flowing into the cloud palaces."

Master Xuanying says: "The 'golden perfection' is the perfection scripture inscribed upon gold. 'Shining' means the scripture’s characters are bright and clear. 'Resplendently' describes the brilliance. The 'cloud encampments' are the name of the Hundred Jade Countenance Hall within the Dark Metropolis, which stands upon Dragon Mound Mountain. 'Flowing echoes' clarifies that when the host of sages chant, their voices resound through the cloud encampment palaces—hence it is called 'flowing echoes through the cloud encampments.'"

The jade tones gather qi, and the numinous winds assemble mist.

The Eastern Master says: "The 'jade tones' are the jade-light scriptures. The flying divine beings of heaven constantly ride the azure auroras’ brushes, soaring through the Jade Exaltation Heaven."

At the three daily hours, the great sages of heaven are led to ascend and pay court at the Seven Treasures Palace. The Heavenly Kings offer their rejoicing, striking jade chimes and sounding the dawn. With a single cry from the attendant of the morning, the numinous winds gather the mist.

Once the numinous winds stir, their tones form the Cavern Scripture.

Master Youqi says: "The 'jade tones' are the chanting voices of the Supreme August High Perfected. When the Supreme August chants, the jade tones crown the heavens to gather qi, and the numinous winds arise from the void to assemble the mist."

The Purple Void flourishes in radiance, aiding and sheltering the myriad immortals.

The Eastern Master says: "The 'Purple Void' is the Purple Tenuity Palace. 'Flourishing' means vigorous; 'radiance' means emerging. The Purple Tenuity’s halls flourish and emerge above the Jade Clarity Heaven. Within it lies the Sarana Palace, where those newly attained to the Numinous Treasure reside—countless multitudes. Their merits not yet complete, they remain dispersed therein. When the kalpa’s turn arrives, the throngs of Mount Tu assess the weight of their merits and ascend to the Vermilion Numinosity Palace to receive blessings and rise as immortals, thereafter becoming perfected transcendents."

Master Youqi says: "The Middle Origin of the Jade Clarity Heaven is named the Purple Clarity, hence it is also called the Purple Void. Though these three honored ones each serve as the origin of a single realm, all belong to the ranks of the Jade Clarity. Moreover, the Perfected of the Dao all ascend to the Jade Clarity. The Purple Void’s palace naturally flourishes in radiance, and with the myriad immortals’ luminous wings, it enhances the brilliance of the host of sages."

Master Shaowei says: "The 'Purple Void' is the Purple Tenuity Palace, also named the Sarana Palace. Its halls are majestic and flourishing. Within dwell the throngs of Mount Tu—countless multitudes, all newly attained. As the time of destiny has not yet arrived, they remain dispersed therein. When the kalpa’s turn comes, the Three Divisions, Eight Effulgences, and Twenty-Four Perfected will assist and aid them, ascending to the Southern Palace to receive their immortality."

A thousand harmonies, ten thousand unions—naturally perfected as true.

The Eastern Master says: "'Harmony' means dissolution; 'union' means gathering. Since the Perfected began their cultivation, they have passed through countless kalpas, dissolving forms and altering bodies, relinquishing one vessel to receive another, revolving with the kalpa’s cycles. From the coarse they enter the subtle, tempered by the jade gaze, and only then do they become true."

Master Youqi says: "If the practitioner of recitation harmonizes with a thousand Perfected and unites with ten thousand Dao-qi, the true merges with the spirit, the body of the Dao unites with qi, and naturally they become true."

Master Shaowei says: "Those who ascend all establish three thousand virtuous deeds, with the ten thousand practices perfected. Only then do the Three Bureaus review their records, allowing them to ascend to the Southern Palace. Nourished by the Great Harmony, tempered by the jade nectar, they pass through harmonies and unions, and only then do they become true."

Within the true resides the spirit—the Great Lord of Longevity.

The Eastern Master says: "Within the Longevity Palace dwells the Lord of Longevity."

Master Youqi says: "Having united with the true, the body contains the true, and within the true resides the spirit—this Great Lord and the subsequent deities are such."

The Great Lord resides in the Life Gate Palace below the navel, also called the Hall of Brightness.

Master Shaowei says: "This speaks of the original spirit of the attainer. 'Within the true' refers to the Southern Perfected Palace. The 'Great Lord of Longevity' is the Lord of Life Extension, whose name is Xu Yuan, who presides over the preservation of the decaying body."

The Lordless Duke and the White Prime Honored Spirit.

The Eastern Master says: "The Left Lordless is named Duke; the Right White Prime is named Dongyang. They are called the Specialized Spirits."

Master Youqi says: "The Lordless and White Prime are the names of two spirits, both dwelling in the Cavern Chamber Palace. The palace lies two inches directly within the space between the brows. The Lordless also resides in the liver at times, also called Duke. The White Prime also resides in the lungs at times. 'Honored Spirit' is an emphatic reference to the White Prime, not a separate title."

The Great One, Controller of Destiny, and the Peach Prosperity and Union Longevity.

The Eastern Master says: "The Great One is named Wu You Shou; the Controller of Destiny is the Celestial Controller of Destiny, named Li Ming Chu. Peach Prosperity is the spirit of the Life Gate."

Master Youqi says: "The Great One is also the Great Lord. The Great Lord is the honored one among the hundred spirits of the body and the master of the ten thousand qi, hence called the Great One, also named the Great Lord. The 'Controller of Destiny' governs life, also called the Controller of Destiny. The two spirits Peach Prosperity and Union Longevity share names with the Great Lord, but this is an interchangeable reference, not strictly accurate."

Master Shaowei says: "The Great One is named Wu You Shou; the Controller of Destiny is named Xuan Du Qing; the Peach Lord is named Hui Hai; the Prosperity Lord is named Jing Yan."

Master Xuanying says: "The Great One governs all offices as the master of the host of spirits. The Controller of Destiny and other Perfected officials are all positions within the Southern Ascension of the Attainer’s bureaucracy."

Holding talismans and grasping registers, they preserve life and root its origin.

The Eastern Master says: "The Duke holds the talisman; the Controller of Destiny grasps the register. The Great One subdues demons, and with the Cavern Scripture, they ascend the attainer to the Longevity Palace."

Master Youqi says: "The Great Lord constantly holds the eight talismans to preserve human life and root its origin."

Master Xuanying says: "This clarifies that when the attainer achieves the Dao, the Duke is commanded to hold the talisman of the Primordial Beginning’s Ascension of the Attainer; the Controller of Destiny’s palace grasps the register of the attainer’s name; the Great One governs the restraint of the host of demons. Together, they elevate the practitioner, preserving life and rooting its origin."

Ascending to the Upper Clarity, entering and exiting the Flowery Chambers.

The Eastern Master says: "The 'Upper Clarity' is the Purple Tenuity Palace."

The Purple Tenuity resides above the Jade Clarity. The "Flowery Chambers" are the Supreme Ultimate Palace, which has the Azure Flower Gate, and within lies the Curved Chambers.

Master Youqi says: "These spirits originally dwell among the gods of the Upper Clarity’s Great Tenuity Palace. They divide and descend their qi, entering the human body, thus at times ascending back to the Upper Clarity, exiting and entering the Flowery Chambers—the chambers of the Great Tenuity. Within the Eight Darknesses, amid the subtlest of the subtle."

The Eastern Master says: "The 'Eight Darknesses' are the Eight Poles. The 'subtlest of the subtle' refers to the tip of a hair. This speaks of advancing beyond the Eight Poles and within the tip of a hair."

Master Youqi says: "The 'Eight Darknesses' lie beyond the Eight Poles, obscure and unfathomable—hence called the Eight Darknesses. These spirits are so vast that nothing lies beyond them, so minute that nothing lies within them. They may expand throughout the Eight Darknesses or penetrate the tip of a single hair. In humans, they become the Dao; in things, they become life—the qi of the Dao-nature. Below, they guard the human body, settling in the Mud-Pill Palace and the Crimson Palace."

The Eastern Master says: "The Mud-Pill is the brain. The Crimson Palace is the heart. The Heavenly Venerable resides in the Upper Clarity Palace, known as the Great One Lord. Below, within the human body, he becomes the Lord of the Mud-Pill. As the *Scripture of Unfolding the Scripture and Treasuring the Incantation* states: 'Though the Heavenly Venerable is distant and wondrous, he is near through the Lord of the Mud-Pill.' This is what it means."

Master Youqi says: "This clarifies how they guard within the human body, some in the Mud-Pill, others in the Crimson Palace. The Mud-Pill lies three inches inward from the space between the eyebrows; the Crimson Palace is the heart. They regulate the Five Qi and harmonize the Hundred Spirits."

The Eastern Master says: "The Five Qi are the qi of the Five Viscera. The Hundred Spirits are the Hundred Passes. 'Harmonize' means to blend, to regulate the Hundred Passes and unite the spirit and qi."

Master Shaowei says: "The Flowery Chambers are the Three Flowery Chambers of the Jade Clarity. The Eight Darknesses are the Eight Poles. The 'subtlest of the subtle' refers to the tip of a hair. The Mud-Pill is the brain; the Crimson Palace is the heart. These true spirits, with the Great One as their master, roam the Three Clarities, exiting and entering the Three Flowery Chambers, circling within the Eight Poles, and pervading the tips of hairs. When they guard the human body, the Great One resides in the brain, governing all spirits; the Controller of Destiny dwells in the heart, receiving the origin of life. The Non-Beginning is in the liver, governing the Three Hun; the White Prime is in the lungs, restraining the Seven Po. The Peach Lord resides in the navel, preserving the root of essence; the Extending Health dwells in the kidneys, guarding the Gate of Life. Within the Hollow Cavern, they regulate the qi, harmonize the Hundred Spirits, manifest auspicious numinous texts, and in accordance with the kalpas, deliver people. As the *Book of Changes* states: 'The spirit has no direction; the Changes have no form—this is what is meant by the unfathomability of yin and yang.' Thus, the spirit is nowhere absent, and wherever it is, it is nowhere. It cannot be known by wisdom, nor can it be defined by being or non-being. Some hold that within the human body, each has these spirits. Upon examining the various scriptures, the principles are not uniform.

According to the *Heavenly Elder’s Secret Prognostication*: 'Among spirits, there are ranks of honor, and the Great One is the most noble. Above, it guards the Three Clarities; below, it roams the Nine Palaces.' The *Cavern Spirit Scripture* states: 'The Great One is named Wu You Shou, styled Gui Hui Chang, and governs all heavens and earths—its spirit is the most revered. Its form is black above and red below, and it wears the Heaven-Piercing Crown, its eyes gazing straight ahead. If one constantly contemplates it, one will attain long life and never die.'

The *Jade Scripture of the Great Cavern* says: 'The Controller of Destiny receives the Emperor’s writ and is titled the Dark Deliverance Minister. Its form is white above and blue below, with a perfectly round face.'

The *Record of the Three Primes of the Cavern Spirit* states: 'The Three Prime Lords are the Three Prime Lords of the Great Simplicity. One is a woman whose head has three cloud-like topknots, with the rest of her hair hanging loose to her waist. She wears a floating-morning crown and robes, a purple floating-cloud brocade sash at her waist, and a nine-colored dragon brocade feathered skirt, with a belt bearing flowing-gold fire bells and tiger talismans. Beneath her knees, she emits red, green, and blue qi. The Three Prime Lords give birth to the Three Simplicity Prime Lords: the eldest daughter, the Purple Simplicity Prime Lord, gives birth to the Non-Beginning; the middle daughter, the Yellow Simplicity Prime Lord, gives birth to the Yellow Elder; the youngest daughter, the White Simplicity Prime Lord, gives birth to the White Prime. The Yellow Elder, White Prime, and Non-Beginning are called the Three Prime Emperor Lords. The mother of the Emperor Lords is called the Three Simplicity Prime Lords—these are the Three Prime Lords. After years of devoted practice and austerities, the Three Primes descend to the chambers, and the Three Simplicity Jade Maidens arrive first. If one studies the Dao without knowing the Three Primes, one’s cultivation will be ineffective. These Three Primes are all natural spirits, born together with the Primordial Beginning. When ten thousand people together invoke the true qi, each has its corresponding spirit.'

Ten revolutions return the numinous; the myriad qi ascend as immortals.

The Eastern Master says: "The 'myriad qi' are the myriad spirits. When the Lord of the Mud-Pill recites the scripture ten times, all spirits ascend as immortals. The Three Offices and Six Palaces, along with all the spirit-officials, each lead their hosts of a hundred million chariots and ten thousand riders, transforming in majestic splendor, with grand processions of cloud-riding and dragon-mounted escorts. Together, they elevate the human body, and all the hundred officials and spirit-officials likewise ascend as immortals."

Master Youqi says: "The 'ten revolutions' refer to the ten revolutions of the Heavenly Pass. When one person attains the Dao, the Heavenly Pass revolves ten times, returning the hundred spirits to complete the nature and transforming the myriad qi to ascend together as immortals."

Master Shaowei says: "Gathering those seven spirits, they compassionately pity the multitudes, revolving through the ten directions to deliver living beings, desiring that the myriad qi flow and all attain the immortal Dao. The immortal Dao values life and delivers boundlessly."

The Eastern Master says: "The 'boundless' refers to the revered gods among the hosts of great sages. In the heavens, there are boundless hosts of great sages, all governing the flying immortals of the ten directions, who receive their ranks and ascend accordingly. The 'deliverers of people' are the flying immortal spirits. At the first crow of the rooster, they ascend to the Jade Terrace above and the Immortal Hall within, gathering the essence of the five-directional cloud sprouts and reverently swallowing the light of the sun, moon, and three luminaries. They constantly review the registers of life and death of those who study immortality, deliver the souls of the Nine Dark Regions, and raise them into the Gate of the Dharma Wheel."

Those who study this method can spur the divine wind to swift as smoke, ascending to the work of the soaring forest, so that the seven ancestors emerge from the palace of the eternal night and ascend to the palace of renewed life.

The Lesser Florescence says: "What the immortal Dao values lies solely in life. Thus, the boundless deliverance of people cannot be reckoned."

Above, the Eight Gates open—the Dharma Wheel of the flying immortals.
Sin and blessing, prohibitions and admonitions, past lives and karmic conditions.

The Eastern Master says: "The Eight Gates are the eight directional gates of the Dharma Wheel in heaven. Within them lies the realm of sin and blessing. The Most High Dao Lord opens the Eight Gates to deliver the souls of those who study the Dao from life and death. Thus, it is called the Dharma Wheel."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Once one attains deliverance in life, the Demon King opens the Eight Gates of the Dharma Wheel to deliver them. The student then naturally ascends, unbound by the gates of heaven."

The Lesser Florescence says: "The Eight Gates of sin and blessing are governed by the flying immortals. Thus, it is called the Dharma Wheel of the flying immortals. The Dao Lord questions sin and blessing at the Eight Gates, while the flying immortals recount past lives and explain the roots of karmic conditions, all of which are detailed in the *Dharma Wheel Sutra*."

Universally receiving deliverance, the dead soul revives in a living body.

The Eastern Master says: "The Dharma Wheel’s gates are the realm of sin and blessing, each with its prohibitions. The origins of sin and blessing are all recorded in the *Dharma Wheel Sutra*. The Most High Dao Lord, in his great compassion, extricates the souls bound by past karmic debts from hell, examines their sins, then pardons and releases them, allowing them to enter the Dharma Wheel’s gates. They ride the chariot of the Eight Effulgences, ascend to the Jade Purity, and pay homage at the Purple Tenuity Palace, attaining the rank of honored guests among the sagely hosts—this is what is meant by the dead soul reviving in a living body."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "The seven ancestors gave rise to this one body, fostering these five karmic deeds. Now that this body has received deliverance, the five deeds naturally vanish, and the seven ancestors refine and transform to be reborn. The five deeds fall away rootless. Thus, it is said that all universally receive deliverance, looking up to bear the grace of liberation. The body attains rebirth and is heard above by the various heavens."

The Eastern Master says: "Heard means opened. The body attains rebirth and opens the various heavens above. Above the various heavens, each has its Gate of Life."

The Eastern Master says: "Within the Eight Gates, each has its Gate of Rebirth."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Once the living body receives deliverance and the dead soul is reborn, the Three Realms and Five Emperors ascend to serve the various heavens. Above the various heavens, they are recorded in the register of life. Thus, it is said that each has its Gate of Life."

The Lesser Florescence says: "When the dead soul is reborn, it is reported to the various heavens. Above the various heavens, each has its Gate of Rebirth. Then the Three Offices review and record them, assigning them to their destined places of rebirth. Within these are the hymns of the Empty Cavern, the numinous chapters of the Demon King, and verses that match the lofty perfected ones."

The Eastern Master says: "The Empty Cavern refers to the Three Realms—all is empty within the Three Realms. The Demon King is Mara, who dwells within the Three Realms, singing wanton songs and verses that disrupt the human heart. The numinous youths turn the locks of the Eight Gates, and the assembled perfected ones ascend to pay homage. At a single resonant chant, the Demon King is bound. Those who recite the numinous verses have their names inscribed in the Dharma Wheel of the Purple Tenuity Palace, listed in the registers of the Life-Commanding Office. They awaken, deliver souls, and ascend to the palace of renewed life."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Once the Demon King has safeguarded and escorted them above the various heavens, there are hymns sung within those heavens. Their verses align with the lofty perfected ones, resonating with the principle of the Empty Cavern. Reciting them leads to immortal ascension—thus, they are called the numinous chapters."

The Lesser Florescence says: "Within the Three Realms, above the Empty Cavern, the Demon King submits and transforms, singing hymns. The numinous chapters and virtuous verses harmonize with the true sages."

The first is the Desire Realm, the sound of flying through emptiness.

The Eastern Master says: "The Desire Realm extends from the Yellow and Growing Heaven to the Six Heavens of the Upper Brightness and the Seven Luminaries of Māyā—this is the domain of the Desire Realm. Within it dwells the Demon King named Yu Mo, who sings the song of flying through emptiness."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "The first is the Desire Realm, the lower realm. It refers to the world above this one, hence it is called the first. Desire means attachment. Realm means boundary. The Desire Realm has six heavens, where the people of these heavens have form and desire, clinging to things and becoming attached—thus, it is called the Desire Realm. The Demon King sings this hymn within the empty mystery of this realm—thus, it is called the sound of flying through emptiness."

The Lesser Florescence says: "The Daoist scriptures state: If a person’s oral karma is pure and they accumulate ten virtuous deeds, they may ascend to the heavens of the Desire Realm. The human realm is minute and fragmented; the immortal Dao is vast and obscure."

The Eastern Master says: "Minute and fragmented refers to the multitude of petty beings. Vast and obscure means dark and indistinct. The human realm exists among the petty, making success difficult. The immortal Dao is vast and obscure, difficult to comprehend—it cannot be seen. Thus, it is called vast and obscure."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Slight of eye is called minute—visible yet distant. Vast and boundless is called obscure—profound and unfathomable. The human realm cannot be governed by distant effort; the immortal Dao is dark and motionless, yet easily thwarted. The ghostly realm is joyful, facing the Gate of Human Life."

The Eastern Master says: "Joyful means delight. The Gate of Life is the life-gate of the Three Realms. The ghostly realm lies within the Three Realms, leading ghostly soldiers to obstruct human lives, wantonly killing people for their delight."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "The ghostly realm indulges the heart’s desires, following its nature and the world’s ways—thus, it is called joyful. This is the path to death, where life is daily lost. Life and death stand as opposing gates—thus, it is said to face the Gate of Human Life."

The Lesser Florescence says: "The ghostly realm delights in killing, acting violently in groups, constantly obstructing the Gate of Human Life. The Gate of Life is the gate of rebirth in the Three Realms. The heavenly Dao values life; the ghostly realm values death."

The Eastern Master says: "Values means favors. The heavenly Dao favors life; the ghostly realm favors killing."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "The Dao of divine immortals lies in long life and enduring vision, abiding in serene perpetuity. The Dao of malevolent ghosts, however, seeks to draw humans into the Great Yin, all ending in annihilation. The immortal Dao is ever auspicious; the ghostly Dao is ever inauspicious."

The Eastern Master says: "Those who favor life are auspicious; those who favor killing are inauspicious."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Since the immortal Dao is life, auspicious omens arise of themselves. Since the ghostly Dao is death, calamities respond of themselves."

The Lesser Florescence says: "The human realm lies below the Three Realms. The immortal Dao lies above the Three Clarities. The ghostly Dao resides in the Fengdu Six Heavens. The lofty and pure numinous spirits chant mournful songs, resounding through the vast firmament."

The Eastern Master says: "The Lofty One is the Heavenly King, named Alan, who ever rides the Wheel of Radiant Clouds, roaming the nine-tiered peaks, dwelling atop the Jade Towers. He recites luminous scriptures to summon demons—above, a sanctuary for immortals and perfected beings; below, a dwelling for ghosts and spirits. His chanting of sacred verses, mournful songs resounding, echoes through the vast firmament."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Though even the highest perfected sages, their numinous qi pure and luminous, still chant mournful songs in sorrow, resounding through the empty void—these are the hymns of the Five Sufferings."

The Mysterious Splendor says: "The preceding passage exhorts humans to attain the Dao; this passage extols the beauty of mournful songs, universally delivering boundless beings. These words make clear that the Lofty Jade Emperor, grieving for the Three Realms, ever chants these mournful songs atop the Three Clarities. His song resounds through the vast firmament, compassionately pitying the multitudes. Thus it is said: *mournful songs resound through the vast firmament.* The *numinous spirits* refer to the Jade Emperor’s essence, the swift and luminous qi. He wishes only for the immortal Dao to be fulfilled, not for the human realm to fall into destitution."

The Eastern Master says: "The Heavenly King, atop the cloud towers, chants boundless scriptures. Seeing that scholars below cannot transcend the trials of the Three Realms, he recites them to restrain demonic spirits. Demons and devils respond at once, binding themselves; hordes of ghosts prostrate before his seat. Thus he delivers the bodies of seekers, perfecting their utmost true Dao."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Destitution means extremity. The extremity of the human realm is its nobility. If the immortal Dao is fulfilled, then all wondrous gatherings converge, the sufferings of the Five Turbidities vanish of themselves, and the joys of the Three Clarities never end. Though the human realm may reach its extremity in glory, fleeting honors and myriad pleasures must yield to a single suffering that forever obscures them."

The Lesser Florescence says: "The Lofty Jade Emperor, pure and luminous in spirit, chants mournful songs that resound through the vast firmament, filling the heavens. He wishes only for the immortal Dao to swiftly be fulfilled, not for humans to endure destitution and suffering."

The Northern Capital’s winding Spring Palace holds a host of ten thousand ghosts.

The Eastern Master says: "The Northern Capital’s mountains are governed by the divine demons of the Six Heavens. Within lies the winding Spring Palace, where a multitude of ghosts dwells. The Six Heavenly ghosts are all fierce, violent, and hideous demons, ever seeking to kill humans."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "The Northern Capital lies within the Northern Dark Sea, the capital of the Northern Mysterious Supreme Emperor. Within it is the winding Spring Palace, the Palace of the Nine Dark Eternal Nights. As the great capital of ghosts, it harbors a host of ten thousand ghosts. Though we speak of ten thousand, how could there be only ten thousand? Know but one human, and you know the nature of ghosts. They ever seek to obstruct human destiny, severing the Gate of Life."

The Eastern Master says: "The demonic ghosts of the Six Heavens ever seek to obstruct and sever destiny, cutting off the Gate of Life, wishing humans dead."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "The principle of ghosts is ever to diminish human lifespan, wishing them an early end, severing the root of life, cutting off the Gate of Life. Thus it was said earlier: *the ghostly Dao values death, facing the Gate of Human Life.*"

Ah, the people chant the cavernous scriptures to subdue the Northern Fengdu.

The Eastern Master says: "Ah, the people—this is how the demon kings speak among themselves. They recite and chant the cavernous scriptures to summon the demonic ghosts of the Northern Fengdu, preventing wanton killing and harm. Those who transgress are executed, aiding the celestial governance."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Ah—who, who can chant these empty cavernous scriptures to subdue and govern the ghosts of Fengdu? Then there will be no fear of obstructed destiny, and the scourge of premature death will naturally cease. Luofeng is the name of a mountain in the Northern Capital. Bind and dispatch the demonic essences, behead and mutilate the Six Ghostly Peaks."

The Eastern Master says: "Bind means to restrain. *Guo* means to annihilate the hordes of demons in the Six Heavens. *Peaks* is the general name for demons. Thus the incantation to the Six Heavenly demonic ghosts says: *Tianpeng, Tianpeng, Nine Primes slay the youths*—this is what is meant. The demon king chants this verse to sweep away and annihilate the demonic essences."

The Recluse of the Dark Abode says: "Bind means to detain and record. Dispatch means to banish and expel. Behead means to sever the head. *Guo* means to cut off the ears. If one can chant these scriptures, then demons can be detained, banished, beheaded, and mutilated. The Six Ghostly Peaks are the six peaks of Fengdu Mountain, each with its own palace. As there are six palaces, it is called the Six Ghostly Peaks. Each palace spans a thousand *li* in circumference."

The Lesser Florescence says: "*Aren* is how the demon king refers to himself. Severing the head is called beheading; cutting off the ears is called *guo*. The Six Ghosts are the six demonic thieves of the Six Heavens. *Feng* speaks of their precedence. *Feng* means sharp and keen. The demon king says: *I receive the talismanic command, ever chanting the cavernous scriptures to govern Fengdu, binding and dispatching demonic ghosts. Those who act with malevolence are executed and eradicated.*"

The Mysterious Splendor says: "Truly, it refers to severing the left ear. When many ghosts are slain, from each body the left ear is cut off and presented to the demon king, demonstrating the number killed. The left ear pertains to yang, thus it is taken."

The qi of all heavens flows vast and clear; my Dao daily flourishes.

The Eastern Master says: "Vast and clear means pure and luminous. *Flourishes* means the demon king’s songs soar through the void, sweeping away demonic qi to accomplish his work. Thus it is said: *daily flourishes.*"

Dark Abode says: "Having bound and restrained the essence of demonic spirits and beheaded the ghosts of the Six Peaks, the true qi of all heavens flows unimpeded, and my Dao’s orthodox transformation flourishes ever more."

Lesser Florescence says: "Wielding this awe-inspiring punishment to behead demonic ghosts, the perverse qi of the Six Heavens is swept away, and the true Dharma of the Three Heavens prospers."

**Second Realm of Form: The Chapter of the Demon King**

Eastern Master says: "The Realm of Form extends from the Void-Transcending Equilibrium Heaven to the Great Peace Imperial Cliff Heaven, comprising twelve heavens—this is the division of the Realm of Form. The demon king’s taboo name is *Mo*; his style, *Luo*."

Dark Abode says: "The second Realm of Form is the middle realm, situated above the Realm of Desire—hence it is called the *second*. *Form* denotes material substance; *realm*, a bounded domain. The Realm of Form contains eighteen heavens. The beings of these heavens possess form but no desire—thus it is called the Realm of Form. Since the demon king governs this realm, this chapter is established for him."

Lesser Florescence says: "From the Void-Transcending Equilibrium Heaven to the Boundless Cloud-Vow Heaven, there are eighteen heavens in all, constituting the Realm of Form. The Daoist scriptures state: *With three hundred merits of pure and cool bodily conduct, one may be reborn in the Realm of Form.* The demon king’s taboo name is *Mo Luo*."

**Vast and Lofty, Radiant Qi Soars to the Four Quarters**
Eastern Master says: "*Vast and lofty* means high and distant. *Radiant qi* refers to clarity and luminosity. The qi of heaven is high and distant, pure and bright—thus it is said to *soar to the four quarters*."

Dark Abode says: "*Vast and lofty* means expansive and open. *Soars* means unfolds. The heavens of the ten directions are expansive and lofty, their luminous brilliance unfolding to the four quarters."

Lesser Florescence says: "*Soars* means ascends. My realm is vast and lofty, unfolding high and wide; the qi of Brahma shines brightly, ascending in all four directions."

**The Brahma-Conduct Heavens Encircle the Ten Directions**
Eastern Master says: "*Brahma* refers to the great Brahma qi. *Ten directions* denotes the flying celestial beings of the ten quarters. Riding the great Brahma qi, they traverse the Three Realms and roam the ten directions."

Lesser Florescence says: "When the great Brahma qi pervades all heavens, the immortals of the ten directions encircle them tenfold—hence it is said to *encircle the ten directions*. Such immortals are numberless; through my protection and deliverance, they attain the rank of great immortals. Thus it is said: *All proceed from my being.* I possess the cavernous scriptures—chanting them ten thousand times, one becomes an immortal. These are the very songs. The boundless great deities all proceed from my being."

Eastern Master says: "*Boundless* refers to the boundless great deities of the ten directions. Those who study the Dao alongside the demon king and attain realization all proceed from the demon king’s sponsorship to become perfected beings. Thus it is said: *All proceed from my being.*"

Dark Abode says: "*Brahma-conduct* denotes the conduct of the utmost truth. *I* is the demon king’s self-reference. The thirty-two heavens’ Brahma-conduct perfected beings, along with the boundless great deities of the ten directions, all proceed from my sponsorship to dwell in these heavens. I possess the cavernous scriptures—chanting them ten thousand times, one becomes an immortal."

Eastern Master says: "*Cavernous scriptures* are the demon king’s songs. If a disciple recites them ten thousand times, the demon king will sponsor their direct ascent to immortality. The Dao of immortals values deliverance; the way of ghosts is intertwined with it."

Eastern Master says: "The Dao of immortals seeks to deliver beings upward; the way of ghosts seeks to bring about their death. The two are intertwined, dragging one another into the evil destinies."

Dark Abode says: "I possess these cavernous scriptures—chanting them ten thousand times, all may ascend as immortals. The Dao of immortals values the deliverance of both form and spirit; the way of ghosts values the continuity of life and death. Deliverance uplifts one’s ancestors as well; continuity ensnares one’s descendants."

**Heaven and Earth Vast and Obscure, Foul Qi Billows**
Eastern Master says: "*Vast and obscure* means dim and indistinct. *Foul* means evil; *billows*, chaos. Heaven and earth are high and distant, all-encompassing. The pure dwell above; the turbid, below. Demonic essences and evil qi fill the void."

Dark Abode says: "Heaven is boundlessly high; earth, boundlessly vast. Foul qi constantly billows, pervading the great void."

**The Three Realms’ Joy—Transcend It to Abide Forever**
Eastern Master says: "The *Three Realms* are the Realm of Desire, the Realm of Form, and the Formless Realm. These are not the ultimate joy. Only by transcending the Three Realms can one attain the Dao of immortality, revolving with the kalpas yet free from birth and death—thus abiding forever."

Dark Abode says: "If the beings of the Three Realms are deluded by joy and dwell in it, their joy will end, and they will sink into degradation. If they awaken to the truth that joy is not true joy, they will transcend it and abide forever."

**Delivered Across My Realm, the Body Enters the Natural**
Dark Abode says: "If one awakens to the truth that joy is not true joy, they will not dwell in it but cultivate progress. Thus they are delivered across the perils of the Three Realms and enter the state of the Natural."

Lesser Florescence says: "Though the Three Realms bring joy, when merit is exhausted, one falls. Even if one’s lifespan equals the grains of sand, in the end, all must perish. This moment’s joy—how slight it is, owing to my grace."

Eastern Master says: "Having entered the Formless Realm, one attains this bliss. *My grace* is the demon king’s self-reference. You all proceed from my sponsorship to enter the ranks of immortals—thus it is said: *how slight it is, owing to my grace.*"

Dark Abode says: "Entering the state of the Natural, one abides in the true joy of the Natural. The joy of the Three Realms is illusory, revolving in delusion. This joy shares the name but differs in principle; beings diverge, and realms differ. All proceed from the demon king’s sponsorship to reach this domain of true joy—thus it is said: *how slight it is, owing to my grace.*"

Lesser Florescence says: "Only by transcending the Three Realms can one attain joy—thus it is said: *this moment’s joy—how slight it is, owing to my grace.* Through my protection and deliverance, one enters the Three Clarities—thus it is said: *owing to my grace.*"

**The Dragon-Han Eon Vast—How Can One Discern the True?**
Eastern Master says: "In the Dragon-Han eon, the Jade Script first emerged from the Great Blessing Hall Kingdom, and the sun and moon first shone."

The Primordial Beginning compiled the Jade Scriptures and issued the Dharma to deliver beings. The customs of that land were refined beyond naming; its people first attained governance, and rites and music flourished. Human lifespans reached thirty-six thousand years. In the vast transformation of the eon’s end, after the passing of the Yan-Kang era, it sank into an aeon of oblivion—so distant and boundless that its truth, though certain, was not empty. Without penetrating the profound and exhausting the subtle, none could recognize it.

Lesser Florescence says: "Having refined the body to become immortal and cultivated the mortal to attain sagehood, one departs suffering for joy and leaves death for life—thus one knows the numinous transformation of the Dao, whose wondrous efficacy brings this about. At the time of the Dragon-Han eon, when chaos had not yet divided, heaven had not yet arisen, and the void stretched boundless—how could one discern the true?"

Lesser Florescence says: "In the initial kalpa of the Dragon-Han, people were all simple and unadorned, content in their natural state, knowing no desires. Though vast and level, none could distinguish truth from falsehood. My realm abounds with trials, and thus truth and falsehood may be discerned. My realm is difficult to cross—hence the creation of the Cavern Scriptures."

Eastern Master says: "The demon king declares: 'Since the Dragon-Han eon, my merit and virtue have been most weighty, yet I have not attained immortality. Those who study the Dao superficially seek to cross my realm—truly, this is difficult.' Thus he sings this song to exhort learners, that they may recognize the true."

Lesser Florescence says: "This realm is difficult to transcend, not because the Cavern Scriptures cannot ferry one across. Therefore, the demon king established this text to guide and aid, for one relies both on the grace of elevation and the virtue of support."

Lesser Florescence says: "The demon hosts of my realm abound with illusions and deceptions, making it difficult to cross—hence the creation of the Cavern Scriptures. They transform and soar through the void to test your body."

Eastern Master says: "The demon king, within the boundless void, flies and sings ballads to test whether the hearts of learners are upright or not."

Lesser Florescence says: "Fearing that the pursuit of the Dao may not be earnest or the grasp of integrity firm, he manifests transformations in the void to observe, and treads water and fire without delusion."

Lesser Florescence says: "Flying and transforming, displaying divine powers, he tests your body and mind, causing you to lose the true Dao. How many succeed or falter, how few are delivered? Those who cross are few indeed."

Eastern Master says: "The hearts of scholars are hesitant and unsteady; few reach attainment. Unable to discern truth from falsehood, they are deluded by demonic hosts, leading to slackness. Among ten thousand, not one is delivered."

Lesser Florescence says: "Having endured the trials of water and fire, there are those who succeed and those who fail. Few cross alone; many waver and fall back. None are delivered. Laughing at those who do not cross, he sings this song."

Eastern Master says: "You—it is you. I laugh at you for having only the aspiration for the Dao but lacking its realization. Though you revolve through aeons without end, if your heart is not profoundly unified, you will never be delivered."

Lesser Florescence says: "For those who succeed or fail and retreat, he sighs and pities them, thus composing this song to universally enable their deliverance."

**The Third Song of the Formless Realm’s Demon King**

Eastern Master says: "From the Utmost Wind Heaven of Manifest Concentration to the Ten Heavens of Prohibited Joyful Elegance, this is the division of the Formless Realm. From the Utmost Constant Fusion Heaven to the Four Heavens of the Supreme Polarity’s Nurturing Splendor, this is the upper Formless Realm."

Lesser Florescence says: "The third Formless Realm lies above the Form Realm—hence it is called the third. 'Formless' means without physical form; 'realm' means domain. The Formless Realm has four heavens, and the people of these heavens are empty of both form and desire—hence it is called formless. The demon king’s song refers to the ballads of this realm’s demon king."

Lesser Florescence says: "The Daoist scriptures state: 'With six hundred merits of pure karmic deeds of the mind, one is born in the four heavens of the Formless Realm.' The demon king of this realm is named Shao. Above the Three Realms, boundless and vast, lies the Great Veil."

Eastern Master says: "Miao-miao sounds like 'lofty and distant.' The Great Veil refers to the Great Veil Heaven, which lies above the Three Realms."

Lesser Florescence says: "Above the Three Realms, beyond the Round Veil, though not yet reaching the Utmost Non-Being, it is still the domain of the Great Veil."

Lesser Florescence says: "Miao-miao means lofty and distant. Above the Three Realms lie the Four Brahma Heavens and the Three Clarities, and only then does one reach the Great Veil. Here, the demon king’s song abbreviates the text."

Above, no roots of form; cloud-layers towering, lofty.

Eastern Master says: "Layers mean stacked and repeated; e’e means high and steep. The Great Veil Heaven does not partake of the Form Realm but lies above all heavens, forming mountains from condensed clouds. Above are nine-tiered cloud-palaces, towering and lofty."

Lesser Florescence says: "Within this Great Veil are five realms. Above, there is no obstructing form; below, no fixed roots. All are transformations of wondrous qi, like radiant clouds, ethereal and shimmering. This is the form of no-form, elusive and indescribable—thus it is said to exist yet not exist."

Lesser Florescence says: "The realm of the Great Veil forms mountains from condensed clouds, with nine-tiered terraces, towering and steep. Jade forests stand empty, born without roots."

Mystic Splendor says: "This describes the true emptiness of the Great Veil Heaven’s realm. Mountains, forests, cities, palaces, terraces, and pavilions are all formed from the natural wondrous qi, not through construction. The mortal eye cannot see them—hence they are called formless. Floating in the void, they are called rootless."

Only the Primordial Beginning, the home of boundless kalpas.

Eastern Master says: "The Primordial Beginning is the Heavenly Worthy. 'Boundless kalpas' means vast and innumerable. The Dao of the Primordial Beginning, through countless kalpas, eternally dwells in the Great Veil Heaven."

Lesser Florescence says: "The palaces and towers of these five realms are all the abodes of the Primordial Beginning. The Primordial Beginning is without end, eternally abiding in stillness—hence it is called the home of boundless kalpas."

Beyond the Five Realms, all is governed by the Primordial Beginning—each realm’s sovereign holds the Primordial Beginning as supreme.

Lesser Florescence says: "The Primordial Beginning Heavenly Worthy dwells within these realms, vast and boundless, its kalpas beyond reckoning. It governs our realm, receiving authority from the Mysterious Capital."

Eastern Master says: "To 'govern' means that within the Great Veil Heaven, the Heavenly Worthy presides, with all great sages above. There lies the Mysterious Capital Mountain and the Seven-Treasure Terrace. Upon the terrace rests the *Scripture of the Three Treasures*. Thrice daily, the great sages ascend the Seven-Treasure Terrace, circumambulating in recitation to subdue the myriad demons."

Lesser Florescence says: "The Primordial Beginning is not merely the sovereign of a single realm but also restrains the demon kings of the Three Realms. It unifies the Mysterious Capital, spreading and transforming the myriad manifestations. The Mysterious Capital is the Jade Capital of the Great Veil Heaven."

"Should one transcend our realm, the body enters the Jade Void."

Eastern Master says: "Our realm is the Formless Realm. The body itself enters the realm of the Jade Void. As the Formless is the upper realm, it borders the Jade Void. The Jade Void is the qi of the Jade Void. Having ascended beyond the Formless, the body enters the Purple Ultimate Palace, where the Jade Void Emperor governs within. The Purple Ultimate is another name for the Supreme Ultimate."

Lesser Florescence says: "The Jade Void is the Mysterious Capital Jade Capital."

Lesser Florescence says: "The Primordial Beginning governs our realm, receiving authority from the Mysterious Capital Purple Tenuity. Transcending our realm, the body enters the Jade Void—having passed beyond our Formless Realm. After surpassing the Four Heavens of the Form Realm, one enters the Jade Void. The myriad qi of the Upper Origin, the Three Divisions and Eight Sceneries, all coalesce into human form from the qi of the Jade Void. Our position is that of the Upper King, rectifying and ruling the host of demons."

Eastern Master says: "The Upper King is the sovereign of demon kings, named Shao. He declares, 'Our position is that of the Upper King, restraining and ruling the host of demons—hence the title Upper King.'"

Lesser Florescence says: "The King is the supreme sovereign over all demons. Thus, it is said he rectifies and rules the host of demons. 'Rectify' means to correct; 'rule' means to restrain."

Lesser Florescence says: "The demon king of this realm holds the highest position, governing the Three Realms below and regulating the multitude of demons. Yet in the void, ten thousand transformations arise, and impure qi blooms in profusion."

Eastern Master says: "'Profusion' means chaos; 'bloom' means flourishing. The Three Realms and the void together teem with demonic spirits and ghosts, their transformations chaotic and resplendent, deluding the hearts of seekers—hence called 'blooming in profusion.'"

Lesser Florescence says: "The 'ten thousand transformations in the void' test the seeker, as transformations soar through the air to assay one’s body. 'Blooming in profusion' refers to the pervasive miasma—worldly defilements that fill the empty void, congesting the cosmos."

"Those who preserve the true are few; the deluded are many."

Eastern Master says: "'Preserve' means to secure; 'deluded' means perverse and disordered. Those who secure the true are few; the perverse and disordered are many."

Lesser Florescence says: "Alas! How rare are those who preserve the true in this world, while the deluded and unenlightened abound—how much more so when the whole world is lost in confusion."

"The Dao of immortality is hard to secure; the path of ghosts readily turns to perversity."

Eastern Master says: "The Dao of immortals is formless, hence difficult to uphold; the path of ghosts is rife with desire, hence easily perverted. As the scripture says: 'Not seeing what may be desired keeps the heart undisturbed.'"

Lesser Florescence says: "The Dao of immortal cultivation demands that the true nature be hard to secure; the ghostly path requires no learning, for the mundane heart is already perverse. Drifting with the wind, following the current, one strays ever further—hence it is said the ghostly path readily turns to perversity."

"The human path lies in the heart—truly, it does not depend on others."

Eastern Master says: "The decline of the human path begins in the heart. One must assess one’s own feelings and not rely on others."

Lesser Florescence says: "The principle of the human path resides in the square inch of the heart. Whether one awakens to the Dao and cultivates the true, or strays into perversity and enters the ghostly path, all depends on one’s own heart and lungs—truly, it does not depend on others. 'Truly' means to believe."

"The Dao of immortals values substance; the human path values splendor."

Eastern Master says: "The Dao of immortals accords with nature, discarding superficial splendor to embrace utmost substance. The human path values glory and splendor, the opposite of the immortal Dao."

Lesser Florescence says: "The Dao of immortal cultivation values truth and substance; the path of worldly conduct values superficial splendor. Thus, the scripture says: 'Dwell in its substance, not in its splendor.'"

"If you do not delight in the immortal Dao, how can you transcend the Three Realms?"

Eastern Master says: "'You' means 'you.' If you are not single-minded, how can you ascend beyond the Three Realms?"

Lesser Florescence says: "If you, O worldly people, do not cultivate the immortal Dao and ascend to the Five Realms, then the trials of the Three Realms cannot be overcome. This means to rise beyond their bounds, not merely to pass through them."

"If you wish to revolve through the Five Paths, what can I do for you?"

Eastern Master says: "The Five Paths are the fields of the five sufferings. 'What can I do' is an expression of sorrow. The demon king, seeing seekers in the Three Realms who fail to transcend, defeated by perverse spirits and unable to attain right vision, sink into evil destinies and lose their prior merit, must then endure all manner of suffering within the Five Paths—how grievous! Hence this profound lament."

Lesser Florescence says: "If you do not rise above the Three Realms, you will naturally revolve through the Five Paths. Since this is the consequence of your own actions, what can I do for you? Thus, it is said: 'The human path lies in the heart—truly, it does not depend on others.' The meaning of the Five Paths has been explained above."

Lesser Florescence says: "Those who do not delight in the Three Heavens but instead revolve through the Five Paths, prizing splendor and abandoning substance—what can I do for them?"

Above the Three Realms, in the midst of the floating void, the demon king’s song resounds, its verses interwoven with cavernous hymns.

Eastern Master says: "Above the Three Realms, the demon king chants sacred texts in the void, yet remains within the Three Realms, his verses intermingling with cavernous hymns."

Lesser Florescence says: "The demon king, ever above the Three Realms in the empty void, sings this hymn, lamenting the plight of worldly people with profound sorrow."

The hymn’s meaning interpenetrates, far harmonizing with the Great Cavern. The demon king is the lord of demons, not a king who is demonic. Thus, though his person is most numinous, his words align with the Great Cavern. Reciting it a hundred times is called "crossing the Southern Palace"; reciting it a thousand times, the demon king safeguards and welcomes; with ten thousand recitations, the Way is complete—one soars into the Great Void, transcends the Three Realms, and ascends to the rank of Immortal Duke.
