Lesser Florescence says: To recite it a hundred times refers specifically to this demon king’s hymn, not the entire scripture. After a hundred recitations, one’s name is registered and ascends to the Vermilion Palace above the Southern Crossing. After a thousand recitations, the demon king protects and escorts one in all goings and comings. When the Way is perfected through ten thousand recitations, one rides a dragon to ascend to the Great Clarity, soars to the Great Ultimate, roams the Great Void, personally transcends the tribulations of the Three Realms, and attains the rank of Immortal Duke. Yet those today who recite it ten thousand times without achieving this result either practice good and evil equally, with merit and transgression balanced, or recite with the mouth while the heart wanders, violating the rites and losing the method—such people only invite further descent, how can they hope for ascent? If the heart accords with the scripture and conduct aligns with its teachings, uniting solely in goodness and cutting off all entanglements, then even after only a few thousand recitations, one may glimpse the effect; why must one wait until ten thousand recitations to ascend into the Great Void?

Mysterious Splendor says: The Immortal Duke is a rank among the Most High Perfected. To fly beyond the Three Realms, one first arrives at the Four Heavens of Seed People; above that lie the Three Clarities, which are the ranks of the Immortal Dukes. The phrase "flying beyond the Three Realms, ascending to the rank of Immortal Duke" is an abbreviation in the text.

Those who hear the numinous sound—before them, the demon king shows reverence.

Mysterious Splendor says: "Those who hear the numinous sound" refers to hearing the original hymn of the Numinous Treasure. The Dao Lord praised it, saying that even the demon king of the Three Realms composed a hymn of the Cavern Mystery, and those who recite and uphold it can still achieve perfection and enter the Way. How much more so for those who hear the original hymn of my Numinous Treasure—if they recite and uphold it, all the demon kings of the Three Realms will revere their persons. Thus it is said, "the demon king shows reverence."

He commands and restrains the earth spirits.

Lesser Florescence says: This is the command of the Most High.

*The Bowu Zhi* states: The abodes of the earth spirits lie beneath Mount Kunlun.

**Attendant escort for departure and return.**
*Youxi* says: Should there be those who hear the verses of this numinous hymn, the demon kings shall command and restrain the earth spirits, so that when one remains at home, they stand guard, and when one goes forth or returns, they escort and receive.

**Deliverance from the Five Sufferings and Eight Adversities of the earthly prisons, with seven generations of ancestors ascending and migrating, forever departing the offices of the ghostly bureaucracy.**
*Youxi* says: To lift the seven generations to immortality, to transcend the eight adversities of ghostly exile, to forever emerge from the Dark River of the netherworld, to bid eternal farewell to the officials of the Northern Bureau. The Three Paths and Five Sufferings together form the Eight Adversities, as previously annotated.

**The soul crosses to the Vermilion Mound, undergoes refinement and rebirth—this is called boundless and universal deliverance without end.**
*Youxi* says: Once the seven generations have ascended, they all enter the Southern Palace to undergo refinement. When the refinement is complete, they are reborn. This may be called universal deliverance without limit, vast salvation without measure. The Vermilion Mound is the Southern Vermilion Mound Palace.

**There are secret celestial patterns, revered by all the heavens.**
**To leak or slight them is to fall into hell, with calamity extending to seven generations of ancestors.**
*Youxi* says: If one treasures and venerates these texts, then the Heavenly Emperors, all the sages, and the numinous spirits shall together hold them in reverence. If one treats them with carelessness or leaks them, the body shall be punished by the Three Offices, and misfortune shall extend to the seven generations. Since the scripture has now concluded, these admonitions are reiterated—these are the two chapters.

**The Dao says: These two chapters are the hidden and sacred sounds of the Heavenly Emperors and the most numinous demon kings.**
*Dong* says: "The Dao says" refers to the Dao Lord’s own preface. The "two chapters" are: first, the *Primal Cavern Mystery Hymn*, and second, the *Primal Cavern Jade Calendar Hymn*—together called the two chapters. The names and hidden mysteries of the great gods of the heavens, the Heavenly Emperors, and the demon kings are profound, hence they are called the hidden and secret purport.

*Youxi* says: From this point onward, every chapter that begins with "The Dao says" is likewise the speech of the Dao Lord, consistent with the preceding preface. These two chapters of the original scripture were spoken by the Primordial Beginning. The preceding preface was later added by the Most High. The first chapter contains the hidden names of the thirty-two Heavenly Emperors, while the second holds the secret sounds of the demon kings of the Three Realms. All are the words of the Great Brahma, not the common speech of the mundane world.

*Youxi* says: Since they were spoken by the Primordial Beginning and expounded by the Most High, they are the secret hymns of the heavens and the hidden melodies of the numinous and demonic. Naturally, they embody the supreme principles of the Great Brahma—how could they be the ordinary words of the mundane world? Their language lacks ornate rhythm, their verses lack florid elegance; thus they are called profound and obscure, difficult to fathom in detail.

*Youxi* says: Since they are not the common speech of the mundane world, they lack ornate rhythm. As they convey the profound purport of the heavens, they lack florid elegance. Unless one is a perfected person who has penetrated the mysteries and investigated the subtle, none can fully comprehend them. "Language" refers to discourse; "verses" refer to the lines and phrases.

*Shaowei* says: "Profound" means deep; "obscure" means hidden. The names of the Heavenly Emperors and the titles of the demon kings in these two texts—all their language lacks melodious beauty, their verses lack ornate refinement. This depth and obscurity are why they are difficult to interpret.

**These are treasured by the heavens and kept secret in the Purple Tenuity Palace of the Mysterious Capital.**
*Youxi* says: Since they are revered by the sages of the heavens, they are kept secret in the Jade Capital of the Mysterious Metropolis above. The Three Realms—Grand Ultimate, Jade Purity, and Highest Purity—each has its own Purple Tenuity Palace.

**According to the Mysterious Regulations, they are transmitted once every forty thousand kalpas.**
*Dong* says: "The heavens" here refer to the heavens of the upper realms. This scripture is treasured by the sages of the upper heavens and kept secret in the Purple Tenuity Palace of the Mysterious Capital. According to the Mysterious Regulations, it is transmitted once every forty thousand kalpas. "Mysterious" refers to the heavens. This is the time limit of the heavens; in the human realm, it is transmitted once every forty years, hence it is called the Mysterious Regulations.

It is also said that in the study of the Dao and the transmission of scriptures, one may transmit to one person every forty years. Those who extend their lifespan gain four hundred years; those who attain earthly immortality gain four thousand years; those who attain heavenly immortality gain forty thousand years; and those who fully realize the Dao of the Supreme Perfected gain forty thousand kalpas.

*Youxi* says: Since it is said that "ten thousand kalpas are like last night," this is the celestial measure of the Dao. "A thousand springs are like this morning"—thus, transmission once every forty thousand kalpas is not considered distant. This is the standard of the celestial perfected, hence it is said to follow the Mysterious Regulations, without specifying the time limits for transmission among perfected persons.

**If there is a perfected person who offers gold and treasures, pledges sincerity according to the ancient standards, and makes oaths to the Ten Heavens, only then shall it be bestowed.**
*Dong* says: As previously stated, the heavens have their time limits. Among them, if there is a person of utmost faith whose heart is devoted to the great Dharma, who can use gold and treasures as a pledge of sincerity, and who comes seeking to receive it, they must then transgress the prohibitions, make oaths to the Ten Heavens, and only then may it be transmitted.

*Youxi* says: Both the preceding preface and this passage mention offering gold and treasures, without specifying the quantity. Since this is a pledge of sincerity, the heart of the perfected person is one, but the amount may vary. According to one’s means, one makes oaths to the ten directions and swears before the heavens. Though the gold and treasures may be modest, the oath is weighty. Since the preface has already spoken of this, and the scripture concludes with another oath, it is reiterated again and again to ensure that none neglect the unseen regulations.

**The Dao says: The revolutions of heaven and earth also have their ends in adversity.**
*Dong* says: "Revolutions" refer to four: the generation of humans, the death of humans, the averting of disasters, and the benefits of meritorious deeds. It is also said: Heaven one, Earth two, Heaven three, Earth four. "Revolution" refers to the kalpas; "measure" refers to the calculations. The Yang Nine and Hundred Six are all measures of prosperity and adversity. Though heaven and earth are vast, they too have their periods of decline and ruin—this is the meaning.

*Youxi* says: Heaven’s distress is the Yang Nine calamity; Earth’s adversity is the Hundred Six disaster. Hence it is said that the revolutions of heaven and earth also have their ends in adversity.

*Shaowei* says: In minor cases, the Hundred Six and Yang Nine; in major cases, the dissolution of the Three Realms.

**Xuan Ying says:** *"Adversity’s end"* refers to the Yang Nine and Hundred Six calamities, while *"end"* signifies the dissolution of the Three Realms. The Yang Nine and Hundred Six: according to the *Zhou Yi*, nineteen years form one *zhang*, four *zhang* form one *bu*, twenty *bu* form one *tong*, and three *tong* form one *yuan*—a *yuan* spanning four thousand six hundred twenty years. Within this cycle, fifty-four years bring floods and droughts. The Yang Nine: as the odd number of Yang culminates at nine, calamities manifest—at their greatest, nine years of drought; lesser cases bring seven, five, three, or one year of fire. The even number of Yin culminates at eight, with calamities bringing eight, six, four, or two years of floods. The Hundred Six: upon entering a *yuan*, the first one hundred sixty years—an odd number of Yang—bring minor droughts, hence the term *"Hundred Six calamity."* Broadly speaking, the conjunctions of Yang Nine and Hundred Six: the first three hundred years of a *yuan* mark the lesser Yang Nine and lesser Hundred Six; nine hundred years bring the great Yang Nine and great Hundred Six. At their greatest, nine years of severe drought and eight years of catastrophic floods. The *Han Shu* states: four thousand six hundred seventeen years form one *yuan*; when the count of three *yuan* is exhausted, it marks the end of the great kalpa, and heaven and earth dissolve. Three *yuan* total thirteen thousand eight hundred fifty-one years. The first one hundred sixty years of a *yuan* bring minor calamities, hence the term *"Hundred Six."* The meaning of *"adversity’s end"* is roughly outlined as above.

The sun, moon, and five planets also wax and wane. **Dong says:** The sun declines after noon; the moon wanes after fullness. When the stellar lodges halt or fail to revolve, it too marks heaven’s appointed time—all are natural principles of numerology. **Youxi says:** The sun and moon undergo eclipses and phases; the five planets deviate from their proper paths.

Even the most sagely and divine beings experience prosperity and adversity. **Dong says:** The most sagely are not yet the greatest sages—King Wen was imprisoned at Youli, and Confucius faced hardship in Chen and Cai—all were times of adversity. **Youxi says:** Even the sagely and divine endure cycles of prosperity and decline; how much more so for the common folk, whose trials defy description!

Scholars of lesser learning also suffer illness and harm. **Dong says:** If heaven, earth, and sages experience adversity, how can lesser scholars avoid affliction? **Youxi says:** For humble students of minor learning, illness and misfortune are natural; if they encounter such, they should accept it without resentment.

When such calamities arise, those of shared *qi* must unite in heart to perform purification rites. **Shaowei says:** *"Shared qi"* refers to shared methods—those who together receive the wondrous *qi* of the Dao. Burning incense in the six periods and reciting the scriptures ten times will summon blessings and dissolve all misfortune. The boundless scriptures universally deliver limitless beings. **Youxi says:** In times of calamity, summon fellow students and like-minded companions to unite in heart and strength, perform purification rites, repent, burn incense in the six periods, and recite these scriptures ten times around. The reward of virtue will manifest immediately, and inauspicious disasters will naturally dissipate. Thus, we know the scriptures’ power is vast and universal, broadly aiding the world.

**The Dao says:** Those of lesser learning, whose Dao is shallow or whose immortal rank remains unfulfilled, may face karmic dissolution, their bodies passing through the Palace of Great Yin. **Dong says:** All who die pass through the offices of Great Yin; for such individuals, reciting scriptures and practicing the Way is essential. **Youxi says:** Lesser scholars may have weak past-life merits or insufficient present virtue, causing their resolve for the Dao to falter and karmic obstacles to encroach. Unable to attain the rank of immortals, their names are already inscribed in the ghostly registers. Thus, when the mysterious workings of fate summon them, they meet their end, their souls returning to Great Yin and their corpses lying in the earth. **Shaowei says:** The ghostly path is the Palace of Great Yin.

At the moment of passing, fellow students and perfected beings should burn incense and recite the scriptures ten times to deliver the corpse according to the proper method. **Youxi says:** Companions of the same covenant and learning, true friends, should wholeheartedly perform purification rites and recite the scriptures ten times. At the time of death, they collectively deliver the corpse, so that the living gain the merit of salvation, and the deceased receive the blessing of liberation. *"According to the proper method"* refers to following the Five Refinements for the Living Corpse. The soul then ascends directly to the Southern Palace. **Dong says:** For those facing death, if fellow students again burn incense and recite scriptures to deliver the corpse, the soul will ascend to the Southern Palace and receive natural blessings. According to their accumulated merit, they will be reborn after a calculated period, escape the cycle of rebirth, and attain immortality. **Dong says:** When merit reaches three thousand, one ascends to heaven in broad daylight. **Youxi says:** Having performed the corpse-deliverance rites, the soul ascends to the Vermilion Palace, refined in the flowing fires of the courtyard. Depending on the depth of their cultivated merit, the length of their allotted time—years, months, or days—is measured. Once the term is complete, the spirit returns to the body, and they are reborn. Though outwardly deceased, after a time of accumulation, it feels like a brief slumber, unaware of the passage of years. From then on, they attain immortality—this is also the path of corpse liberation.

**The Dao says:** When the revolutions of heaven and earth near their end, purification rites must be performed, incense burned, and scriptures recited. **Dong says:** To avert calamitous revolutions. **Youxi says:** When heaven and earth face adversity and their cycles approach their end, perform purification rites, repent, and recite these scriptures to pacify and ward off disaster.

When the stellar lodges deviate from their paths and the sun and moon lose their proper phases, purification rites must be performed, incense burned, and scriptures recited. **Dong says:** To preserve peace and tranquility. **Youxi says:** When the five planets deviate from their celestial paths and the sun and moon suffer eclipses or lose their proper phases, perform purification rites, repent, and recite these scriptures to restore order.

When the four seasons lose their balance and Yin and Yang fall out of harmony, purification rites must be performed, incense burned, and scriptures recited.

**Dong says:** To regulate Yin and Yang.

**Youxi says:** When spring, summer, autumn, and winter fail to transition in their seasons, when Yin and Yang’s pitch-pipes fall into discord, and when the qi and climate grow perverse, purification rites must be performed, repentance offered, and these scriptures recited to restore harmony.

When the sovereign faces disaster and warfare erupts on all sides, purification rites must be performed, incense burned, and scriptures recited.

**Dong says:** To safeguard and protect.

**Youxi says:** When the state suffers calamity and arms rise on all fronts, purification rites must be performed, repentance offered, and these scriptures recited to dispel the disaster.

When pestilence spreads and the multitudes perish or suffer harm, purification rites must be performed, incense burned, and scriptures recited.

**Dong says:** To suppress and subdue.

**Youxi says:** When epidemic poisons rage and seasonal maladies afflict the people, causing countless deaths and injuries, purification rites must be performed, repentance offered, and these scriptures recited to eradicate the calamity.

**Xuanying says:** The Son of Heaven refers to the people as *zhaomin* ("the multitudes"), while feudal lords call them *wanmin* ("the ten thousand"). A *zhao* denotes ten billion, signifying their vast number. This clarifies that when the sovereign faces disaster, the multitudes suffer harm.

When masters, teachers, or friends face the end of their allotted span, purification rites must be performed, incense burned, and scriptures recited.

**Dong says:** When masters, disciples, or friends reach the end of their destined time, burn incense and recite the scriptures ten times to deliver and ferry their souls.

**Youxi says:** When Daoist masters or companions approach the end of their lives, perform purification rites according to the preceding methods to deliver their corporeal forms, that they may attain immortality.

The merit of purification rites and scripture recitation is profound. Above, it dispels heavenly disasters and safeguards the emperor; below, it wards off poisonous harm and delivers the multitudes.

**Youxi says:** The merit of purification rites, precepts, incense offerings, and scripture recitation is deep, and the blessings they bestow are weighty. Above, they can eliminate heavenly calamities and secure the emperor’s reign; below, they can dispel poisonous harm and universally deliver the people from peril.

**Shaowei says:** Each year, in the twelfth month, the *Daling* (Great Mound) star, also called the *Jishi* (Accumulated Corpses), emits qi that descends upon the earth, seeping into mounds and decaying bones. Its ascending qi is ridden by ghosts, spreading febrile diseases known as epidemic poisons. Reciting the scriptures can dispel these afflictions, sparing the people from death.

The blessings of life and death depend upon it, their merit boundless. Thus it is said: "Limitless deliverance of heaven and humanity."

**Youxi says:** "Life depends upon it" means attaining the Dao in this body and ascending to heaven in broad daylight. "Death depends upon it" means the soul is ferried to the Vermilion Mound, where it undergoes refinement and immortal transformation. Heavenly beings ascend to the joy of the Three Clarities, while mortals instantly transcend the eight sufferings. The merit of broad salvation is vast, and the virtue of universal deliverance is profound.

**Shaowei says:** All references to purification rites denote the *Huanglu* and other such rites, which employ the Five Scriptures for stabilization and thanksgiving—these are not the purification rites of the common world. Petitions are presented in the three periods to move heaven and earth, summon blessings, and dispel calamities.

*The Wondrous Scripture of the Upper Chapters on the Limitless Salvation of Humanity, with Four Commentaries, Fascicle Three*
*The Wondrous Scripture of the Upper Chapters on the Limitless Salvation of Humanity, with Four Commentaries, Fascicle Four*

**The Dao says:** Wherever this scripture exists, if the sovereign of heaven and earth or the multitudes perform these meritorious deeds in times of disaster, resolve to perform purification rites, burn incense, and recite the scriptures ten times, all the heavens will record their names, and the myriad spirits will guard them.

**Youxi says:** "Record their names" means inscribing their virtuous deeds. If one can uphold this scripture, follow the preceding instructions, and resolve to perform purification rites with sincerity, then above, they will dispel the disasters of heaven and earth; in the middle, they will augment the sovereign’s blessings; and below, they will relieve the suffering of the multitudes. The heavens will then inscribe their names on the Yellow Registers and White Tablets, and the myriad spirits will guard them in walking, standing, sitting, and reclining.

Only those of exceptional attainment may become ministers of the Golden Gates of the Sage Lord.

The Eastern Master says: "The term *right distinction* here follows the convention of official documents, where matters are itemized on the right." ○ Youxi says: "If there are those of profound understanding who embody the truth, able to follow the scriptural precepts and cultivate accordingly, they will surely assist the Sage Lord and stand in attendance at the Golden Gates. The Golden Gates are the abode of the Sage Lord." ○ Shaowei says: "The Sage Lord is the Later Sage, the Great Peace Lord Li of the Golden Gates. His personal name is Hong, and in a future kalpa, he will descend to become the ruler of humanity, hence he is preemptively called the Later Sage Lord. The *Xuan Zhong Ji* of Master Yin states: The Most High Lord Lao constantly dwells in the Purple Tenuity Palace, also known as the Heavenly August Great Emperor, the Celestial Worthy of Grand Unity, and the Sage Lord of the Golden Gates. The myriad things of heaven and earth are none that do not arise from his transformation. If one can fast with utmost sincerity, recite and chant the numinous scriptures, they may ascend to the Purple Tenuity and become his ministers." The *Jade Record* states: "Those who do not invoke the Twenty-Four Spirits or know the names of the Three Eights and the Scenic Forms cannot become ministers of the Sage Lord of the Golden Gates." The heavens record the merits and transgressions of people without the slightest error. Youxi says: "The heavens oversee and report correspondences, distinguishing and recording the good and evil of people, scrutinizing the merits and faults of practitioners. Since not even the finest detail is missed, neither is the most minute speck overlooked. The Demon Kings of the heavens will also protect and recommend you. Only those who attain the Way may thoroughly comprehend the ultimate teachings." The Eastern Master says: "The Five Heavens, the Three Realms, and the supremely numinous Demon Kings will protect your person and surely commend your merits. Those with the bone structure and destined portion of the elect, who are to attain the Way and achieve perfection, must thoroughly examine the scriptural words and deeply embody their true purport." ○ Shaowei says: "People should only diligently cultivate fasting and purification; on the day they attain the Way, they will naturally understand the ultimate teachings. This is said lest those who have not yet grasped the profound meaning grow lax midway and abandon their resolve." The Immeasurable Sounds of the Great Hidden Language of Brahmā in the Heavens ○ The Dao Lord composed this. The Eastern Master says: "Hidden' has four aspects: first, the concealment of names; second, the concealment of taboos; third, the concealment of matters; and fourth, the concealment of language." ○ Youxi says: "This is the title. *Brahmā* means the Dao. This chapter consists of the hidden and tabooed language of the Great Dao in the Thirty-Two Heavens, which cannot be fathomed." ○ Shaowei says: "The Great Brahmā refers to the qi of the Primordial Beginning’s Great Brahmā, which separates and combines to form sounds. *Brahmā* means 'pervasive,' for it is the same throughout the Six Directions. *Hidden language* refers to the secrets of the heavens, which worldly people do not understand. *Immeasurable sounds* means that beings of different regions and kinds universally hear the wondrous meaning without limit." In total, there are two hundred fifty-six characters, distributed among the Thirty-Two Heavens, with eight characters per heaven, and also inscribed upon the palaces and gates of the Mysterious Capital and the celestial towers. If one can ingest these characters, they will, according to their practice, ride the qi and return to their respective abodes. ○ Xuan Ying says: "When practitioners ingest these characters, on the day their merit is complete, they will ride the qi and return to their respective abodes. The method is found in the *Inner Sounds Jade Precepts*." The Middle Chapter of the Numinous Writ of the Primordial Beginning The Eastern Master says: "This chapter’s text consists of two hundred fifty-six characters, each a square zhang in size, with eight radiating edges. First, they are distributed among the Thirty-Two Heavens, eight characters per heaven, to dispel misfortune and accomplish all salvation. Second, they are inscribed upon the gates, towers, and palaces of the Mysterious Capital and the heavenly abodes. If one cultivates and ingests these characters, they will ascend to those places and summon the immortals of the ten directions." The Dao Lord himself appended this beneath the title. The *Numinous Writ of the Primordial Beginning* refers to the sounds of the Eight Assemblies of the Primordial Celestial Worthy’s Numinous Writ, which exist within the Thirty-Two Heavens. Since they pertain to both principle and practice, this was compiled. ○ Shaowei says: "In the present commentary, I have followed the *Inner Sounds* explanations of the Heavenly Perfected Sovereign, sometimes abridging to retain the essentials, sometimes adding characters for clarity. Where the scriptural text is rearranged and not in sequential order, the aim is to enable people to quickly grasp its meaning." Dǎnlóu Ācāng, Wúhé Guānyīn. ○ Shaowei says: "These eight characters are the inner sounds of the Yellow and Once-Heaven. *Dǎn* means vast and boundless. *Lóu* is the name of the long tower at the foot of the Jade Capital Mountain. It supports the Palace of the Mysterious Capital, also called the Tower Capital, for the mountain and towers rise in mutual prominence, vast and boundless. *Ā* is the name of the Ānà spirit in the Mysterious Capital, who oversees the tower’s surveillance and governs the qi of the Great Brahmā. When the qi’s cycles complete their circuit, the Ānà spirit sounds the drum of the Tower Capital to assemble the multitude of perfected beings and ascend to pay homage to the Primordial Beginning. The drum sounds once every three cycles as a regular observance. *Cāng* is the name of the terrace where the Celestial Lord roams; it is lush and luxuriant, hence called *Huì*. *Wú* means the Great Nonbeing; it is said that within the Great Nonbeing, the true sages naturally arise. The *Tai Xiao Lang Book* states: 'The formless gives birth to the true; the true arises from the formless.' *Hé* is the name of the gate of the sun and moon, where the sun and moon meet at the Hé Gate. *Guān* means observation and awakening; it is the taboo name of the Celestial Lord of this heaven, who oversees the records of the long night. *Yīn* refers to the sound of these eight characters. If one can recite the sound of these eight characters, then perfected persons will ride the golden wheel to open the dark, and jade maidens will wave flower banners to unfasten the locks. The Observer of Awakening oversees the records of the long night, delivering the four dark realms and the nine nether palaces, causing the seven ancestors to be illuminated and the decayed bones to live again." ○ Xuan Ying says: "The Heavenly Perfected Sovereign stated that these eight characters are from the *Flying Mystery Natural Writ*, each a square zhang in size, their radiant patterns shining brilliantly and illuminating the eight directions. The Primordial Beginning transmitted them downward, instructing me to transcribe the characters, interpret their sounds, and compose the *Great Hidden Language of Brahmā* and the *Immeasurable Sounds* of the Yellow and Once-Heaven, entrusting them to the Dao Lord to teach those in the Yellow and Once-Heaven who are destined to attain the Way."

The *Immeasurable Cavern Chapter* is composed by harmonizing the flying primordial qi of the five directions within the Yellow and Once-Heaven with the natural sounds of the eight characters, and this principle applies to all heavens below. "Must extend the luminous head, the Dharma grasps the bodhi-dhāraṇī."

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the sounds within the Jade Perfection Heaven. *Must extend* (Xuyan) is the name of the northwest gate of the Kingly Perfection Heaven. When the great kalpas intersect, it is through *Must Extend* that they unfold. The jade perfected and supreme sages then turn to the *Luminous Head*, who is the capital warden of the Primordial Beginning. When the Primordial Beginning initiates the kalpa, the capital warden opens the Way, and the qi of Brahmā conduct swiftly illuminates of its own accord. *Dharma* refers to the field of the Dharma-wheel where sins and blessings are determined. *Grasps* (Lan) means awakening. This is the taboo name of the Heavenly Emperor within this heaven, who presides over the deliverance of souls and their rebirth. *Bodhi* (Pu) is bodhi. He wields the nine-colored banner. *Dhāraṇī* (Tan) is dhāraṇī. She holds the ten absolute banners, both being the perfected of the Upper Primordial. Those who constantly recite the *Cavern Chapter* will have the Dharma-wheel draw their register before the Controller of Destiny, awakening to deliver souls unto rebirth. The bodhi turns the nine colors in wheeling motion, and the dhāraṇī revolves the ten absolutes to halt the kalpa. Heaven and Earth thereby remain unshaken, and the myriad beings endure forever.

"Jiana Ayixi, Huhe Liuyin."

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the sounds within the Heavens of the Divine Youth. *Jiana* is the title of the Heavenly Master of Charts, the firstborn. He oversees the records of life and death, governs immortals and transcendentals, and presides over the Golden Flower Palace. The Golden Flower connects with the Dragon Mountain, resplendent above the Jade Purity and flourishing within the Cavernous Void. *Ayixi* is the name of a tree in the Seven Treasures Grove, whose canopy covers the four directions. It is the pleasure garden of the supreme sages and the playground of the perfected. *Hu* means awakening, the name of a flying heavenly spirit who governs the great and small kalpas. *He* is *Hemo* (Hā Mā), by which the heavens address the Primordial Heavenly Worthy. *Liuyin* means to disseminate songs and chants. When the kalpa reaches its end, *Hemo* reveals the transformative teachings, universally delivering heavenly and human beings. Heavenly and human beings rejoice, and the myriad Dao flow freely. At that time, the heavenly kalpa contracts, the human Dao declines, and the coming kalpa’s destruction approaches, concealing the true scriptures. The Heavenly Worthy, foreseeing this, preemptively composes songs and chants. Those who constantly recite the *Cavern Chapter* will have the Master of Charts erase their sinful records from the long night and inscribe their names of life in the Southern Palace.

"Huadu Quli, Xianpu Yuzhen."

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the sounds within the Heaven of Level Nurturance. *Huadu* is another name for the Azure Flower Gate of the Great Ultimate Palace within the heavens. *Qu* refers to the heavenly Brahmā spirit-people flying above the Great Ultimate, singing the *Cavern Chapter*’s melodies amidst the qi of the refreshing numinous wind. *Li* is the name of the Jade Maiden of Supreme Harmony. *Xian* is *Xianyun* (auspicious clouds). *Pu* is *Pulou*, the name of a heavenly tower. When the Jade Maiden at the Huadu Gate chants the songs of the spirit-people, auspicious clouds unfurl in timely response, scattering above the *Pulou* tower. *Yu* is the hidden name of the Heavenly Emperor. *Zhen* means to arrive. The *Yu* Emperor constantly rides the eight-scene chariot, roaming beyond the eight poles, arriving at the abodes of ghosts and spirits. He revolves the ten absolute banners to summon heavenly demons and universally delivers heavenly and human beings. Those who constantly recite the *Cavern Chapter* will have flying heavens sing from afar, the three realms’ controllers welcome them, the seven ancestors emerge from the long night, and ascend to the Southern Palace.

"Da Luo Dafan, Sanyan Qingyun."

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the sounds within the Heaven of Literary Elevation. *Da* is the name of a jade tower within the heavens, serving as the convenient gate of the three realms. *Luo* describes the tower’s resplendent brilliance. *Great* (Da) refers to the Great Amnesty. At the beginning of the Heavenly Worthy’s kalpa, a great amnesty is always proclaimed, called the Great Amnesty, emptying the three evil destinies and halting the trials of the nine nether realms, granting them a new beginning. *Brahmā* (Fan) is the qi of Brahmā conduct, which can seal the Dragon Han kalpa and initiate the era of Red Clarity. *Sanyan* refers to perfected ones scattering incense in the jade tower. *Qingyun* (auspicious clouds) are those with all five colors, said to waft fragrance to brush the perfected, with auspicious clouds reaching the Purple Palace and flying heavens dancing in the empty wheel.

"Feisa Yudu, Mingmo Shangmen."

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the sounds within the Heaven of Māyā. *Fly* (Fei) is the title of the flying heavenly spirit-people. When the kalpa of heaven and earth changes and sinks into *Yankang*, the obscure qi opens, and the flying heavens reveal their light, scattering radiance so that all heavens receive qi. *Sprinkle* (Sa) refers to the swift revolution of the Dragon Han kalpa. *Jade* (Yu) is the sacred title of the Jade Perfected who opens the long night. *Capital* (Du) is Fengdu, the capital of the nine nether realms. Those with meritorious deeds will have the Jade Perfected open the gates of the long night, and Fengdu deliver them from the eight difficulties. The seven ancestors thereby return to life, and the hidden souls thereby shine forth. *Bright* (Ming) means to understand the meaning of the eight characters. *Demon* (Mo) is the demon king. *Supreme* (Shang) is the Supreme Emperor. *Gate* (Men) is the gate below. Those who clearly understand the meaning of the eight characters will have the demon king respectfully submit, and the Supreme Emperor nurture them at the Gate of the Spirit of Initial Life. Below the gate, the Han Lord Controller of Destiny and the Recorder of Registers calculate their deliverance in the Southern Palace, bestowing blessings upon the nine clans and granting grace to life and death.

"Wuxing Shangshou, Huizhi Liuxuan."

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the sounds within the Heaven of Transcendent Balance. *Wu* is the Upper Way, referring to the qi of the Primordial Beginning that illuminates the Upper Way of the Primordial. *Conduct* (Xing) is the guiding principle of the Heavenly Primordial, weaving the eight poles, pervading the Brahmā qi, and flowing ceaselessly. *Upper Head* (Shangshou) is the sin official of the Northern Dipper. He turns the celestial pivot, calculates the conjunctions and degrees, and when the numbers are exhausted, the great kalpas intersect.

"Return" (*Hui*) means to revolve. "Tread" (*Zhi*) means to step. At the inception of the kalpic revolution, the Primordial Beginning treads upon the void and wheels in revolution, disseminating transformation throughout the ten directions. "Flow" (*Liu*) is the radiance of the streaming dawn. It also causes the light of the streaming dawn to illuminate the repositories of the long night. "Mysterious" (*Xuan*) is the void. Above the Heaven of Transcendent Balance lies the Mysterious Capital’s scenery, where the Mountain of Empty Peaks stands—realm where the myriad sages wander and the living and dead return. When the Dao is not yet fully perfected, the body must undergo extinction; the soul ascends to the Empty Peaks, undergoes refinement, and is delivered to the Southern Palace.

*Ātuó Lóngluó, Sìxiàng Xūyuán.*

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the sounds within the Heaven of Obscuring Veils. *Ā* refers to the nine-fold mountains within heaven, linked in continuous ridges. *Tuó* is the tower upon the mountain, ascending to communicate with the qi of Jade Purity, gazing upon the realms of the Three Worlds. The Thearch constantly rides the cloud of Three Simplicities, driving the chariot of nine dragons, ascending the ridges of Ātuó, and descending to oversee the transgressions of the myriad beings. *Dragon* (*Lóng*) refers to Dragon Mountain, separated from Ātuó by ninety million myriad li. *Luó* is the name of the sun and moon. The *Jade Weft* states: The Perfected of the Nine Heavens of Upper Clarity call the sun *Zhuóyào*. *Luó* signifies the interlocking mountain forms, where the sun and moon shine above the peaks. *Four* (*Sì*) refers to the palaces of the Four Poles—Eastern Florescence, Southern Culmen, Western Numen, and Northern Perfection—where the Perfected of the Four Poles govern the registers of life and death. *Image* (*Xiàng*) is the wheel-chariot of images. The Perfected constantly ride these chariots through the Three Worlds, reviewing the records of life, death, and transgressions, and initiating the deliverance of those who study the Dao. *Exhale* (*Xū*) means to nurture. It is the taboo name of the Heavenly Thearch, who serves as the Deliverer of Destinies in the Southern Palace, presiding over the refinement and deliverance of decayed souls. *Round* (*Yuán*) means youth. It refers to the Youth Born of the Sun, who pours celestial nectar upon the heavenly beings. Those who recite and chant the cavernous scriptures shall have their jade names inscribed in the Thearch’s register; their lives and deaths shall be delivered in the Southern Palace, the Four Poles shall bestow upon them natural feathered chariots, and their seven ancestors shall rejoice and wander in the halls of fortune.

To the right, the Eastern Direction: the Nine Qi Azure Heaven, the spontaneous jade characters.

The Mysterious Splendor says: Heaven possesses eight characters, combining to form sixty-four sounds, also called the sixty-four chapters. According to the inner sounds of the jade characters, the esoteric incantation of the Eight Heavens of the East is called *Lingyin Bashu Liushisi Pian* (The Sixty-Four Chapters of the Eight Divine Sounds). Practitioners, according to what they wear and bear, embody the sounds of heaven. For example, when cultivating the Heaven of Sovereign Radiance, one wears and bears its eight characters. According to the first section of the *Inner Sounds Jade Characters Formula*: In the Heaven of Sovereign Radiance, the first, second, and third characters are all inscribed facing upward upon the Long Tower of the Mysterious Capital. Their script rectifies the celestial degrees and summons the divine spirits of the ten directions. The fourth and fifth characters are then inscribed upon the southern pavilion of the Thearch’s Wandering Terrace, governing the void wherein spontaneous divine Perfected are born. The sixth, seventh, and eighth characters are inscribed upon the gates of the sun and moon, governing the light that penetrates the obscure and opens the repositories of the long night. Each character measures one *zhang* square, their eight corners resplendent within the Heaven of Sovereign Radiance.

The Perfected Sovereign of Heaven says: To practice the Dao of ascending transcendence, on the ten fast days of the month, inscribe in cinnabar the first, second, and third characters of the Heaven of Sovereign Radiance, face *ren* (north) while wearing them, and recite the incantation as prescribed. After one hundred days, the myriad spirits shall attend your body. On the fifteenth and thirtieth days of the month, inscribe in cinnabar the fourth and fifth characters, face east while wearing them, and recite the incantation as prescribed. After twenty-four years of this practice, divine Perfected shall be born within you, and both in life and death, you shall ascend to the Thearch’s Wandering Terrace. On the waxing, waning, and full moon days, inscribe in cinnabar the sixth, seventh, and eighth characters, face the moon while wearing them, and after eight years, light shall emanate from within your body, your face shall turn golden, and both in life and death, you shall ascend to the abodes of the sun and moon, undergo refinement, and attain immortality. Those who bear these scripts shall have no further adverse records in the Three Bureaus; their names shall be inscribed in the Heaven of Sovereign Radiance, and through the revolutions of life and death, they shall endure for kalpas without end. This method is wondrous and profound, its merit equal to that of the flying transcendents.

To the right is a brief illustration of one heaven to clarify the principle; the remaining heavens for wearing and bearing follow the *Inner Sounds Jade Formula*.

*Southern Flaming Cavern Floating, Jade Eyes Gleaming Bright.*

The Lesser Florescence says: These eight characters are the inner sounds of the Heaven of Harmonious Yang. *Southern Flaming* refers to the southern Flowing Fire Court, seventy thousand *li* in breadth, its flying flames resplendent in the eight directions. *Cavern Floating* refers to the Cavern Yang Palace, where the qi of flowing fire blazes and floats. *Jade Eyes* is the essence of flowing fire. When the body is refined, jade-like radiance is born, bright as the pupils of the eyes—hence, *Jade Eyes*. The Perfected of the Southern Culmen govern within the palace, and all practitioners who first attain the Dao proceed to the Flowing Fire Court. The Perfected of the Southern Culmen then washes and refines them with the fire’s essence, scouring away the dust and filth, allowing them to become companions of the Perfected. *Gleaming bright* describes their multitude. The Brahmanic form falls into the void, the Nine Numinous Ones propel them forward.

Minor Tenuity said: These eight characters are the inner sounds of the Reverent Florescence Heaven. *Brahmanic form* was the title of the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning in the Dragon Han kalpa. By the Crimson Clarity kalpa, he was called the Nameless Lord; when the High Sovereign inaugurated the kalpic movement, he was titled the Primordial Venerable. His Brahmanic qi transforms his form, manifesting through kalpic changes with a single spirit—unborn of womb-gestation—hence, *Brahmanic form*. *Falls into the void* describes how the Primordial Beginning arises from the void itself. *Nine Numinous Ones* are the Nine Radiant Perfected. They govern within the Southern Superior Palace, presiding over the karmic records of deceased souls in the Nine Glooms. *Propel them forward* refers to the Nine Radiant Perfected, who oversee the ledgers of destiny, calculating the merits of souls’ past lives. In heaven stands the Scattered Flowers Terrace, where the Four Dipper Perfected reside. Those with virtuous deeds receive from the Four Dipper Perfected the talisman of extended life, and by its conferral, they are delivered from the Nine Glooms.

Marsh Luo’s Brahma Terrace, the Green Gauze of the Great Thousand.

Minor Tenuity said: These eight characters are the inner sounds of the Ancestral Fluttering Heaven. *Marsh* is the name of a mountain in heaven. Upon this mountain lies the cavern of the host of dragons, within which stands the Yellow Chamber, also called the Jade Countenance Hall. *Luo* is the inner name of the Perfected of the True Dawn. He governs within the Yellow Chamber, enduring through the great kalpas without end, persisting through the Dragon Han with ever-greater clarity—thus, the Glooms hold joy for him. *Brahma* is the hidden title of the Flying Celestial Perfected, who number beyond count. *Terrace* is the Jade Terrace, situated on the southern face of Marsh Mountain. *Green Gauze* refers to the Lady of the Moon, whose name is Luo Ying. Her countenance is like jade, and she wears a green mantle and azure robes—hence, *Green Gauze*. She governs within the Palace of Sun and Moon, ascending the Great Brahma Heaven of the Dao’s qi, the gate of kalpic movement, aligning with the reckoning of heaven and earth until the great kalpa’s end. Having received the conjunction of sun and moon, she then meets upon the Jade Terrace.

The Great Thousand denotes the reckoning of worlds. Master Lu states: "Counting a thousand thrice—first to a thousand, then a thousand thousands, yields the Lesser Thousand. Counting the Lesser Thousand to a thousand yields the Middle Thousand. Counting the Middle Thousand to a thousand yields the Great Thousand. Thus, the greatest of thousands is called the Great Thousand." Should one recite and chant the Cavernous Chapters, one may then ride the feathered-wheel chariot, ascend to the chambers of the Yellow Chamber, wander atop the Jade Terrace, and behold the realms of the Great Thousand.

*"Vast and boundless, the Nine Shameful Ones—
Vernal hymns weave through the winding paths."*

Master Shaowei says: These eight characters are the celestial sounds of the Imperial Reed Heaven. *Vast* (眇) means "dim and distant." In ancient times, the Primordial One sank into the midst of Yan Kang, where the celestial script of jade characters lay veiled and unmanifest—dim and distant indeed. *Boundless* (莽) refers to the Dragon Han’s opening of the kalpic movement, when its texts shone forth once more, vast and resplendent. Should one encounter the Way, both men and women shall live for thirty-six thousand years. When this kalpic movement reaches its end, another kalpa shall pass, and the Nine Qi shall each give birth to a beast to harm the wicked. Once the kalpa unfolds, these nine beasts are called the Nine Shameful Ghosts. The Northern Emperor and the Perfected of the Upper Realms preside over the Registers of Life and Death, thus establishing the Nine Shameful Ones to assist the Three Officials. When the reckoning reaches eighty-one myriad, the convergence of celestial qi is measured, and the Nine Shameful Ones shall be deemed fit to assist, styled the Envoys of the Nine Capitals.

*Vernal* (韶) is the inner name of the Divine Sovereign of the Imperial Reed Heaven. The Divine Sovereign of the Divine Empyrean is the spirit of the Demon King, who constantly tests whether those who study the Way are upright or not. The Demon King ever composes ballads to disturb the human heart. Should one’s heart remain steadfast, the king shall commend them and swiftly ascend to the midst of the Imperial Reed Heaven. *Winding paths* (缘邅) is the inner taboo of the Lords of the Southern and Northern Dippers. Should one’s meritorious deeds be recorded by the Southern Dipper, it shall deliver them from the trials of the Three Realms, rescue them from the sufferings of the Nine Glooms, and report to the Demon King, who shall not dare to harm them. Should one commit evil, the Three Officials shall record their sins before the Northern Dipper, which shall then report to the Demon King, who shall annihilate their souls and consign them to the depths of the Nine Glooms, bound to the labors of the Long Night for ten thousand kalpas without end.

Above the Imperial Reed Heaven lies the Mountain of Golden Splendor, upon which stand the palaces of the Five Emperors. There, five-colored clouds ever arise, with the sun and moon flanking its sides, and flying immortals attending its radiant chariots. Once their studies are complete and the Way is attained, all shall journey to the Mountain of Golden Splendor to receive the token of the Grand Unity, thereby commanding the Divine Sovereign of the Divine Empyrean and vanquishing the trials of the Great Demon. Only then may they ride the luminous-wheel chariot and wander the eight directions in revelry.

The Nine Qi, according to the *Scripture of the Orthodox Methods of the Three Heavens*: The Primordial Qi gives birth to Three Qi—first, the Crimson Cavern; second, the White Luminance; third, the Pure Vastness. The Primordial Qi further gives birth to Three Qi—first, the Verdant Radiance; second, the Yellow Effulgence; third, the Azure Chaos. It is also said: The White-Concealing Mysterious Qi gives birth to Three Qi—first, the Purple Fusion; second, the Azure Flame; third, the Black Flow. These are called the Nine Qi.

*"Above the clouds, the Nine Capitals—
Flying immortals arise in soaring flight."*

Master Shaowei says: These eight characters are the celestial sounds of the Hall of Radiance Heaven. *Above the clouds* (云上) is the inner taboo of the Divine King of the Flying Heavens. It opens the kalpa of the Dragon Han, inaugurates the movement of the Crimson Clarity, unfolds the books of spontaneity, and establishes the roots of heaven and earth. The *Nine Capitals* (九都) are the nine-tiered terraces that arise once the Three Images divide, situated upon the Mountain of the Jade Capital, resplendent above the Void Mystery. The divine beings of the Flying Heavens ever scatter the hundred harmonies of incense and stream the blossoms of the five clouds to behold the Flying Celestial Perfected. Atop the terrace stands the Jade Lad of the Grand Perfected, who thrice daily revolves the Ten Absolute Banners. With each revolution of the banners, the Celestial Thearchs of the myriad heavens thrice ascend the Mysterious Terrace; circling the terrace thrice, they recite and chant the Cavernous Chapters.

*Flying immortals* (飞生) is the name of the spirit of renewed life in the Southern Upper Realm. Should a scholar recite the Cavernous Chapters with a voice that reaches the Upper Palaces, the myriad heavens shall rejoice, and the Flying Immortals shall open the path of deathlessness, streaming the qi of long life to refine the Five Souls below. Once the Five Souls are refined, the Eight Radiant Ones shall abide within. *Arise* (自) means "to follow." *Soaring flight* (骞) refers to the Forest of Soaring Flight. Once they together elevate the human body to ascend the nine-tiered Mysterious Terrace and wander beneath the Forest of Soaring Flight, girded with the celestial script and reciting the Cavernous Chapters from their lips, after twenty-four years, they shall ascend to pay homage at the palaces of the Mysterious Capital.

*"Nurturing fragrance, the Wheel of Dharma turns—
Mara’s law revolves in ceaseless motion."*

Master Shaowei says: These eight characters are the celestial sounds of the Upright Tranquility Heaven. *Nurturing* (那) is the inner name of the Attendant Gentleman of the Celestial King. He governs the qi of the four seasons of heaven, the guiding principles of the Dao’s emptiness and non-being, and rectifies the divisions of the Upright Tranquility Heaven. *Fragrance* (育) is the name of the Wheel of the Celestial Pass. *Luxuriant* (郁馥) is the name of the numinous youth within the Dipper. Ever revolving the Nurturing Wheel within the Great Non-Being, turning it ten times to summon the Perfected of Heaven—when the Wheel of the Pass turns ten times, the Great Sages of the ten directions ascend to pay homage to the Jade Emperor, and the myriad spirits all arrive as Luxuriant sings the rites. *Mara* (摩罗) is the inner taboo of the Great Demon of Heaven. At Luxuriant’s first chant, the Demon King binds his form. Should a scholar know the qi of the four seasons and the turning of the Ten Passes, they shall enter the gate of the Wheel of Dharma, ride the chariot of the Eight Radiant Ones, ascend to the midst of the Jade Clarity, and pay homage atop the Terrace of the Purple Tenuity.

*"Holding the mirrorless, seizing form to move countenance."*

Master Shaowei says: These eight characters are the celestial sounds of the Reverent Celebration Heaven. *Holding* (霐) is the inner name of the Supervising Divine Overseer of Heaven. *Holding* (持) is the name of the Dragon Abyss, wherein the myriad dragons coil, ever driving golden jars to convey the blossoms of the Eastern Well and irrigate the Celestial Perfected. *Blossoms* (华) are the essence of the Yellow Blossoms within the sun, which pour into the streams of the Eastern Well, the inexhaustible source of celestial fluid. *Mirrorless* (无镜) is the taboo of the Divine King of the Flying Heavens. Wandering above the Great Empyrean, emitting light without color, he governs the registers of life and death and delivers those who study the Way. *Seizing form* (揽姿) is the name of the gate of the Three Realms. Should one know the name of this divine king, they shall open the storehouses of the Long Night, rescue the souls of the Nine Glooms, and deliver them through the gate of the Three Realms.

*"Conveying Countenance"* is the name of the Jade Maiden of Mystic Harmony. When one attains passage through the gate of the Three Realms, *Conveying Countenance* guides them with the crimson spirit-qi into form, while the fluid of Supreme Harmony irrigates their spirit. They ascend to the Hall of Fortune and Virtue, preserving their kalpic destiny without end.

*Fragrant Radiance, Vast Brilliance*—the divine sash emerges from the palace.
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the Jade Heaven.

*Fragrant Radiance* is the alternate name of the Mystic Terrace of the Jade Capital in Heaven. The Western Numinous Perfected constantly recites the cavernous scriptures while wandering above it. *Vast Brilliance* is the inner name of the Heavenly Divine Duke, coeval with the Primordial Beginning, serving as the model of mystic qi and instructing those who study immortality. One who masters the sound of these eight characters will have the Divine Duke open the gates of the Eternal Darkness, allowing ascent into the Gate of Renewed Life and mounting the terrace of the Jade Capital.

*The Divine Sash* is the numinous youth of the Purple Tenuity Palace, who presides over the corpses of the extinguished. If one obtains the *Song of Boundless Chapters* of the Divine Sash, they shall return to form within the Chamber of Triple Refinement, receive the qi of spontaneity, and rejoice in limitless longevity.

Above: The three black cinnabar heavens of the southern quadrant, with their spontaneous jade characters.

*Tao-li Chan-yu, Po-ni Kau-tong.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the K’ung-sheng Heaven.

*Tao-li* is the name of the Southern World of Non-Ultimate. *Chan* is the kingdom of Tao-li, also called *Chan-li*. Above this kingdom lies the Cavernous Yang Palace, where floating embers form the Flowing Fire Court. The numinous scripture begins with refinement in the Flowing Fire, adorning and illuminating its radiance. Once enlightened, the kingdom of Tao-li transforms into the Hall of Fortune and Virtue, and all suffering souls attain passage into the Cavernous Yang Palace.

*Yu* is the inner name of the Southern Supreme Lord of Life. *Po-ni* is the numinous youth of the Fire-Refining Pool. *Kau-tong* is the demon-god of the Tao-li world, who constantly obstructs the paths of life. If one knows the name of the Lord of Life, they attain passage to the Cavernous Yang Palace, proceed to the Fire Pool for refinement, and are reborn into the kingdom of Fortune and Virtue—whereupon the demon-god submits. One who recites the sound of these eight characters will have the boundless numinous officials of the Tao-li world attend their body, escorting them directly to the Southern Palace, where immortals receive them. Within three years, they shall surely ride the cinnabar wheels of the Empyrean, ascending to the heavens of the Three Qi.

*Wan-sou Ti-se, Tai-miao’s Hall.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the Huang-ya Heaven.

The name *Wan-sou* is the inner appellation of the Emperor of Huang-ya Heaven. He presides over the opening of the *Tai-mo* scriptures to illuminate the eight characters, and once the Dao is made manifest, the Great Canopy above becomes serene and limpid.

*Di-se* is the name of a flying immortal of the Form Realm. He constantly rides a chariot of radiant clouds, drawn by nine-colored dragons, roaming above the Form Realm, entering and exiting the Jade Purity, sweeping away defiled qi, and delivering those of good root.

*Tai-miao’s Hall* is the Hall of Transformed Birth. The transformation of the hollow emptiness forms natural patterns, vast and boundless, opening the passage for the deliverance of the myriad beings. When a practitioner masters the sound of the eight characters, the flying immortal descends in his chariot of radiant clouds to bear the adept upward to the Hall of Transformed Birth.

*Liu-luo Fan-meng, Jing-wei Xiao-yu.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Ji-feng* Heaven.

*Liu* is the inner name of the Heavenly King, who dwells above the Purple Empyrean and roams the Jade Capital Mountain. *Luo* is the taboo name of the Moon Maiden, who oversees the rites of the King’s excursions and feasts, her radiance flowing through the *Ji-feng* Heaven to illumine the ninefold mysteries of the Dark.

*Fan* is the name of a flying immortal who governs the revolving gates of the Nine Heavens. *Meng* is the Primordial Heavenly Spirit, the root of the *Ji-feng* Heaven. *Jing* is *Jing-huang*, the Perfected of the Four Poles. *Wei* is the transcendent of *Yu-xiu Jing-xiao*. Together, they govern the Terrace of the Jade Capital, ever riding clouds of three colors, traversing the long night to deliver the souls of good root.

*Xiao* is *Xiao-ren*, the palace of the White Primordial Sovereign. *Yu* is the guest-receiving hall of *Xiao-ren’s* mountain. One who constantly recites the cavernous scriptures shall ride clouds of nine colors and ascend to the Terrace of Radiant Yellow.

*Yi-miao Wu-ji, Wan-shou Shao-du.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Xiao-mang* Heaven.

*Yi-miao* is the title of the Heavenly King of the *Xiao-mang* Heaven. *Wu* is emptiness; *ji* is stillness.

This is the courtyard of emptiness and stillness. This Heavenly King has come since the *Long-han* era and emerged in the *Chi-ming* era, dwelling within the void and abiding in the courtyard of stillness.

*Wan-shou* is the inner title of the Supreme Dao Lord. The Dao Lord ever rides the eight-scene jade chariot, urges the three-pure flying clouds, unfolds the mysteries of the primordial beginning, and expounds the great Dharma to deliver humanity.

*Shao-du* is the name of the numinous youth within the sun. He constantly scatters solar essence to irrigate the perfected, and scatters flying blossoms to brush away dust. Should the adept know the sound of these eight characters, the Heavenly King shall descend in a chariot of flying-scene clouds, with a canopy of three-pure hues, to deliver the adept above the Three Realms and enter the courtyard of stillness.

*A-lan Yu-zhu, Hua-mo Yan-you.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Weng-chong* Heaven.

*A-lan* is the taboo name of the Heavenly Emperor. He ever rides the wheel of *Jing-xiao*, roams to observe the nine-tiered terrace, abides in the jade tower, and chants cavernous scriptures to subdue demon kings.

*Yu* is the hidden name of the demon king of the *Yu-mo* Heaven. *Zhu* is desire. This demon king, *Du-bo*, ever dwells above the Realm of Desire, chanting songs of empty melodies.

*Hua* refers to the radiant splendor of the Form Realm. *Mo* refers to the vast and untraceable expanse of the Realm of Desire. *Yan* is the courtyard that binds ghosts; *you* is the chamber that imprisons ghosts. When the Heavenly King ascends the cloud tower and chants the boundless scriptures, the heavenly demons respond by binding themselves, and the multitude of ghosts submit in the *you* chamber. Those who uphold these tones shall open prosperity for nine generations of ancestors; those who cultivate them shall cause their ashen bones to be reborn.

*Jiu-kai Zi-bian, A-na Pin-shou.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Jiang-you* Heaven.

*Jiu-kai* refers to the great unfolding at the dawn of time, when heaven and earth were yet undivided. The revolving Three Qi opened into nine divisions. Once the nine measures were clarified, the nine ranks were arrayed, and the myriad beings of yin and yang were born, their inherent brightness became self-evident.

*A* is the ancient name of the *A-qiu* Heavenly Sovereign. He ever rides a nine-colored dragon, drives a canopy of three-pure hues, ascends the peaks of *Long-shan*, and roams within the Nine Mysteries.

*Na* is the hidden name of the *Na-xie* flying heavenly immortal. He traverses above the Three Realms, examines the long night, and delivers the souls of the good. Should one know the sound of these eight characters, the Heavenly King shall rank and deliver the adept’s body, entering the assembly of flying immortals, transforming withered bones into the visage of a youth.

*Wu-liang Fu-gai, Fu-luo He-shen.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Ruan-le* Heaven.

*Wu-liang* is the primordial spirit of the boundless great sage within heaven. He governs all flying heavenly immortals, who receive their ranks from him and thereby ascend.

*Fu* is the inner name of the reborn perfected. He ever examines the records of the dark night, distinguishing the roots of good and evil. *Gai* is the title of the fortune hall within the mystery.

*Fu* refers to the souls of the dark night, delivered by the perfected and thus called "floating." They ride the turning destiny to return and ascend to the fortune hall.

*Luo* is the Great Luo. It opens the great thousandfold world, summons the guests of rebirth, and leads them to the Heaven of Great Luo, where their registers are settled in the various palaces and their deaths erased in the Three Offices.

*He* is union in celebration. *Shen* is the divine duke, the prime minister of the Great Luo. Should one know the sound of these eight characters, one shall unite in celebration with the divine duke, receive deliverance as a guest of rebirth, and thus be called "united with the divine."

*Yu-dan Chang-sang, Bo-kong Du-xian.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Tan-shi* Heaven.

*Yu-dan* is the name of the jade capital within the *Tan-shi* Heaven. *Chang-sang* is the heavenly *Qian-lin*, also called the *Sang-lin Qian-mu*, which shades the Eastern Florescence Palace. Upon its leaves are the great cavernous scriptures, purple writings and jade characters gleaming in the *Shang-qing*. Below stands the *Fu-sang* tree, above rise the thickets of *Qian-mu*. Azure phoenixes sing beneath its canopy, green mists and emerald peaks adorn its heights. Divine winds stir the fragrant herbs of reversal, and the *Sang-lin* resounds with a hundred pipes. When the divine wind stirs once, the cavernous scriptures form their sound—thus it is called *Bo-kong*.

*Du-xian* are the flying heavenly immortals. Ever at the first crow of the cock, they ascend the jade terrace, gather the cloud-teeth of the five directions, and swallow the light of the Three Luminaries. They examine the life-and-death registers of those who study immortality, deliver the souls of the Nine Darks, and ascend into the gate of the Dharma wheel.

To the right: the spontaneous jade characters of the Seven Qi of the White Heaven of the West.

*Jue-wu Zi-yu, Jiu-ri Dao-qian.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Xiao-du* Heaven.

*Jue-wu* is a flying heavenly immortal from the *Long-han* era. From the primordial beginning’s qi, within the formless primordial chaos, *Jue-wu* emerged by riding the turning destiny and coagulated qi to establish *Xiao-du*. Once established, it endured through the unending kalpas.

*Yu* is the inner name of the Heavenly King of *Xiao-du*. *Jiu* refers to the Heavenly King *Yu* riding a chariot drawn by elephants, entering the gate of the Nine Mysteries, turning the nine mechanisms of measure, and responding to the appointed time of the kalpa.

*Ri* is the solar youth within heaven. *Dao* is guiding and harmonizing qi. At the end of heaven’s turning, the solar youth halts its light to deliver the adept, irrigating them with the essence of the water mother and guiding them with the qi of great harmony. The five spirits are refined and washed, entering the vermilion palace—thus it is called *Dao-qian*.

*Kun-mu Dong-fu, Xing-she Shang-xuan.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Yuan-dong* Heaven.

*Kun-mu* is the mother of the Nine Numinous Ones, the steward of the Great Yin. She governs the Eastern Sea’s *Fu-sang* and the abyss of *Tang-gu*, ever regulating the earth’s mechanisms and turning the wheel of primordial qi, ascending to correspond with the heavenly gate. When the heavenly gate turns, the earth’s axis moves, and with each revolution of heaven, the waters surge in three thousand three hundred measures. When the qi of heaven and earth intermingle, the nine seas merge into one, and the waters fill the sky.

The East is where the Eastern Sea receives its confluence, governing the source of the Yellow River. *Fu* is the water spirit. She presides over Mount Kunlun, consolidating the vast seas, damming the Eastern Well—thus the earth’s mechanisms do not sink, and the kalpa endures long. *Xing-she* refers to the time of calamitous convergence, when the Mother of Earth emerges above the Eastern River, summoning the Bird Mother with a phoenix chariot to welcome those who study immortality, ascending to the ruins of Kunlun. The Bird Mother is the steward spirit of water. *Shang* means the Mother of Earth ascends to the Lord Emperor to report the kalpa’s convergence, delivering those who study immortality, announcing their names in the Palace of the Dark Capital. Some say *Shang-xuan* refers to the Lord of Life and Death. When the waters seek to emerge, the Lord of Life and Death examines those who study immortality, announcing their names in the Upper Palace.

*Tuo-luo Yu-miao, Miao-qi He-yun.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Miaocheng* Heaven.
*Tuo* is the inner name of the Heavenly Emperor. Born with *Miaocheng* upon the Cloud Ridge, *Luo* is the name of the moon at its first rising. *Tuo* dwells above the Cloud Ridge, embracing the moon to shine. *Yu* is the name of the divine king of *Miaocheng* Heaven. *Yu* means "to give birth," governing the flying gods of the ten directions. *Miao* is the name of the celestial overseer of the Feathered Forest. The divine king constantly dispatches him to guard the Three Realms, reviewing the registers of life and death, commanding demon kings to protect and deliver those who attain the Dao. *Miao* means "remote and lofty." Those who are protected and delivered ascend to the Feathered Forest to receive talismans and rise to heaven, journeying remotely through the cloud palaces. *Qi* is the cloud-qi. *He* means "to merge with the radiance." Having entered the Feathered Forest, they weave cloud-qi into robes, soaring to the Vermilion Palace to receive blessings in the Heavenly Hall, then ascending with the hosts of heaven, merging with the radiance.

*The Flying Heaven’s Great Ugly One, Overseer of the Upper Heavens.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Jinshang* Heaven.
*The Flying Heaven* refers to the divine kings of the ten directions’ flying heavens. In the heavens, there is the *feixuan* qi, which coalesces into the scriptures of the Great Cavern. The divine kings of the ten directions constantly recite these scriptures in the empty firmament to harmonize the qi of spontaneity and guide those who study the Dao. *Great* is the general record of the Three Realms, governing the registers of life and death. *Ugly* means "elder." He is the demon king of the Three Realms, serving the Great Ugly One. If scholars recognize his tone, the demon king protects their authenticity, and their bodies ascend to the Three Clarities. *Overseer* is the official who governs the flying heavens, constantly gathering the qi of the eight assemblies to hasten the revolutions of heaven and earth, supervising the officials of the long night and delivering the souls of the Nine Darks. If scholars know the tones of heaven, the heavenly demons array their words, and the Great Ugly One commands the registers of immortals to ascend to the heavens.

*Sha-tuo Jie-liang, Long-han Ying-xian.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Changrong* Heaven.
*Sha* refers to the *Shalan* Palace in heaven, a detached hall of the Purple Tenuity, situated above the Jade Clarity, resplendent within the Purple Void. *Tuo* is *Tuoqiu*. The multitudes of *Tuoqiu* number in the countless millions, all newly delivered and attained. Their merits incomplete, they remain scattered there. *Jie-liang* means that at each kalpa’s convergence, the multitudes of *Tuoqiu* are measured by their merits, ascending to the Vermilion Mound Palace to receive blessings and become immortals. *Long-han* is the name of the first kalpa, when the Great Dao was pure and simple, its transformations effortless and unadulterated. *Ying* is the name of a flying god from the *Long-han* kalpa, constantly delivering the souls of the Nine Darks to ascend into the *Lan* Palace. *Xian* is the youth of the Southern Palace. When scholars attain deliverance, *Xian* refines their forms and delivers them above the Vermilion Mound.

*The Azure Fall’s Floating Li, Empty Song Preserves the Precious.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Yulong* Heaven.
*Azure* means that within the *Yulong* Heaven, azure mists constantly arise to shade the *Yulong* Heaven. *Fall* is the name of a flying god in the empty firmament, constantly riding a chariot of azure mist to wander the *Yulong* Heaven. Thrice daily, he leads the hosts of heaven’s sages to ascend and pay homage at the Seven Treasures Palace. *Floating Li* is the inner name of the Heavenly King. When the hosts ascend to pay homage, the Heavenly King rejoices. *Empty* is the name of the celestial attendant of dawn. *Song* refers to the melodies of the Cavern Chapters. When the attendant of dawn utters a cry, the numinous wind plays, and the sound forms the Cavern Chapters—hence *Empty Song*. *Preserves the Precious* means that if scholars know these eight characters, they ascend to the Southern Palace as guests of the flying heavens, preserving themselves through the endless kalpa. They treasure the spontaneous patterns—hence *Preserves the Precious*. This meaning differs from the chapter’s opening: if one attains the Dao without form, they merge with the cloud-qi, and the subtlety of emptiness—how could it be discerned? Thus, the *Cavern Chapters* say: "Soaring triumphantly through layered azure clouds, the net of *Luo* shines upon the Upper Mystery." The *Numinous Writ* also says: "The Numinous Writ glows brilliantly, illuminating the Great Void." Thus, *Fall* and *Empty Song* are not merely personal names.

*Wu-yi Wu-pin, Dong-miao Zi-zhen.*
The Lesser Mystery says: These eight characters are the inner tones of the *Fandu* Heaven.
*Wu-yi* is the inner name of the Heavenly King. In the *Long-han* kalpa, all karmic conditions were exhausted, and he transcended the courts of the Three Realms, ascending to the halls of the Great Void to receive the registers of the Nine Immortals and assume the title of Great Sage. At the dawn of the *Chi-ming* kalpa, the Primordial Beginning bestowed upon him the kingship of the *Fandu* Heaven. *Wu* is the *Taiwu* Perfected, who receives the Heavenly King’s talismans to deliver the souls of the long night. *Pin* means "to measure the sins and blessings of the dark souls." *Dong* means "to thoroughly understand past karmic conditions." *Miao* is the Hall of Wondrous Transformation. Once past karmic conditions are resolved, one enters the Hall of Wondrous Transformation. *Zi* means "with"; *Zhen* means "heavenly authenticity."

The *Taiwu* Perfected delivers the souls of the Nine Dark Realms, thoroughly discerning past karmic conditions. When all evil affinities are exhausted, he guides them into the Hall of Wondrous Transformation, uniting with the Flying Celestials to merge with heavenly authenticity.

The Primordial *Fan* is vast and boundless; in profound stillness, souls are delivered.
*Shaowei* says: These eight characters are the inner sounds of *Jiayi* Heaven.

*Yuanfan* refers to the qi of the Primordial Beginning and the Great *Fan*, which uplifts the essence of the limpid Han, soaring high and pervading the void, suspended yet never falling.
*Huimo* means distant yet unobstructed, existent yet as if nonexistent, subtle yet unnameable, wondrous yet untraceable.
*Youji* means profound and silent, inaudible and invisible, yet within it lies the true, and within the true lies the essence, mysteriously delivering the celestials and humans.

The Heavenly True August One says: The inner sounds of all heavens, being natural jade characters, are woven from the radiance of soaring mystery, harmonizing the sounds of the Five Directions. They arise above the Primordial Beginning and emerge within the empty vastness. Their script is profound and intricate, difficult to trace in detail. The Heavenly Worthy, in encouragement, commanded the elucidation of their meaning. As the mysterious statutes have their decrees, I dare not disobey the mandate. When I took up my brush, my spirit ascended to the Great Empyrean, refining both essence and coarse matter to the utmost of my heart’s contemplation. Once the August Way was made clear, all heavens rejoiced in celebration. Those who treasure it receive the descent of perfected beings; those who cultivate it undergo transformation in form. Its majestic numinosity is vast and boundless, beyond naming.

Above: The Five Radiant Mystery of the Northern Dark Heaven’s Natural Jade Characters.

The Dao says: These are the great *Fan* esoteric utterances among all heavens, the sounds of the boundless.
*Youqi* says: The thirty-two heavens each possess eight characters, together forming the great *Fan* esoteric utterances among all heavens, the sounds of the boundless. Thus, they are called the inner sounds of all heavens. This is the soaring mystery’s natural true scripture, born above the Primordial Beginning and issuing from the empty vastness. It shapes heaven and earth, responds to kalpas and eons. The Heavenly True August One also roughly grasped its purport. The old script was a full *zhang* in length and breadth. The Heavenly True August One once transcribed its text to establish the correct sounds.

*Dong* says: The Dao’s words are the words of the Most High. The "all heavens" refer to the thirty-two heavens. The "great *Fan* esoteric utterances" are the names of the Heavenly Emperors, all concealed and not manifest. The "sounds of the boundless" mean that the resonant chapters naturally resound through all heavens, hence called the sounds of the boundless—the old script is thus. The original script, with its eight-cornered characters, was a full *zhang* in length and breadth, each side a *zhang*, making it the foremost of the ten thousand virtues. The Heavenly True August One was an ancient high perfected. In the *Long-han* kalpa, he transcribed this script to serve as the foremost virtue among all heavens.

*Youqi* says: The original script’s old characters were each a *zhang* in breadth, with eight corners radiating light. Their literary brilliance shone resplendently, illuminating the eight directions. The Primordial Heavenly Worthy then commanded the Heavenly True August One to compile these characters, explicate their meanings, and transmit them to the Dao Lord, instructing him to teach them to all heavens—those who attain the Dao, achieve perfection, and have their names recorded in the registers of immortals. The August One then examined and verified them. The Great Emperor appointed him to oversee the Dong’e Grotto.

*Shaowei* says: According to the *Inner Sounds Sutra*, the Primordial Heavenly Worthy was seated in the *Bailing* Lodge of the *Chi-ming* world. At that time, clouds and mist surged for three days and nights, and the dark *yin* did not disperse. The Five Elders addressed the Heavenly Worthy, saying: "Today, while attending your seat, we have witnessed what we have never seen before. When the Heavenly Worthy expounds the teachings, rivers and seas fall silent, and mountains and peaks conceal their mists. Yet now, in broad daylight, the sky is overcast, and the celestials and humans are alarmed. We do not know the reason." The Heavenly Worthy replied: "Today, all heavens manifest auspicious signs, and numinous responses arise naturally. The jade characters blaze with brilliance, obscuring the light of heaven. I command all present to close their eyes and listen reverently." Suddenly, the celestial qi parted, the dark obscurity vanished, and five-colored radiance illuminated the ten directions. A spirit script, each character a *zhang* in breadth, appeared above the empty mystery. Its literary brilliance blazed, with eight corners radiating light, its luminous essence dazzling the eyes, making it impossible to behold. The Heavenly Worthy proclaimed to all: "This is the spirit script of the Eight Assemblies. Its characters have no fixed form; their purport is profound and intricate, difficult to trace in detail.
