Let them be transcribed and explicated." Thereupon, the Heavenly True August One received the Heavenly Worthy’s luminous command, annotating their sounds, distinguishing their divisions. The thirty-two heavens each possess eight characters, together with the soaring mystery’s natural scripture, harmonizing the qi of the Five Directions’ soaring mystery to blend with the sounds of the eight characters. This is called the great *Fan* esoteric utterances—these are the sounds of the boundless.

The *True One’s Five Teeth Sutra* says: Of the August One, none know the beginning of his attainment of the Dao. His body was nine *chi* tall, covered in dark hair, each strand over a *chi* long. In the time of the Yellow Emperor, he dwelled beneath the Absolute *Yin* of Mount Emei, his dwelling made of azure jade, his seat of yellow gold. He unfurled banners of patterned silk and burned thousand-fold harmony incense. His attendants were jade lads and maidens; his three seated guests were all called the Celestial Perfected Kings of the Great Clarity. The Yellow Emperor bowed twice and inquired of the Dao, receiving from him the scripture of the Five Teeth and Three Ones. Those who know its sounds and can purify themselves in fasting to recite it will have all heavens dispatch Flying Celestial Divine Kings to descend and observe their person, recording their meritorious diligence and reporting it to all heavens.

*Youqi* says: Those who know the great *Fan*’s esoteric sounds and can purify body and heart to uphold and recite them will have the thirty-two Heavenly Emperors summon the Flying Celestial Divine Kings of the Ten Directions’ boundless realms to descend to their chambers, observe their body and heart, list their meritorious diligence, and report it to all heavens. The myriad spirits will pay homage, and earthly deities will attend at the gates. The Great Merit Demon Kings will protect and recommend them as perfected immortals. Once their Dao is complete and they attain perfection, they will roam the Three Realms and ascend into the Golden Gate.

*Dong* says: The Golden Gate lies within the Nine Palaces of the Great Auroral Empyrean. Within it stands the *Qianlin* Tree, atop which perches the Golden-Winged Bird and the smelting pool. The Golden-Winged Bird weaves its feathers into immortal robes, ascending to the Nine Palaces.

Youxī says: Once the myriad spirits pay homage and earthly deities attend at the gates, the great demons of the Three Realms and Five Emperors will jointly protect and recommend them for immortal deliverance. Thus, their names shall be inscribed upon the imperial tablets, and their ranks recorded in the register of perfected beings. When the Dao is fulfilled through ten thousand recitations and a thousand meritorious deeds are complete, they shall ascend in cloud chariots to stand before the Emperor of the Golden Portal.

This sound repels all, dispels all, delivers all, and accomplishes all—it is the spontaneous sound of celestial perfection.

*Dong* says: It expels demonic thieves, averts misfortune, rescues lost souls, and fulfills all things—all by the power of this secret celestial script.

Youxī says: This boundless sound can drive away all spectral perversities, dissolve all calamities, liberate all from the cycle of birth and death, and perfect all celestial and mortal beings. Thus, it is called the *Celestial Perfected Writ*, the spontaneous inner sound of the jade script.

Therefore, when one recites it, flying celestials descend to observe, the Supreme Emperor chants from afar, the myriad spirits pay homage, the Three Realms attend in reverence, all malevolent forces bow their heads, and demonic spirits vanish of themselves.

Youxī says: If one can recite it, the divine kings of the Ten Directions will descend to observe, the thirty-two Heavenly Emperors will chant from afar, the myriad spirits and numina will pay homage, the demon kings of the Three Realms will flank and protect, all perversities will naturally bow their heads, and all ghosts and specters will surely perish.

The jade tones resound, and the Ten Directions grow solemn and clear.

*Shaowei* says: The celestial script is of jade, hence "jade tones." To chant and intone its pivotal verses is called "resounding."

Rivers and seas fall silent, mountains and peaks swallow the mist.

*Dong* says: All by the divine power of this scripture.

The myriad spirits tremble and submit; immortals are summoned and gathered.

*Shaowei* says: Thus, the jade groves vibrate with celestial resonance, the Ten Directions bask in the radiance of the Three Luminaries, rivers and seas still their winds and waves, mountains and peaks swallow the clouds and mists, the myriad spirits submit in awe, and immortals are summoned to one’s chamber.

Heaven is free of defiling qi, earth is free of demonic dust. Profound wisdom illumines the void, and the vastness of the Mystery is most mysterious.

*Dong* says: *Profound* refers to the profound numen; *wisdom* to sagely insight; *illumines* to penetrating clarity; *void* to emptiness; *vastness* to impartiality. It universally delivers all beings, embracing all without exception, liberating all things. *Most mysterious* refers to its depth and remoteness. The merit of this boundless scripture is profound and far-reaching—hence, "most mysterious."

Youxī says: At this time, heaven is free of defiling qi, earth is free of demonic dust. If one further unites profound insight with numinous wisdom, congeals the radiance of celestial light, and illumines the clarity of the empty void, then within the wondrous lies the most wondrous, within the mysterious lies the yet more mysterious—so abstruse as to be unfathomable. Thus, it is called the *vastness of the most mysterious*.

*Shaowei* says: Cultivating the life of profound wisdom penetrates the Three Clarities. *Vastness* is the deepest and most wondrous.

*Xuanying* says: This reveals the inner sound of the various heavens and the power of profound wisdom’s illumination. *Profound* means deep and unfathomable; *wisdom* means boundless illumination. Wisdom can illumine emptiness—hence, "profound wisdom." Lofty and limitless is called *illuminating the void*; shining above the Three Clarities is called *illuminating clarity*. *Void* means emptiness; *clarity* means purity. Boundless and infinite is called *vastness*. Within vastness lies true emptiness. Within the true lies the essence, and within it, the truth. It gives birth to true sages, neither existing nor non-existing, eternally serene and subtle, so profound as to defy comprehension. Within the mysterious lies the yet more mysterious—hence, "the vastness of the most mysterious."

The supreme sages, in their compassion, bestowed this true scripture upon the lower realms, arranging it into mysterious precepts to enlighten humanity and deliver all beings. Those who recite and wear its sacred writ shall, in accordance with the qi they attain, fulfill their merit and complete their deeds, ascending as ministers of the Golden Portal. Thus, through accumulated study, one becomes perfected; through attaining perfection, one enters sagehood. Born in heaven or born on earth, their efficacy is boundless. Those who know the sound of the jade script shall one day ascend with flesh and bone together. Scholars of the highest learning, strive diligently!

*The Supreme Wondrous Scripture of Boundless Salvation, Upper Chapter, with Four Commentaries, Volume Four* concludes.

**Scripture Exegesis**
This scripture was received by the Supreme Lord of the Dao from the Celestial Worthy of Primordial Beginning and transmitted to the world. The Lord of the Dao composed three prefaces: the first, the middle, and the last.

The first preface begins with "The Dao speaks: Formerly, in the Azure Heaven of Primordial Beginning..." and ends with "facing east to recite the scripture."

The middle preface follows the "Hymns of the Three Realms" and comprises these two chapters, which are the most profound and luminous utterances.

The last preface begins with "Among the various heavens..." and ends with "the vastness of the most mysterious."

The scripture contains two chapters: the first from "The Primordial Beginning’s Mysterious Cavern" to "proclaiming the Upper Clarity," and the latter from "The Primordial Jade Calendar" to "calamities befalling the seven ancestors."

The great Brahmā’s hidden speech is not counted among these two chapters. Some mistakenly consider the scripture as one chapter and the hidden speech as two, but this is incorrect. The middle preface states that reciting the scripture ten thousand times enables one to attain the Dao and illuminate the most profound utterances. Thus, the hidden speech is abstruse and arcane, not part of the two scriptural chapters—this is evident. Those who study this scripture should revere it with unwavering faith. When merit is fulfilled and the Dao complete, they shall naturally comprehend the shared blessings of heaven and humanity, benefiting both the living and the deceased. How can one not be resolute? How can one not strive?

*The Record of Mysterious Efficacy* and *The Daoist Anthology of Verified Miracles* both contain accounts of those who attained verification through reciting this scripture. Those who seek communion with the true should recite it with reverence and diligence.

**Phonetic Annotations**

Miaoxing: pronounced *Yu* (as in *Meng*).
Wuyang: pronounced *Yang*.
Yin: pronounced *Jin*.
Yin: pronounced *Yin*.
Bo: pronounced *Bo* (as in *Wo*).
E: pronounced *A*.
Gu: pronounced *Gu*.
Ren: pronounced *Ru* (as in *Zhen*).
Dizang: pronounced *Lang*.
Ze: pronounced *Ze*.
Bobo: pronounced *Fu*.
Zi: pronounced *Zi* (meaning "jealousy").
Shijie: pronounced *Jia* (referring to liberation through simulated death, where the physical form is discarded and the inner self attains immortality).
Duandi: pronounced *Duan*.
Sanhua: level tone.
Lian: pronounced *Bian* (as in "expedient means").
Fanxing: pronounced *Meng*.
Yulan: pronounced *Lan*.
Wei: pronounced *Wai*.
Huangjia: pronounced *Jia*.
Aqie: pronounced *Qie*.
Die: pronounced *Die*.
Ruanle: pronounced *Yue*.
Bobo: pronounced *Pei*.
Xiule: pronounced *Luo*.
Ming: pronounced *Ming*.
Xing: pronounced *Ding*.
Niwan: pronounced *Wan*.
Guo: pronounced *Bo*.
Bule: pronounced *Xiao*.
Degu: pronounced *Ge*.
Dan: pronounced with the upper tone.
He: pronounced *He* (departing tone).
Guanyin: pronounced *Guan*.
Zongjian: pronounced *Jian*.
Lower Guanyin: pronounced *Guan*.
Mo: pronounced *Mo*.
